201 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. Connecticut Gaming Policy Bd.


No. 14481


Supreme Court of Connecticut


224 Conn. 693; 620 A.2d 780; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 25


October 30, 1992, Argued  
February 23, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision ordering the termination of the plaintiff's employment as head of the lottery unit of the state division of special revenue, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Freed, J., denied the defendants' motion to dismiss; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Norko, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed his administrative appeal of defendant state agency's decision to terminate his employment. On appeal, the case was transferred to the Connecticut Supreme Court pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 4023 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c).


OVERVIEW: The employee was the head of a state agency's special revenue division. He refused to follow the agency's executive director's orders and as a result, the director recommended to the agency's board that the employee be terminated from his position. A hearing was held and the board terminated the employee's employment. The employee filed an administrative appeal with the lower court, which was dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The court affirmed finding that there was no subject matter jurisdiction over the appeal because the appeal had not been taken from a decision in a contested case under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-166(2). The court found that the agency was not statutorily required to determine the employee's legal right or privilege to his continued employment. Moreover, the employee held an appointed position that was served at the "pleasure of" the executive director. This further supported the finding that the agency was not required to do more than give the employee a termination hearing. Thus, the court found that § 4-166(2) limited contested case status to those proceedings where agencies were required to determine a party's legal rights or privileges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding of the lower, which dismissed the employee's administrative appeal of the state agency's decision to terminate his employment.

 

202 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ellis


No. AC 10760


Supreme Court of Connecticut


224 Conn. 711; 621 A.2d 250; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 28



February 23, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by the defendant for review of an order by the Appellate Court granting the state's motion to strike certain portions of his brief on his appeal to that court from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, Purtill, J., convicting him, after a jury trial, of the crimes of robbery in the first degree and larceny in the first degree.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion requesting the court to review of an order entered in the appellate court (Connecticut), which granted the State's motion to strike certain portions of defendant's brief filed in defendant's appeal from his conviction for robbery in the first degree and larceny in the first degree after a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: During jury voir dire, defendant moved to dismiss a panel on the ground that the absence from the panel of minority residents was evidence that the panel had not been randomly selected. The trial court denied the motion and the jury convicted defendant, an African-American, of first degree robbery and first degree larceny. On appeal, the appellate court granted the State's motion to strike the issue of lack of random selection of the jury panel from defendant's brief and appendix. Noting that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-197f limited the court's subject matter jurisdiction to final judgments of the appellate court, the court dismissed defendant's motion for review of the order because the appellate court's action in striking the issue was not a final judgment. The court further ruled that it had discretion to transfer the case to its own docket under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c) but declined to exercise that discretion. The court determined that, given the current state of the record, it preferred to await the ultimate outcome of the appellate court's appeal before considering whether to review defendant's claim.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's motion.

 

203 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Red Rooster Constr. Co. v. River Assoc., Inc.


No. 14403


Supreme Court of Connecticut


224 Conn. 563; 620 A.2d 118; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 21


November 4, 1992, Argued  
February 9, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mechanic's lien on certain property owned by the named defendant, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Berdon, J., granted the motion by the defendant Connecticut Savings Bank for reduction of the mechanic's lien; thereafter, the action was withdrawn against the defendant Kenneth Kraus, and the court, Schaller, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to cite in the Connecticut Attorney's Title Insurance Company as a party defendant; the matter was tried to the court, Schaller, J.; judgment for the named defendant et al. discharging the mechanic's lien; subsequently, the court, Schaller, J., denied the plaintiff's motion to open the judgment, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut). The trial court rendered judgment in favor of defendants, owner and bank, in plaintiff's action to foreclose a mechanic's lien. The trial court concluded that plaintiff's lien was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owner entered into a contract with plaintiff contractor pursuant to which plaintiff agreed to construct condominium units and commercial space on defendant's property. When the owner ordered the contractor to stop working, the contractor filed a certificate of mechanic's lien to secure its claim. The contractor served a copy of the certificate on the owner, but did not serve a copy on defendant bank, an encumbrancer of the property. The trial court concluded that the mechanic's lien was invalid because the bank, as a mortgagee of the property, was an "owner" within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-34 and was thereby entitled to notice of the filing of the lien. The appellate court first held that the contractor was not required to give notice to all encumbrancers. The court affirmed the trial court, however, and found that the lien was invalid because no oral oath was administered, the contractor's president did not sign a statement swearing to the truth of the facts contained in the certificate, and no ceremony was performed as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-22.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of defendants, owner and bank. The court held that the mechanic's lien held by plaintiff contractor was not sworn within the meaning of the mechanic's lien statute and was, therefore, invalid.

 

204 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reddick


No. 14336


Supreme Court of Connecticut


224 Conn. 445; 619 A.2d 453; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 13


September 22, 1992, Argued  
January 26, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crime of robbery in the second degree and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the jury before Fuller, J.; verdict of guilty of robbery in the second degree; thereafter, the defendant pleaded nolo contendere to being a persistent dangerous felony offender and the court rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict and the plea, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of conviction, after a jury trial before the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), for robbery in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-135, and, following a plea of nolo contendere, for being a persistent dangerous felony offender in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-135, and, following a plea of nolo contendere, of being a persistent dangerous felony offender in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(a). On review, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly failed to notify him of the contents of the second part of the substitute information charging him as a persistent dangerous felony offender. The court found no merit in this contention because defendant, having had actual notice of the contents of the second part of the information, did not contest the persistent dangerous felony offender charge. Instead, he pleaded nolo contendere to it. Defendant also claimed that the trial court improperly failed to instruct the jury that, in order to find robbery in the second degree to have been proven beyond a reasonable doubt, it had to agree unanimously on one of the aggravating factors that distinguished robbery in the second degree from robbery in the third degree. The court found no violation of defendant's rights because none of the jury instructions expressly sanctioned a non-unanimous verdict. Accordingly, the convictions were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for robbery in the second degree and for being a persistent dangerous felony offender.

 

205 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Campbell


No. 14130


Supreme Court of Connecticut


224 Conn. 168; 617 A.2d 889; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 385


September 30, 1992, Argued  
December 15, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and presented to the court, Dean, J., on pleas of guilty; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for a psychiatric examination at the Whiting Forensic Institute and, subsequent to that examination, the Institute filed a report recommending against psychiatric commitment and that the defendant be sentenced pursuant to his conviction; subsequently, the court, Bingham, J., denied the defendant's motion to correct the disposition refusing commitment and rendered judgment of guilty, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which denied his motion to correct the disposition refusing commitment and, upon his guilty pleas, convicted him on two counts of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-245, which required a trial judge to follow the presentence report of the Whiting Forensic Institute advising against commitment of a convicted defendant to the institute. In determining the merits of defendant's challenge, the court first noted that statutory language did preclude the trial court from ordering the commitment of defendant contrary to the Institute's recommendation. However, such preclusion did not violate the separation of powers doctrine; the judiciary did not have exclusive authority over the sentencing of criminal defendants; and the delegation of sentencing authority to the Institute contained reasonably definite standards. Because defendant had no liberty interest derived from the due process clause in obtaining treatment at the Institute instead of being incarcerated, his due process claim was meritless. In addition, because he was a member of the advantaged class, he lacked standing to challenge, on equal protection grounds, the constitutionality of the statute with regards to its differing treatment of convicted but unsentenced defendants, civilians, and sentenced defendants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Scalzo v. Danbury


No. 14485


Supreme Court of Connecticut


224 Conn. 124; 617 A.2d 440; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 383


September 23, 1992, Argued  
December 8, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in four counts to recover damages for the alleged taking by inverse condemnation of certain of the named plaintiff's real property without just compensation, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the case was withdrawn as to the defendant Russell M. Foti et al. and where the first and second counts of the complaint were withdrawn; thereafter, the court, Pickett, J., granted the motion for summary judgment as to the third count filed by the named defendant et al.; subsequently, the court, Geen, J., granted the motion to dismiss the fourth count filed by the named defendant and rendered judgment thereon, and the named plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee zoning authorities in an action by the landowner seeking damages for the alleged taking of his property under Conn. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: In separate actions, the owner sought both a variance and an amendment to the zoning regulations to allow him access to his industrial acreage through his adjacent residential acreage, which was prohibited under the regulations. Both requests were denied and while the appeals were pending he brought his action alleging inverse condemnation. The trial court, on appeal of the first actions, determined that neither the denial of the variance application nor the denial of the amendment application resulted in an unconstitutional taking. Accordingly, the trial court granted the zoning authorities' summary judgment motion in the inverse condemnation action and concluded that the owner's claim was precluded because it had been fully and fairly litigated in the prior appeal. The court affirmed the judgment but did so on the grounds of issue, not claim, preclusion. The court reasoned that the trial court's ruling on the taking issues was necessary and essential to the prior judgment because, if the trial court had found that an unconstitutional taking had occurred, it would have been required to sustain the appeals, whether or not the zoning authorities' actions were supported by evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted summary judgment in favor of the zoning authorities in the action by the landowner alleging inverse condemnation.

 

207 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roman


No. 14073


Supreme Court of Connecticut


224 Conn. 63; 616 A.2d 266; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 350


September 23, 1992, Argued  
November 17, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Roman v. Connecticut, 507 U.S. 1039, 113 S. Ct. 1868, 123 L. Ed. 2d 488, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 2915 (1993)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Roman v. City of Hartford, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 68226 (D. Conn., May 14, 2013)
Related proceeding at State v. Miranda, 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 451 (Conn. App. Ct., Sept. 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Purtill, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) for murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a.


OVERVIEW: Defendant executed a waiver of his Miranda rights in Spanish so that the police could interrogate him regarding a murder. Although a translator was present at the interrogation, defendant did not use his services. At trial, defendant did not use the services of the translator either. Defendant claimed that he was entitled to a word by word translation of the interrogation, he did not sufficiently understand the interrogation because it was in English, and he was unduly coerced at the interrogation because it was in English. The court held that the convictions were proper because defendant spoke and understood English. The court noted that defendant's failure to use the translators at the interrogation and at trial indicated that he had a sufficient command of English to understand the interrogation and the trial. Also, defendant stated in Spanish at the end of the interrogation that he understood what happened at the interrogation. There was no abuse of discretion in allowing a fellow jail inmate to testify against defendant after the State and defendant rested, especially where defendant did not ask for a continuance to question the witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

208 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Calfee v. Usman


No. 14541


Supreme Court of Connecticut


224 Conn. 29; 616 A.2d 250; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 349


September 22, 1992, Argued  
October 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the plaintiff as a result of the defendant's alleged negligence, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Dean, J., denied the plaintiff's application for a prejudgment attachment against certain of the defendant's real property; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiff's motion to open the order denying the prejudgment remedy, and the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured person filed an application for a prejudgment remedy in conjunction with the personal injury action that she filed against defendant driver. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) denied her application as a matter of law. Thereafter, she filed a motion to open the order. The trial court denied the motion, and she filed a complaint with the appellate court. The court transferred her appeal.


OVERVIEW: To secure her right to collect a possible judgment, the injured person sought, in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278d, to establish probable cause to sustain the validity of her claim. The trial court ruled that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-278c, 52-278d were facially unenforceable. On appeal, the court reversed and noted that there was a strong presumption of constitutionality. In the absence of weighty countervailing circumstances, the trial court's invalidation of the legislation was improvident. The court construed the legislative intent and concluded that the provisions for a prejudgment remedy found in Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-278c and 52-278d were not unconstitutionally vague on their face. Because the driver was afforded the opportunity, in an adversarial hearing, to contest the validity of the claims made in support of the application, a prejudgment attachment could have constitutionally been issued without a showing of exigent circumstances. When there was no ex parte impairment of the driver's property rights, a judicial finding of probable cause sufficed to satisfy his constitutional right to due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which denied the injured person's application for prejudgment interest as a matter of law. The court remanded the personal injury action for further proceedings.

210 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Lozada v. Warden


No. 14359


Supreme Court of Connecticut


223 Conn. 834; 613 A.2d 818; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 283


March 25, 1992, Argued  
September 1, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Kaplan, J., granted the respondent's motion to quash and rendered judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, Landau and Heiman, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings, and the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent warden appealed the judgment from the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which reversed a judgment that granted the warden's motion to quash an amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus and rendered judgment dismissing the petition, and granted certification of the writ petition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner entered a plea of guilty to murder and subsequently petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus on the ground of ineffective assistance of counsel. After his unsuccessful writ, the petitioner sought another writ of habeas corpus challenging the effectiveness of his appointed counsel in his first proceeding for writ of habeas corpus. The petition was denied, but the appellate court reversed and held that he could seek the writ on the grounds of ineffective assistance of habeas counsel. The warden appealed and the court affirmed the appellate court's decision. The court reasoned that the right to effective assistance of counsel is inherent in the right to appointed counsel for an indigent petitioner in a habeas action. The court held that nonconstitutional claims could be raised in habeas proceedings as well as constitutional issues. And finally, the court held that release from incarceration was not required to be the immediate relief achievable from a habeas petition and that the grant of a new trial would be the appropriate relief. Thus, the court held that a writ of habeas was permissible on the ground that an attorney at a prior habeas corpus proceeding was ineffective.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversing the denial of a successive habeas corpus proceeding on the ground of ineffective habeas counsel was affirmed.

 

211 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


In re Valerie D.


No. 14420


Supreme Court of Connecticut


223 Conn. 492; 613 A.2d 748; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 274; 20 A.L.R.5th 981


May 6, 1992, Argued  
August 18, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition by the commissioner of children and youth services to terminate the parental rights of the respondents with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Plainville, and tried to the court, Brenneman, J.; judgment granting the petition, from which the respondent mother appealed to the Appellate Court, Spallone, Norcott and Lavery, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the respondent mother, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother sought review of the judgment from the Appellate Court, which affirmed the trial court's judgment terminating her parental rights pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 45a-717(f)(2) & (f)(3), arising from mother's use of cocaine in the hours before giving birth to the child.


OVERVIEW: After the mother, a cocaine user, gave birth to her child, the commissioner of children and youth services obtained temporary care and custody of the child due to the mother's alleged cocaine use within hours of beginning labor and petitioned for termination of parental rights. The trial court terminated the mother's parental rights. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court reversed. The court first found that the trial court's factual finding that the mother injected cocaine after beginning labor was not supported by the evidence. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-717(f)(2) was to be construed narrowly, in a way that minimizes state interference. The court held that § 45a-717(f)(2) did not permit termination of parental rights based on prenatal conduct of the mother. The court's reading of the statute required that only the conduct of a parent of a child already born could be considered. The court also held that the actions of the state in taking the child away from the mother effectively prevented the development of an ongoing parent-child relationship, the absence of which constituted grounds for termination under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-717(f)(3).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the lower courts terminating the mother's parental rights. The court held that the statute authorizing termination for a parent's conduct could not justify termination for conduct committed before the child was born and that the statute permitting termination for failure to develop an ongoing parent-child relationship could not justify termination when the relationship was frustrated by the state's actions.

State v. Canty


No. 14463


Supreme Court of Connecticut


223 Conn. 703; 613 A.2d 1287; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 281


April 2, 1992, Argued  
August 12, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of sale of a narcotic substance by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the jury before Mottolese, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk, Geographical Area No. 20 (Connecticut), which convicted him in a jury trial as an accessory to the sale of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(b), 53a-8.


OVERVIEW: In an undercover operation, defendant helped a co-defendant sell a packet of heroin to an officer. While admitting he was at the scene, defendant claimed he was a mere bystander, and neither knew what was occurring nor participated in the crime. He claimed that due process was violated by asking him at trial about his failure to tell his attorney and authorities that a third party had allegedly dropped a brown bag containing vials of crack cocaine. While comment on defendant's post-arrest silence was barred, the alleged violation was harmless error. The court rejected defendant's next claim that it was an abuse of discretion to allow merely cumulative rebuttal testimony. The record failed to support his claim that the trial court's jury instructions unfairly marshaled evidence for the State while ignoring evidence favorable to defendant, thus depriving him of a fair trial. Any error in refusing to allow a defense witness to remove handcuffs before testifying was determined to have been harmless. Finally, the court rejected a claim that a mistrial was in order due to the prosecutor's references in closing argument to the absence of two defense witnesses, as any error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant as an accessory to the sale of narcotics.

Walker v. Commissioner of Correction


No. 14339


Supreme Court of Connecticut


223 Conn. 411; 611 A.2d 413; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 260


June 9, 1992, Argued  
August 11, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of error from the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, Scheinblum, J., denying the plaintiff in error's petition for certification to appeal from the dismissal of his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which denied him a grant of certification to appeal its decision dismissing his writ of habeas corpus. The inmate claimed that the habeas court abused its discretion in denying his petition for certification to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of murder. The conviction was affirmed on appeal. The inmate then filed for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging his incarceration was illegal because he was denied the effective assistance of appellate counsel because his appellate counsel failed to challenge an instruction on circumstantial evidence. The habeas court dismissed the writ. The inmate timely filed a petition for certification to appeal the habeas court's decision. The habeas court denied the petition for certification. The inmate then filed a writ of error alleging that the habeas court abused its discretion in denying the certification to appeal because it failed to evaluate the allegedly erroneous instruction in isolation from the remainder of the charge in order to determine whether the instruction diluted the state's burden of proof. The court affirmed the judgment of the habeas court finding that its conclusion that the allegedly improper charge had to be examined in the context of the entire charge was correct. The court thus held that the inmate's claim that the habeas court abused its discretion in denying certification to appeal was without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the habeas court dismissing the inmate's writ of habeas corpus and denying his request for a grant of certification to appeal was affirmed.

State v. Waller


No. 14367


Supreme Court of Connecticut


223 Conn. 283; 612 A.2d 1189; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 255


March 31, 1992, Argued  
August 4, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Hauser, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Landau and Heiman, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument that was denied.

215 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Esposito


No. 14012


Supreme Court of Connecticut


223 Conn. 299; 613 A.2d 242; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 256


April 30, 1992, Argued  
August 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, robbery in the first degree and burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument that was denied.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which entered a jury verdict that convicted him of felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(2), and burglary in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of felony murder, robbery in the first degree, and burglary in the first degree. Defendant argued that the trial court improperly denied his motions during jury selection to excuse certain venirepersons for cause. The court reversed the convictions and ordered a new trial. The trial court erred in failing to excuse a prospective juror for cause where the juror lived in the neighborhood in which the murder took place and she stated that she would be in an awkward position if she found defendant not guilty. It was reversible error for the trial court to force defendant to use peremptory challenges on persons who should have been excused for cause where defendant subsequently exhausted all of his peremptory challenges and an additional challenge was sought and denied. The trial court's action abridged defendant's right to exercise peremptory challenges in the selection of his jury under Conn. Const. art. I, § 19. On retrial, a question regarding defendant's initial failure to tell police where he was on the night the crimes were committed was not allowable unless its context clearly indicated that it referred only to defendant's prearrest silence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for felony murder, robbery in the first degree, and burglary in the first degree and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

216 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arline


No. 14377


Supreme Court of Connecticut


223 Conn. 52; 612 A.2d 755; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 226


April 29, 1992, Argued  
July 21, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Quinn, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., Foti and Landau, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument that was denied.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a trial to a jury, defendant was convicted of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a). The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the court granted defendant's petition for certification to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The jury could reasonably have found that defendant sexually assaulted a cellmate. Defendant did not testify at trial but presented evidence tending to discredit the complainant's testimony. The court found that a new trial was required because the trial court improperly restricted defense counsel from commenting on certain facts that had been elicited from the complainant on cross-examination, thereby violating defendant's right to the effective assistance of counsel. The trial court improperly assumed that defendant was required to present specific evidence of an agreement between the State and the complainant or of the complainant's belief that he had received lenient treatment on his criminal charges in exchange for his testimony. However, in order to argue the question of the complainant's motivation, defendant needed to establish only a reasonable inference that the complainant could have believed that there was a causal connection between his testimony and the disposition of the criminal charges against him. While the prosecutor's comment regarding defendant's failure to testify appeared to be improper, the court declined to decide whether it would have required a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded to that court with direction to remand the case to the trial court for a new trial.

 

217 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Baybank Connecticut, N.A. v. Thumlert


No. 14392


Supreme Court of Connecticut


222 Conn. 784; 610 A.2d 658; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 220


April 29, 1992, Argued  
July 14, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage on certain real property owned by the named defendant et al., and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, where the court, A. Aronson, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for default and where the court, Allen, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for judgment of strict foreclosure and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court, Allen, J., granted the motion to open the judgment filed by the defendant United Bank and Trust Company and granted that defendant's motion for judgment of foreclosure by sale and rendered judgment thereon; after a sale was held, the court, Goldberg, J., denied the plaintiff's motion for a deficiency judgment and rendered a supplemental judgment confirming the sale, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagee appealed a supplemental judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain (Connecticut) that confirmed a sale and appealed the denial of its motion for a deficiency judgment. The mortgagee contended that the 30-day limit in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-14(a) for deficiency judgment motions in mortgage foreclosure cases did not apply to judgments of foreclosure by sale.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor granted a mortgage to the mortgagee on land to secure a promissory note. The mortgagor defaulted on the note. The mortgagee filed a foreclosure action against the mortgagor in the trial court. That court granted the mortgagee's motion for judgment of strict foreclosure. It then opened the judgment of strict foreclosure and granted the motion of a bank, a subsequent lienholder, for judgment of foreclosure by sale. It then executed and ratified a judicial sale of the property, and rendered the supplemental judgment confirming the sale. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case. Section 49-14(a) was not applicable to judgments of foreclosure by sale given that the language of § 49-14(a) indicated that even though an evidentiary hearing was needed to calculate the value of the mortgaged real property, and consequently the total of any deficiency after a strict foreclosure, this calculation would be unnecessary after any foreclosure by sale. As a result, the 30-day limit had to be interpreted as applying only to strict foreclosures. The mortgagor did not raise the defense of laches as to any delay by the mortgagee in filing the deficiency judgment motion.


OUTCOME: In the action against the mortgagor, the court reversed the supplemental judgment that confirmed the sale, and reversed the denial of the mortgagee's motion for a deficiency judgment. The court remanded the action with instructions to rule on mortgagee's deficiency judgment motion.

 

218 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Perry v. Perry


No. 14404


Supreme Court of Connecticut


222 Conn. 799; 611 A.2d 400; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 224


May 5, 1992, Argued  
June 29, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 29, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, F. Freedman, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief; thereafter, the matter was referred to Edmund H. Miller, family support magistrate, who denied the defendant's motion for modification and granted the plaintiff's motion for contempt, and the defendant appealed to the Superior Court, Bassick, J., which affirmed the judgment of the family support magistrate, and the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Fairfield District (Connecticut), which affirmed the ruling of the family support magistrate that held him in contempt and ordered him imprisoned for failing to pay support to appellee mother. The primary issue before the court was whether the magistrate's contempt power under the Family Support Magistrate's Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46b-231 through 46b-235, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The father was found in contempt and was incarcerated by the family magistrate for failing to pay child support. On his release, the father challenged the constitutionality of that act, arguing that contempt was a power exclusive to judges and could not be given to non-judges by the legislature. On review the court held that the father's release did not make the appeal moot in part because the issue was very important and because the father could well be confronted with the same problem in the future. The court held that the legislative creation of courts or administrative bodies of inferior, limited, or special jurisdiction was lawful and included transferring from the superior court the power to impose sanctions for contempt of court. The court also held that contempt was not an exclusively judicial power, citing various administrative, executive, and legislative bodies that had both quasi-judicial functions and the power of contempt. The court held that the legislature had the authority to order the restraint of anyone if it was necessary for the enforcement of the law; the test was the degree to which it granted that power and whether appellate judicial review was possible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that affirmed the ruling of the family magistrate finding the father in contempt for failing to pay support to the mother and ordering his incarceration.

Supreme Court of Connecticut

DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed a judgment from the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which ordered dismissal of plaintiff landowners' appeal of a grant of a wetlands permit and subdivision approval to defendant developer by defendant Inland Wetlands Commission of the Town of Bethany and remanded the case with direction to dismiss the matter for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The developer applied to the Commission for a permit to build a subdivision on its property. The Commission granted a wetlands permit and subdivision approval to the developer. The landowners brought an action for administrative review against the developer and Commission. The trial court ruled in favor of the developer and Commission. An intermediate appellate court ordered dismissal of the landowners' appeal because an attorney's signature on the citation had deprived the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction to hear the landowners' administrative appeal. OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court, which had ordered dismissal of the landowners' appeal of the Commission's grant of a wetlands permit and subdivision approval to the developer, and remanded the case to the intermediate appellate court for consideration of the merits of the landowners' claims challenging the decision of the Commission.

State v. Geisler


No. 14365


Supreme Court of Connecticut


222 Conn. 672; 610 A.2d 1225; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 214; 61 U.S.L.W. 2093


February 19, 1992, Argued  
June 18, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle, evading responsibility and operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the jury before Lewis, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., Borden, O'Connell, Norcott and Lavery, Js., with Spallone, Daly and Foti, Js., dissenting, which reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and for a new trial on the assault charge; on petition by the state to the United States Supreme Court for a writ of certiorari, that court vacated the Appellate Court's judgment on the assault charge and remanded the case for further consideration; on remand, the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., O'Connell, Norcott, Foti, Lavery, Landau and Heiman, Js., with Spallone and Daly, Js., dissenting, ordered a new trial [***2] on the charge of assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which on remand from the United States Supreme Court, ordered a new trial of defendant charged with assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle in connection with a hit-and-run accident in which the inebriated defendant struck and injured a motorcyclist.


OVERVIEW: After a hit and run accident, police found at defendant's home a car matching the description given by the injured cyclist. When they did not get a response to their inquiries, the officers entered the home, found defendant and arrested him. At the police station, the police administered blood alcohol tests and obtained other evidence used to convict him of second degree assault with a motor vehicle. Defendant appealed his conviction and eventually, the United States Supreme Court remanded to the state appellate court, which ordered a new trial. The state sought review. The court affirmed, holding that although under federal exclusionary rule, the evidence obtained outside the home would be admissible, the Connecticut constitution afforded greater protection than did the U.S. Constitution against unlawful searches and seizures. The court held that the evidence obtained both inside and outside the home was inadmissible under the state constitution because the warrantless entry into defendant's home was unlawful. The court held that the appellate court had used the proper standard in determining that no emergency existed to justify the police entry into defendant's home.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's order granting a new trial to defendant, earlier convicted of second degree assault with a motor vehicle, because the state constitution made inadmissible blood-alcohol and other evidence obtained outside the home after a warrantless entry into defendant's home that was not justified on the basis of exigent circumstances.

Bunkley v. Commissioner of Correction


No. 14305


Supreme Court of Connecticut


222 Conn. 444; 610 A.2d 598; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 186


December 5, 1991, Argued  
June 3, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Potter, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment after a trial in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which dismissed the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus alleging a constitutional claim of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel after his conviction on charges of second-degree manslaughter and third-degree assault.


OVERVIEW: The inmate killed three people while fleeing from police in his automobile. After a jury trial, the inmate was convicted on charges of manslaughter and assault. On appeal, the inmate's appellate counsel did not raise a claim that the trial court gave an improper instruction to the jury concerning permissible inferences that could be drawn from circumstantial evidence. After his conviction was affirmed on appeal, the inmate filed a petition for habeas corpus asserting that he was denied effective assistance of counsel in connection with his appeal. The Superior Court entered judgment denying the petition. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the Superior Court properly applied the Strickland test to his challenge to the effectiveness of appellate counsel, under which the inmate was required to establish that, but for appellate counsel's unprofessional errors, the result of his trial would have been different. The court held that when considering the "prejudice" component of the Strickland test, the Superior Court properly focused on the result of the trial, not the appeal, and that the ultimate issue was the reliability of the verdict that resulted in an appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Iovieno v. Commissioner of Correction


No. 14278


Supreme Court of Connecticut


222 Conn. 254; 608 A.2d 1174; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 173


February 13, 1992, Argued  
June 2, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of error from the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, Scheinblum, J., denying the plaintiff in error's petition for certification to appeal the dismissal of his amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate brought a writ of error challenging the denial by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) of his certification to appeal the dismissal of his habeas petition.


OVERVIEW: After the inmate's habeas petition was dismissed, the inmate sought certification to appeal. However, his certification petition was not brought within the 10-day period provided under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-470(b). In addition, the inmate did not seek permission for an extension of the time limit. As a result, the trial court denied the inmate's petition for certification to appeal. The inmate argued that the trial court had discretion to accept an untimely petition. Affirming the judgment, the court ruled that the trial court correctly concluded that it had no discretion to accept the inmate's petition for certification to appeal after the 10-day time period under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-470(b). The court found the statute to be unambiguous. Even if the statute's meaning were not clear, however, the court determined that the statute's legislative history revealed an intent to remedy a perceived problem of too many frivolous appeals of denied habeas petitions. Thus, the statute's legislative history was consistent with the court's ruling that the trial court lacked discretion under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-470(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Tamm v. Burns


No. 14355


Supreme Court of Connecticut


222 Conn. 280; 610 A.2d 590; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 175


February 18, 1992, Argued  
June 2, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged inverse condemnation of certain of the plaintiff's real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Ryan, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, Norcott and Lavery, Js., which reversed, in part, the trial court's judgment, and the named defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state commissioner of transportation sought review of a decision from the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which reversed, in part, the trial court's decision in an action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged inverse condemnation of certain of the plaintiff trustee's real property. The trial court had granted the commissioner's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue in this appeal was whether the trustee's allegations, that the state's operation of a truck inspection and weigh station on its property, which was adjacent to his, had caused additional noise, unsightliness, and air pollution on his property, sufficiently stated a claim of inverse condemnation under Conn. Const. art. I, § 11. The court held that the facts alleged did not demonstrate an interference with the trustee's property that in a substantial degree abridged or destroyed the value of the property or the trustee's use and enjoyment of it. The court held that although the trustee's allegations could conceivably support a claim of nuisance or some other sort of tortious interference by the state with the trustee's use of his property, they did not amount to a taking of the trustee's property in the constitutional sense. The court further held that an individual who complained of tortious interference by the State that was not so serious as to constitute a constitutional taking of his private property was not without recourse through other avenues of relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, and the case was remanded to that court with direction to affirm the trial court's dismissal of this action.

State v. Marra


No. 13965


Supreme Court of Connecticut


222 Conn. 506; 610 A.2d 1113; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 210


February 18, 1992, Argued  
June 1, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before S. Freedman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a.


OVERVIEW: The state prosecuted defendant for murdering the deceased with a baseball bat, refrigerating the body, and dumping it into a river. The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction under § 53a-54a and concluded that jurisdiction existed because the evidence submitted at the probable cause hearing warranted the inference that defendant intentionally killed the victim. Defendant cross-examined the state's witnesses as to certain evidence, which was not maliciously lost. Moreover, accomplice testimony and tangible evidence were relevant, and admissible evidence showing that the victim was dead, and died as a result of defendant's actions. Thus, defendant was not denied a fair trial or due process. The jury was properly charged on the biases of the accomplice witnesses, and any error was not plain. Defendant was not prejudiced by the expansion of the information. Nor was he prejudiced by the state's comments, which did not improperly address defendant's failure to testify or his right to silence. Finally, the trial court properly instructed the jury on the burden of proof and properly marshaled the evidence. Thus, reversal of defendant's conviction was not required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

 

228 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Fonfara v. Reapportionment Com.


No. 14421


Supreme Court of Connecticut


222 Conn. 166; 610 A.2d 153; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 171


January 16, 1992, Argued  
May 26, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to this court challenging the constitutionality of the plan of redistricting for the state house of representatives filed by the defendant and requesting this court to establish a redistricting plan to correct the defendant's proposed plan or to order the defendant to correct its plan to comply with the town integrity principle mandated in the state constitution.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, citizens and electors of the state, challenged the plan of redistricting the state house of representatives as a violation of the town integrity principle mandated in the state constitution.


OVERVIEW: The citizens and electors of the state challenged the decennial reapportionment of respondent reapportionment commission. The court noted that once a duly appointed reapportionment commission published a redistricting plan, Conn. Const. art. III, § 6(c) prescribed that the redistricting plan had the full force of law. Thus, the court's review of the validity of the plan, like any other judicial review, was limited to an inquiry into the plan's compliance with applicable state and federal constitutional mandates. This review invoked the court's judicial authority, but did not warrant the court's exercise of legislative power. Thus, the court refused the citizens' request that the court correct alleged errors in the plan. The court stated that its judicial reluctance to become too deeply involved in reapportionment disputes was not confined to prudential concerns about entering the political thicket. It also stemmed from the inherent unsuitability of such disputes to the ordinary and traditional principles of adjudication. The court found that the citizens and electors had failed to meet their burden of showing a constitutional violation of the town integrity principle.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.

 

229 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nelson


No. 14250


Supreme Court of Connecticut


221 Conn. 635; 605 A.2d 1381; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 109


January 9, 1992, Argued  
April 14, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Kulawiz, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the case was presented to the court on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him on a plea of nolo contendere pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a of felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot a man in a struggle during a robbery of an after hours club. Defendant sought to withdraw his plea of nolo contendere, claiming that the plea was not made knowingly because, at the time that his plea was entered, the trial court did not inform him that if he went to trial he would have the privilege against self-incrimination. The court held that the federal constitution required only that a defendant, at the time of the entry of a plea of guilty or nolo contendere, be informed by the trial court that, in conformity with his right against self-incrimination, he could not be compelled to enter that plea. The federal constitution mandated only that a defendant be apprised of the fact that he did not have to enter a plea of guilty or nolo contendere and thus incriminate himself. The trial court's canvass, prior to the acceptance of defendant's plea, adequately informed him that he possessed a right against self-incrimination that guaranteed that he need not incriminate himself by entering a plea of nolo contendere. Therefore, defendant failed to establish a constitutional violation clearly existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

230 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hart


No. 14230


Supreme Court of Connecticut


221 Conn. 595; 605 A.2d 1366; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 106


October 2, 1991, Argued  
April 7, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of cocaine by a person who is not drug-dependent, sale of cocaine, conspiracy to sell cocaine and possession of cocaine, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Ripley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Spallone, Norcott and Landau, Js., which reversed, in part, the trial court's decision and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of acquittal of the crime of sale of cocaine by a person who is not drug-dependent and to resentence the defendant in accordance with her other convictions, from which the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a decision of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which reversed a superior court judgment convicting defendant of sale of cocaine by a person who was not drug-dependent in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) and which remanded the case with direction to acquit defendant. At issue was whether defendant or the state bore the burden of proving drug dependence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after obtaining a gram of cocaine in exchange for an undercover narcotics officer's money. At trial, the jury heard evidence that defendant was drug-dependent at the time of the arrest, as defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-240(18), (19). On cross-examination of those witnesses, the state elicited some evidence that she was not. The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction on the ground that the state failed to disprove drug dependence beyond a reasonable doubt. The state could not prove the absence of drug dependence by an impermissible inference of the opposite of the testimony of defense witnesses. However, the absence of drug dependency was not an element of the crime of sale of cocaine by a person who was not drug-dependent under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b). The burden of proving this exemption from liability was on defendant, by a preponderance of the evidence, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a278(b). Because defendant reasonably believed that she needed only to raise the issue at trial, defendant was entitled to a new trial of the charge at which she could attempt to prove her drug dependence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's conclusion that defendant was entitled to a judgment of acquittal. The court ordered the case to be remanded to the trial court with direction to reverse the conviction of sale of a narcotic substance by a person who was not drug-dependent and to order a new trial on that charge.

 

231 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Howard


No. 14285


Supreme Court of Connecticut


221 Conn. 447; 604 A.2d 1294; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 88


November 8, 1991, Argued  
March 17, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, burglary in the first degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree and assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; remanded for modification of sentence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which, following a jury trial, convicted him of robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, burglary in the first degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree, and assault in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his convictions for robbery, conspiracy to commit robbery, burglary, conspiracy to commit burglary, and assault. The court reversed and remanded the case in part. The court found that defendant was not denied due process through an overly suggestive photo identification and he was not denied material discovery. However, the court agreed with defendant that he could not be convicted of both conspiracy to commit robbery and conspiracy to commit burglary. The court held that whether the object of a single agreement was to commit one or many crimes, it was in either case that agreement which constituted the conspiracy which the statute punished. The one agreement could not be taken to be several agreements or several conspiracies because it envisaged the violation of several statutes rather than one. The single agreement was the prohibited conspiracy and, however diverse its objects, it violated but a single statute. For such a violation, only the single penalty prescribed by the statute could be imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court in part and reversed the judgment of the superior court in part. The court remanded to the superior court with direction to combine defendant's two conspiracy convictions and to vacate the sentence for one of the conspiracy convictions.

Gallacher v. Commissioner of Revenue Servs.


No. 14194


Supreme Court of Connecticut


221 Conn. 166; 602 A.2d 996; 1992 Conn. LEXIS 36; 19 Media L. Rep. 2140


October 29, 1991, Argued  
February 11, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the assessment of use taxes on certain purchases of tangible personal property by the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and referred to Hon. Charles S. House, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment for the defendant; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiffs' motion to open the judgment, and the plaintiffs appealed.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners and publishers of a weekly publication, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which affirmed defendant revenue services commissioner's decision that denied an exemption for their publication under the state use tax, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-412(f), and levied use tax assessments. A state trial referee sustained the commissioner's assessments.


OVERVIEW: The free publication contained weekly television listings and entertainment articles but it did not include general news items. The deputy commissioner concluded that: (a) plaintiffs' purchase of the publications from the printer was a purchase of tangible personal property from a retailer for storage, acceptance, consumption or use in Connecticut as described in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-411(1), which imposed the use tax; (b) the publications did not qualify as "newspapers" under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-412(f) and, therefore, they were not exempt from the use tax; and (c) the use tax did not violate the First Amendment or the Commerce or Equal Protection clauses of the United States Constitution. Plaintiffs argued in part that their publication was a "newspaper" entitled to an exemption from the use tax. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. In so ruling, the court examined the format of the publications and concluded that they did not fit within the common understanding of what one would envision as a newspaper, and therefore, that it was not eligible for the exemption in § 12-412(f). The court also ruled that the use tax was rationally related to a legitimate government purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which affirmed the commissioner's decision denying an exemption from the Connecticut use tax for plaintiffs' weekly publication.

State v. Lewis


No. 14034


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


220 Conn. 602; 600 A.2d 1330; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 511


September 24, 1991, Argued  
December 17, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of murder and two counts of the crime of conspiracy to commit murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count each of murder and conspiracy to commit murder, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court, New Haven Judicial District (Connecticut) convicting him of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a and conspiracy to commit murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-48.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from the judgment convicting him of murder and conspiracy to commit murder. The court first concluded that there was sufficient evidence to support the finding that defendant conspired to commit murder. Together, defendant and his associate obtained guns from a car, fired at the victim, and then fled. The State's proof indicated an informal agreement to cause the victim's death, that defendant intended to cause the death at the time of the agreement, and that defendant committed an overt act in furtherance of the conspiracy, satisfying the elements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-48. The court then held that the warrantless seizure of evidence from defendant's wallet was properly admissible under U.S. Const. amend. IV because the search was conducted incident to a lawful arrest. The court also rejected defendant's claims that an oral waiver of Miranda rights was insufficient and that the trial court improperly failed to instruct the jury on defendant's theory of self-defense. Defendant failed to produce sufficient evidence raising a reasonable doubt as to whether defendant acted in self-defense. The court decided that defendant did not raise reversible errors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of murder and conspiracy to commit murder.

Fairfield Plumbing & Heating Supply Corp. v. Kosa


No. 14294


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


220 Conn. 643; 600 A.2d 1; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 513


October 31, 1991, Argued  
December 17, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a judgment lien on certain of the defendant's real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Thim, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for judgment of strict foreclosure and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court, Jones, J., denied the plaintiff's motion for a deficiency judgment, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a judgment creditor, sought review of a decision from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which denied plaintiff's motion for a deficiency judgment.


OVERVIEW: The judgment creditor obtained a judgment against defendant in connection with nonpayment for plumbing hardware and supplies sold to defendant. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-380a(a), the judgment creditor recorded a judgment lien on the land records of two town. At that time, defendant owned a one-half interest in properties located in each town. Because the judgment debt had not been satisfied, the judgment creditor commenced a foreclosure action on both properties and sought relief in the form of strict foreclosure and a deficiency judgment. After concluding that the provisions of § 49-14(a) concerning deficiency judgments did not apply to judgment lien foreclosure proceedings, the trial court ruled that the judgment creditor was not entitled to a deficiency judgment because it concluded that, as a matter of law, the provisions with respect to deficiency judgments contained in § 49-14(a) did not apply to the foreclosure of a judgment lien. On review, the court reversed because it held that § 52-380a(c) and § 49-14(a) had to be read together to afford a judgment creditor access to a proceeding to determine the deficiency remaining after strict foreclosure of a judgment lien.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment denying the judgment creditor's motion for a deficiency judgment and the case was remanded for further proceedings on that motion.

Ghent v. Zoning Com. of Waterbury


No. 14199


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


220 Conn. 584; 600 A.2d 1010; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 514


September 27, 1991, Argued  
December 17, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiffs from a decision by the defendant approving the application for a text amendment to the Waterbury zoning ordinance filed by the mayor of Waterbury, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the plaintiff Gertrude T. Bergen et al. withdrew from the action; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, Heiman, J.; judgment for the defendant dismissing the appeal, from which the named plaintiff et al. appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) dismissing their appeal of a decision of defendant zoning commission, which amended an ordinance to prohibit multiple family dwellings in certain commercial zones.


OVERVIEW: The zoning commission passed an ordinance amendment that prohibited multiple family homes in commercial zones in which the landowners owned property. The mayor sponsored the amendment, presided as the non-voting, ex-officio chairman of the planning commission, and had the city attorney speak before the zoning commission in favor of the amendment. The trial court entered judgment dismissing the landowners' appeal of the zoning commission's action, rejecting the claim that the mayor's involvement in the process rendered the amendment invalid. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that: (1) the mayor had a duty to express what he believed to be in the best interests of the community, and his advocacy of the amendment was within his power under the city charter; (2) the mayor was not disqualified by a conflict of interest under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-21 from membership on the planning commission; (3) the zoning commission was entitled to the city attorney's advice; (4) the zoning commission did not violate Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-1(a) by taking action while short of members lost due to vacancies; and (5) the amendment reasonably served the city's general welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the landowners' appeal of the zoning commission's amendment to an ordinance prohibiting multiple family homes in certain commercial zones.

State v. Tillman


No. 14085


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


220 Conn. 487; 600 A.2d 738; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 530


September 26, 1991, Argued  
December 3, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree, robbery in the third degree, assault in the third degree and larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him for first degree kidnapping pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(B), first degree sexual assault pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a), and other crimes. Defendant argued unconstitutional jury selection, improper jury instructions, and improper exclusion of evidence.


OVERVIEW: After jurors were selected, the trial court called a second panel to choose alternates. Defendant moved for a new panel, arguing that neither panel represented a fair cross-section. The trial court denied the motion as untimely. Later, defendant again unsuccessfully objected to the panel, and informed the trial court that the clerk was dismissing jurors for economic hardship if their employers would not pay the difference between their jury pay and their normal wages. After trial, defendant again raised the objection in his motion for a new trial, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that defendant failed to make a prima facie case of unconstitutional jury selection because he did not offer any evidence that a "distinctive group" was excluded from the panels, or that unconstitutional criteria involving a suspect class was used in selecting the panels. Further, the trial court properly charged the jury about the victim's ability to observe defendant, and that defendant's consciousness of his guilt could be inferred from the fact that, before police told him that the victim had been punched, defendant told police he did not cut his hand hitting a girl.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant for kidnapping, sexual assault, and other crimes.

State v. Williams


No. 14150


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


220 Conn. 385; 599 A.2d 1053; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 484


September 27, 1991, Argued  
November 19, 1991, Decided  
November 19, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, murder, attempted murder, robbery in the first degree, attempted assault in the first degree, assault in the second degree and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Maiocco, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of felony murder, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Fairfield Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted him of felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his companions forced the victim to the ground, took money from his pockets, then shot him. The victim died and defendant was convicted of felony murder. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court determined that the State was entitled to a jury instruction on accessorial liability. Defendant could be convicted as an accessory even though he was charged only as a principal because the evidence presented at trial was sufficient to establish accessorial conduct and defendant was specifically put on notice by the trial court, prior to beginning his defense, that the issue of accessorial liability was still in the case. The exposure of two jurors to a televised interview of the victim's mother was not prejudicial because their exposure was extremely limited, neither juror discussed the program with his fellow jurors, the trial court personally viewed the videotape and concluded that its only effect was to possibly evoke some sympathy. The trial court limited defendant's cross-examination of a witness because the trial court was not satisfied that the prior statements were inconsistent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision convicting defendant of felony murder.
