J., Foti and Lavery, Js., which affirmed the trial court's decision, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed his convictions for sexual assault in the first degree, burglary in the second degree, and sexual assault in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sexual assault in the first degree, burglary in the second degree, and sexual assault in the third degree. He entered pleas of guilty to the first two counts and an Alford plea to the third count. Defendant and the prosecutor agreed that the State would recommend a sentence of 20 years but that defendant retained the right to argue for a lesser sentence. Defendant argued for a 10 year sentence, but the trial court imposed a term of 20 years on the sexual assault in the first degree and two concurrent 5 year sentences on the other counts. Defendant appealed his conviction and argued that the trial court erred in failing to provide him with notice of his right under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-195 to sentence review. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court granted defendant's petition for certification. The court noted that under § 51-195, a sentence resulting from a plea agreement was not subject to review. The court held that defendant's agreement was not a plea agreement under the terms of the statute because no specific term of years was determined.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the action to the appellate court. The court directed the appellate court to remand the action to the trial court with instructions that defendant was to be given the notice required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-195 and that he be allowed to file an application for sentence review within 30 days of his receipt of such notice.

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


220 Conn. 362; 599 A.2d 9; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 481

November 12, 1991, Decided  
November 12, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended December 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a decision by the defendant commission granting with modification the plaintiffs' application for permission to expand a mining and excavation operation on certain of their property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the court, Moraghan, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court, which set aside the trial court's decision and remanded the case for further proceedings; on remand, the court, Karazin, J., rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the judgment on remand of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal. The trial court had previously affirmed the decision of defendant zoning and planning commission granting with modification the landowner' application for permission to expand a mining and excavation operation on their property.


OVERVIEW: The landowners contended that they were deprived of their property rights unconstitutionally by the refusal of the commission to grant in its entirety their application for a permit to expand their sand and gravel mining activities and that the denial of the permit to excavate the entire area constituted a taking as a matter of law in view of the evidence of the financial benefits they were prevented from realizing. The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the landowners' appeal holding that the landowners' claims of no competent evidence to support the finding that the value of the property had increased as a result of the commission's grant of a permit was frivolous, because the testimony and report of the landowners' own expert witness amply supported that finding.The court further found that the trial court did not depart from the remand order because the remand order of the court was not so limited as to have precluded other methods of resolving the issue. The court further rejected efforts to construe remand orders so narrowly as to prohibit a trial court from considering matters relevant to the issues that were not envisioned at the time of the remand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the landowners' appeal against the commission regarding the commission's approval of only part of the landowners' application to expand their mining activities.

Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Carpenter v. Warden, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2662 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 7, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Quinn, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which set aside the trial court's decision and remanded the case with direction to render a judgment of guilty of manslaughter in the first degree and to sentence the defendant in accordance with that conviction; on remand, the court, Quinn, J., rendered judgment of guilty of manslaughter in the first degree and sentenced the defendant accordingly, and the defendant appealed to this court.

State v. Carpenter, 214 Conn. 77, 570 A.2d 203, 1990 Conn. LEXIS 57 (1990)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which , on remand after his conviction for murder was vacated, sentenced him to 20 years imprisonment for manslaughter in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder for causing the death of a toddler by throwing her forcefully into a bathtub and sentenced to 50 years imprisonment. The court affirmed, holding that defendant's sentence on remand was not more severe than the one imposed for his murder conviction. The court held that in order to determine whether a sentence was more severe, it was necessary to examine the overall impact on defendant. The court found that defendant failed to provide any authority to support the validity of his proportionality claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence for the offense of manslaughter in the first degree.

Ralto Developers, Inc. v. Environmental Impact Com.


No. 14155


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


220 Conn. 54; 594 A.2d 981; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 383


May 31, 1991, Argued  
August 6, 1991, Decided  
August 6, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the named defendant's denial of two applications by the plaintiff for wetlands permits to conduct regulated activities on certain of its real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the Tarrywile Neighbors for Sensible Development Association was permitted to intervene as a party defendant in each appeal and where the court, West, J., granted its motion to consolidate the appeals; thereafter, the court, Moraghan, J., denied the plaintiff's motion for judgment in accordance with a stipulation for judgment filed by the plaintiff and the named defendant et al.; subsequently, on reargument, the court, Karazin, J., granted the motion for judgment in accordance with the stipulation and rendered judgment approving the stipulation for judgment in the first appeal and approving the withdrawal of the second appeal, from which the defendant Tarrywile Neighbors for Sensible Development Association filed a consolidated appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervening defendant, an citizen's association, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff developer's motion for a judgment in accordance with a stipulation for judgment filed by the developer and named defendant, a city environmental impact commission. The association contended Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-43(c) did not authorized stipulation approval.


OVERVIEW: The intervening association sought review of the trial court's judgment approving the stipulation agreement which had been filed by the named parties, the developer and the commission, without the consent of the association. The association asserted that the trial court thus violated § 22a-43(c) in approving the proposed settlement of the dispute arising from the commission's denial of the developer's applications for wetlands permits for use of specific properties. The court on appeal reversed the judgment of the trial court based on its determination that § 22a-43(c) did not permit the commission's approval of the proposed settlement without the consent of all of the parties to the pending appeal, including the association as an intervening defendant, because the settlement agreement modified the decision of the commission as an inland wetlands agency. The court noted that the legislative intent was clear that a settlement agreement between all parties was a condition precedent for approval of any settlement involving withdrawal of an appeal to the commission and the court's failure to recognize that requirement was plain error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which entered a conviction for murder.


OVERVIEW: While in an apartment with several people, defendant shot and killed the victim after an argument and also shot a witness who attempted to defuse the argument. One witness identified another man as the shooter from a photographic array, while the witness who had been shot did not identify anyone from the photographic array. At the probable cause hearing and at trial, both witnesses identified defendant as the assailant. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court improperly allowed the admission of an in court identification of defendant after an unnecessarily suggestive pretrial identification procedure had been conducted. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that having defendant seated at the defense table in open court was inherently suggestive, but not unnecessarily suggestive, because defendant had no constitutional right to a lineup. The court also held that the trial court properly instructed the jury on the issue of identification because the instructions given included the material portions of both the model Telfaire charge and defendant's request and, as such, provided sufficient guidance to the jury on the issue of eyewitness identification.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Tweedy


No. 14103


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


219 Conn. 489; 594 A.2d 906; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 341


March 26, 1991, Argued  
July 16, 1991, Decided  
July 16, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree, two counts of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, and one count each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and burglary in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Cretella, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted defendant of two counts of robbery in the first degree, one count of kidnapping in the first degree pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A), one count of kidnapping in the first degree pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(B), and one count of burglary in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was additionally convicted of one count of sexual assault in the first degree. The court noted that the jury could have reasonably found that defendant followed the victim into her apartment building and forced his way into her apartment. Defendant demanded valuables and claimed to have a gun. He also engaged in nonconsensual sexual intercourse with the victim. Defendant forced the victim to go to her ATM and withdraw money for defendant. Defendant argued, in part, that he was punished twice for the offense of first-degree kidnapping and for the first-degree robbery violation and that the trial court deprived him of a fair trial because he was shackled during trial. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) the charged crimes of kidnapping in the first degree under § 53a-92(a)(2)(A), (B) were separate offenses for double jeopardy purposes; (2) where the State charged defendant with the robbery at her apartment and at the ATM, they were two separate and distinct robberies and the trial court was authorized to punish defendant separately for each offense; and (3) the precautionary measures taken by the trial court minimized the potential prejudicial effect of the shackles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of one count of sexual assault in the first degree, two counts of robbery in the first degree, one count of burglary in the third degree, one count of kidnapping in the first degree, and another count of kidnapping in the first degree.

Gil v. Inland Wetlands & Watercourses Agency


No. 14144


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


219 Conn. 404; 593 A.2d 1368; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 331


April 30, 1991, Argued  
July 9, 1991, Decided  
July 9, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a building permit for certain of the plaintiff's real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Fuller, J.; judgment for the plaintiff determining that the named defendant's action constituted a taking of the plaintiff's property, from which the named defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Lavery and Cretella, Js., which affirmed the trial court's decision, and the named defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Agency of the Town of Greenwich appealed a judgment from the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed a judgment by the trial court in favor of plaintiff landowner on the landowner's takings claim in the landowner's appeal of the Agency's denial of the landowner's application for a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The Agency denied the landowner's fourth application for a building permit after denying three previous applications on the merits. The landowner appealed to the trial court, which determined that the Agency's action constituted a taking of the landowner's property. The intermediate appellate court affirmed. The Agency appealed, contending that testimony from the landowner's own appraiser demonstrated the speculative nature of the landowner's purchase and that a claim of diminution of value should have been appraised by the injury to or loss of value of the property in its natural state. On appeal, the court held that the landowner failed to show that the Agency would not have allowed any reasonable residential development of the property and, therefore, a decision on the merits of the landowner's takings claim was premature. Although the landowner submitted four applications, only three were actually reviewed on their merits. The court could not have said the Agency would have rejected a more modest proposal if one had been offered by the landowner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court, which had affirmed the trial court's judgment for the landowner, and remanded to the intermediate appellate court with direction to remand the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment for the Agency on the landowner's takings claim.

Statewide Grievance Committee v. Rozbicki


No. 14101


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


219 Conn. 473; 595 A.2d 819; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 333


March 21, 1991, Argued  
July 9, 1991, Decided  
July 9, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Presentment in three counts by the plaintiff for alleged professional misconduct by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the court, Moraghan, J., rendered judgment granting the defendant's motion to dismiss the entire presentment, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendant cross appealed; this court vacated the trial court's decision, remanded the case for further proceedings and dismissed the cross appeal; on remand, the case was transferred to the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, where the court, Dorsey, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiff's motion to open the judgment and, after a trial to the court, rendered judgment suspending the defendant from the practice of law for three months; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion to open the judgment and to reargue, and the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review from a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain (Connecticut), which suspended the attorney from the practice of law for three months in the appellee grievance committee's action for misconduct against the attorney.


OVERVIEW: The attorney had a social relationship with his client and at one point represented her in an appeal from her dissolution action against her husband. The attorney failed to give the complainant his bill but accepted a quitclaim deed to 30 acres for payment. The trial court concluded that by failing to disclose fully the costs of his representation and by failing to make an unequivocal effort to ensure that the complainant obtained independent counsel, the attorney was guilty of professional misconduct. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the lower court holding that the attorney was suspended from the practice of law for three months. The court rejected the attorney's claim that the presentment should have been dismissed for failure to comply with Comm. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 31(a). The court noted that § 31(a) contained no penalty for noncompliance and purported only to establish a time limit for acting upon complaints. The court rejected defendant's claim that his due process rights were violated. The court found that the presentment apprised defendant of the transactions that were the basis of the grievance committee's allegations of misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court holding that the attorney was properly suspended from the practice of law for three months.

State v. Smith


No. 13867


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


219 Conn. 160; 592 A.2d 382; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 286


April 23, 1991, Argued  
June 11, 1991, Decided  
June 11, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Smith, 26 Conn. App. 279, 600 A.2d 1036, 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 437 (1991)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Smith v. Warden, 1997 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1879 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 14, 1997)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Smith v. Commissioner of Correction, 51 Conn. App. 905, 727 A.2d 821, 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 44 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Smith v. Warden, State Prison, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2135 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, criminal attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree, robbery in the second degree, larceny in the second degree and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; the court dismissed the charge of robbery in the second degree and substituted a charge of robbery in the third degree; verdict and judgment of guilty of kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the third degree, larceny in the second degree and assault in the third degree; thereafter, the court filed a corrected judgment regarding sentencing, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for kidnapping, robbery, larceny, and assault entered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: Defendant grabbed the victim, dragged her into the bathroom, and hit her while unbuckling her belt to "get naked." The victim offered defendant her watch and earrings, which he accepted. He left to find the victim's knapsack and never returned. Defendant was charged with kidnapping, robbery, larceny, and assault. On direct examination, defendant admitted that he falsely stated an alibi to a detective. Defendant was convicted, and he appealed. The court held that where defendant failed to preserve error, there was nothing to review, even where defendant alleged unpreserved constitutional claims. Thus, it was impossible for the court to determine whether defendant's constitutional rights had been impaired, and his claims failed. Defendant's challenge to the trial court's instruction on consciousness of guilt was properly viewed as evidentiary rather than constitutional because the instruction identified a permissive inference, which could be drawn from defendant's false statement. Finally, the trial court's two-inference instruction did not impermissibly dilute the State's burden of proof or the presumption of innocence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

249 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Sanzone v. Board of Police Comm'rs


No. 14102


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


219 Conn. 179; 592 A.2d 912; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 288


March 22, 1991, Argued  
June 11, 1991, Decided  
June 11, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the named plaintiff's wife as a result of a motor vehicle accident and for loss of consortium sustained by the named plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Ballen, J., granted the defendants' motion to strike the complaint; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiffs' motion for judgment and rendered judgment striking the complaint, and the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, driver and spouse, filed suit against defendants, city, board, members, superintendent, and officer (collectively board), for personal injuries the driver sustained after colliding with another driver due to a malfunctioning traffic light, and for the spouse's loss of consortium. The driver and spouse challenged the judgment of the Fairfield Superior Court (Connecticut), which granted the board's motion to strike the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The court had to determine the meaning and scope of a proviso contained within Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n, § 13 of the Tort Reform Act of 1986, No. 86-338 of the 1986 Public Acts, which addressed the liabilities and immunities of political subdivisions, their employees, officers, and agents, because the meaning of § 52-557n was not plain. The court construed § 52-557n to provide that an action under the highway defect statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149, was a plaintiff's exclusive remedy against a municipality or other political subdivision for damages resulting from injury to any person or property by means of a defective road or bridge. It also, therefore, precluded a joint action seeking such damages against a municipality and its officer pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-465 (a). On balance, § 13a-149 afforded a constitutionally adequate right to redress for injuries arising out of highway defects. Section 52-557n, by implicitly barring claims for loss of consortium based on highway defects, did not restrict the right to redress for an actionable injury but, rather, redefined the injury or the class of persons injured to which the constitutional right of redress attached.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

Bombero v. Planning & Zoning Com.


No. 14180


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


218 Conn. 737; 591 A.2d 390; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 252


February 14, 1991, Argued  
May 21, 1991, Decided  
May 21, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant amending a certain subdivision regulation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Dean, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a town planning and zoning commission, sought review of a decision from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which sustained an appeal by plaintiff individual and others from a decision by the commission amending a certain subdivision regulation.


OVERVIEW: The commission appealed from the judgment of the trial court that an amendment to the subdivision regulations of the town was unconstitutionally vague and arbitrary. The individuals had appealed to the trial court from the action of the commission in enacting the amendment. On appeal, the commission claimed that the trial court improperly concluded that: (1) the individuals were aggrieved by the enactment of the amendment; and (2) the amendment was unconstitutionally vague and was arbitrary. The court reversed the trial court, holding that the trial court should not have considered the validity of the subdivision regulation in the context of the individuals' zoning appeal. The court concluded that the appropriate procedural vehicle for the individuals' attack on the regulation was a declaratory judgment action, and not an appeal from its enactment. The court held that because the individuals' claims constituted a general attack on the validity of the regulation, it should have been presented by way of a declaratory judgment action in which other property owners who might have had an interest would have had the opportunity to intervene and be heard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to dismiss the individuals' appeal.

Connecticut Light & Power Co. v. Department of Public Utility Control


No. 14045


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


219 Conn. 51; 591 A.2d 1231; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 265


January 16, 1991, Argued  
May 21, 1991, Decided  
May 21, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant denying the plaintiff's application for approval of amended gas and electric rate schedules, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and tried to the court, Freed, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) affirmed defendant Department of Public Utility Control's (DPUC) denial of plaintiff utility company's application of approval for amended gas and electric rate schedules. The utility company appealed.


OVERVIEW: To settle an audit of excess construction costs of the utility company's nuclear power plant, Millstone III, the utility company and DPUC entered into a settlement agreement that limited recognition of Millstone III costs for retail ratemaking to $ 3.4 billion. The utility company's wholesale power sales rate schedules were determined by the Federal Energy Regulatory Commission, which had allowed an additional $ 400 million in Millstone III costs in establishing wholesale sales rates. The utility company alleged that the additional $ 400 million was "nonutility property," that the revenue attributable to wholesale sales should be excluded from utility company's rate base, and that 10 percent of the wholesale sales should be allocated to shareholders. The utility company challenged the DPUC's refusal to include utility company's electric deferred fuel balance (DFB) in the rate base. The court held there was substantial evidence to support DPUC's decision. Millstone III was a single unit, and no part of it was "nonutility" property. The settlement agreement as to includable costs for Millstone III was controlling. The electric DFB was recovered by a 10-year amortization.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision affirming DPUC's order denying the utility company's application for approval of amended gas and electric rate schedules.

State v. Payne


No. 13998


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


219 Conn. 93; 591 A.2d 1246; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 269


February 19, 1991, Argued  
May 21, 1991, Decided  
May 21, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the third degree with a firearm, robbery in the first degree, larceny in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before O'Keefe, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of burglary in the third degree with a firearm in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103a(a), robbery in the first degree in violation of § 53a-134(a)(4), larceny in the first degree in violation of § 53a-122(a)(2), and kidnapping in the first degree in violation of § 53a-92(a)(2)(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the victim's house at night and took her belongings while threatening her with a knife. Defendant appealed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(b)(3), claiming that the trial court improperly allowed the state to introduce evidence of defendant's commission of a subsequent crime in order to prove identity, allowed one of the victims to testify as to her pretrial identification of defendant while he was being arraigned on unrelated charges, prohibited defendant from cross-examining a witness, excluded the testimony of a witness as to incriminating statements made to her by defendant's brother, and excluded evidence that a third party committed the crimes charged. The court concluded that the trial court improperly allowed evidence of defendant's commission of a subsequent crime in order to prove identification and that that improper admission constituted harmful error. The court held that, under the totality of the circumstances even if the court considered all the common features together, the pattern that emerged was not such a distinctive combination of circumstances and actions that a "signature" or "criminal logo" could be discerned.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant for burglary, robbery, larceny and kidnapping and remanded the case for a new trial.

Connecticut Bldg. Wrecking Co. v. Carothers


No. 14181


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


218 Conn. 580; 590 A.2d 447; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 232; 33 ERC (BNA) 1759


February 15, 1991, Argued  
May 7, 1991, Decided  
May 7, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant finding that the plaintiffs had built and operated an unpermitted solid waste disposal facility and ordering that certain remedial measures be taken, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Mulcahy, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, who included a builder, appealed a decision of the Superior Court at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed plaintiffs' appeal of a decision by defendant Commissioner of Environmental Protection (DEP). The DEP had found that plaintiffs had built and operated an unpermitted solid waste disposal facility, and plaintiffs challenged the constitutionality of the relevant statute and the adequacy of the superior court's review.


OVERVIEW: The DEP charged plaintiffs with depositing waste at an unpermitted solid waste dump, and ordered plaintiffs to cease operations and to remove all solid waste besides "clean fill" from the site. A DEP hearing officer affirmed the order and the superior court affirmed that decision. Plaintiffs appealed, claiming: (1) insufficiency of the evidence, (2) the superior court should have reviewed the DEP enforcement order, and (3) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-207(4) and (6) (Rev. 1985) was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the superior court in part and reversed it in part. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-207(6) could be reasonably construed as being limited to contiguous property that was intended to be a single dumpsite and that the statute was therefore not impossible to obey. The court also noted that had the builder been confused by the statute, it could have sought clarification from the DEP. The builder had shown neither inadequate notice of what was prohibited nor arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. The court held, however, that by affirming the DEP's decision without evaluating the cleanup order, the superior court failed to comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183(j).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court on the issue of liability and found the relevant statute to be constitutional, but the court reversed the judgment on the refusal to review the DEP remedial orders. The court remanded the matter for proceedings consistent with its opinion. The court directed the superior court to vacate the DEP orders and remand the matter to the DEP if it found the orders to be an abuse of agency discretion.

State v. Castonguay


Nos. 13498, 13515


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


218 Conn. 486; 590 A.2d 901; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 235


February 19, 1991, Argued  
May 7, 1991, Decided  
May 7, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Summary judgment granted by, Judgment entered by Castonguay v. Warden, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3004 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crimes of capital felony and felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the state's motion to impanel a jury for a hearing on the imposition of the death penalty and rendered judgment of guilty, and the defendant appealed to this court; subsequently, the court granted the defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence and vacated the sentence imposed on the felony murder conviction, and the state, previously having received permission from the trial court, appealed to this court.
State v. Castonguay, 194 Conn. 416, 481 A.2d 56, 1984 Conn. LEXIS 687 (1984)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, after a jury trial, from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), for capital felony and his prison sentence for 25 years to life after the trial court vacated a felony murder conviction and another prison sentence for 25 years to life. The state appealed the vacation of the prison sentence.


OVERVIEW: A policeman was shot to death during a burglary. After the trial court vacated the felony murder conviction and its prison sentence to 25 years to life, defendant appealed the capital felony conviction and its prison sentence to 25 years to life. The court affirmed. The trial court properly vacated the felony murder conviction. There was no impropriety in admitting defendant's prior testimony. A jury charge equated defendant's transcript testimony with in-court testimony and instructed the jury to consider the prior testimony for the truth of the matters asserted. The charge was correct. The trial court correctly charged the jury on the State's burden of proof beyond a reasonable doubt, on the presumption of innocence, and that the jury could not draw an unfavorable inference from defendant's failure to testify. There was no reasonable possibility that the charge misled the jury. The trial court allowed defendant ample cross-examination designed to impeach of the State's primary witness, which was sufficient to satisfy defendant's constitutional right to confrontation under the Sixth Amendment. Testimony about the policeman's medical treatment was irrelevant, but was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which vacated defendant's conviction for felony murder and the vacation of one of the two prison sentences of 25 to life.

State v. Ireland


No. 13900


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


218 Conn. 447; 590 A.2d 106; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 124


February 19, 1991, Argued  
April 30, 1991, Decided  
April 30, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Benefield, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 238 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, sexual assault in the first degree and burglary in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Gormley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a his conviction before the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) for one count of felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, one count of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of § 53a-70(a), and one count of burglary in the third degree in violation of § 53a-103(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly restricted his cross-examination of the State's primary witnesses, in violation of his rights under the Fifth, Sixth, and Fourteenth Amendments. Finding that the questions on cross-examination exceeded the scope of the permitted direct examination, the court held that the trial court committed no abuse of discretion in limiting the cross-examination. Defendant's theory of the case was that the witnesses lied to protect one of the witness's brother. Defendant's counsel attempted to question one of the witnesses about a conversation between the brother and another accused. The court held that cross-examination was restricted to matters covered in the direct examination, except as they involve credibility alone. A review of the transcript revealed that the subject matter of the questions on cross-examination exceeded the scope of the direct examination. The trial court had discretion to determine the relevancy and the remoteness of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

259 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Couture


No. 13725


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


218 Conn. 309; 589 A.2d 343; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 110


December 12, 1990, Argued  
April 16, 1991, Decided  
April 16, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Amended indictment charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Heiman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Connecticut v. Couture, 469 U.S. 1192, 105 S. Ct. 967, 83 L. Ed. 2d 971, 1985 U.S. LEXIS 728 (1985)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him, following a jury trial, of three counts of felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of three counts of felony murder and sentenced to three consecutive terms of imprisonment, defendant appealed from his judgment of conviction. The court affirmed. Defendant alleged that he was denied a fair cross section of jurors because the trial court conducted the voir dire process on the first day of the Jewish holiday of Passover. However, the court found no merit in this claim because "observant" Jews were not a distinct and cognizable group within the community. A group was considered "cognizable" only upon a showing that the group had a definite composition, and the membership would not vary from day to day. Second, the court found no merit in defendant's assertion that he was denied the intelligent exercise of his peremptory challenges. A jury was presumed to follow the court's instructions. If a juror had served on a prior jury that voted to convict, that was not prejudice to defendant's case. Finally, defendant was not denied proper cross-examination. The trial court had properly declined to grant defendant latitude in cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court convicting defendant of three counts of felony murder.

Wright v. Woodridge Lake Sewer Dist.


No. 14004


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


218 Conn. 144; 588 A.2d 176; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 81


January 15, 1991, Argued  
March 26, 1991, Decided  
March 26, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine, inter alia, the validity of a certain sewer ordinance, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the court, Pickett, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs declaring the ordinance invalid, from which the defendants appealed and the plaintiffs cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners brought an action seeking a declaratory judgment to determine the validity of the Woodridge Lake Sewer District Sewer Ordinance, and for other relief. Defendant sewer district appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut) entered in favor of the landowners, which declared the ordinance invalid. The landowners cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district claimed that the trial court erred by declaring the sewer ordinance invalid without hearing its proffered evidence. The court agreed with the district and reversed and remanded. The court found that the trial court should not have come to its conclusion that the ordinance was invalid without hearing the factual evidence offered by the district in support of the ordinance's validity. At trial, in support of its claim, the district sought to present expert testimony that the purpose of the amended sewer ordinance was to ensure fair availability of the sewer system to all properties and that the restrictions in the amended sewer ordinance appropriately reflected the design, functioning, capacity, and operation of the sewer district treatment plant and sewer system. The court determined that that evidence was relevant to the issue of whether the ordinance, as amended, was rationally related to the operation and maintenance of a sewerage system and, thus, a legitimate exercise of the police power. The court concluded, therefore, that the trial court should not have adjudicated the validity of the ordinance without first considering the evidence offered by the district.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Kane


No. 13836


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


218 Conn. 151; 588 A.2d 179; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 82


December 12, 1990, Argued  
March 26, 1991, Decided  
March 26, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Kane v. Warden, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1092 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 13, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, robbery in the first degree, larceny in the first degree and conspiracy to commit larceny in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the jury before Curran, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Ansonia-Milford District (Connecticut), convicting him of felony murder, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, robbery in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(2), larceny in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-122(a)(2), and conspiracy to commit larceny, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-122(a)(2) and 53a-48(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony murder, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, robbery in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(2), larceny in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-122(a)(2), and conspiracy to commit larceny, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-122(a)(2) and 53a-48(a). Defendant appealed, arguing that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-46a, was unconstitutional and deprived him of due process of law because the statute precluded a motion to suppress at his probable cause hearing and consequently deprived him of the opportunity to suppress his allegedly involuntary statements to the police at that stage of the proceedings. The court ruled that a party who challenged a statute on constitutional grounds had no easy burden, for every intendment was made in favor of constitutionality, and invalidity was required to be established beyond a reasonable doubt. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant, concluding that a damaging confession which could later be suppressed at the trial level on the ground that it was involuntary and illegally obtained by the police could be admitted at a preliminary hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was affirmed.

 

262 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Bartholomew v. Schweizer


No. 13921


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


217 Conn. 671; 587 A.2d 1014; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 72


January 17, 1991, Argued  
March 12, 1991, Decided  
March 12, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in a motor vehicle accident allegedly caused by the named defendant's negligence, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Gormley, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment as to liability; thereafter, the action was tried to the jury on the issue of damages before Berdon, J.; verdict for the plaintiff; subsequently, the court, Berdon, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for judgment and rendered judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment as to liability for personal injuries and rendered a judgment for plaintiff on the issue of damages.


OVERVIEW: During closing arguments in the damages portion of the trial plaintiff's attorney suggested to the jury an appropriate amount of damages. Such argument was permitted by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-216b. Defendant contended the statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment for plaintiff on the issue of damages and liability. The statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine by impeding within the exclusive control of the judiciary. Although trial courts had broad discretion to control oral arguments, there was never a rule that stated that the court's authority was exclusive of concurrent legislative jurisdiction. The history of the statute undermined defendant's claim that the legislature intended to abrogate the power of the court to discipline attorneys or to control their statements during oral argument. The statute's incorporation of a provision for curative instructions when attorneys mention damages meant the statute did not violate defendant's right to a trial by jury. The trial court did not err by instructing the jury that it could consider plaintiff's alleged inability to participate in karate activities in regard to both past and future damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for plaintiff as to liability and the judgment for plaintiff as to damages. Statute that allowed plaintiff's attorney to argue to the jury for an appropriate amount of damages did not violate the separation of powers doctrine or the right to trial by jury. The judiciary's broad discretion to control oral argument was not exclusive of concurrent legislative jurisdiction.

Port Clinton Assoc. v. Board of Selectmen


No. 14115


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


217 Conn. 588; 587 A.2d 126; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 60

February 26, 1991, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for, inter alia, a determination of the validity of a certain zoning ordinance enacted by the town of Clinton, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Burns, J., suo motu, rendered judgment dismissing the complaint, from which the plaintiffs appealed.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs dock owner and manager challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut), which entered an order dismissing dock owner and manager's claim that the decision of defendant, city's board of selectmen, denying them permission to expand their docks constituted an illegal taking in violation of U.S. Const. amends. XIV and V and violated 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Dock owner and manager applied to the U. S. Army Corps of Engineers (Army Corps) and to the Connecticut Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) for permission to extend two of the marina's piers by approximately two hundred fifty feet. The court determined that dock owner and manager had the burden of showing but failed to show that the board had arrived at a definitive position on the issue that had inflicted an actual, concrete injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Spero v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff restaurant owner appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which confirmed a decision by defendant town zoning board of appeals, in a zoning law dispute, denying the owner's permit application for an outside ordering station under Guilford, Conn., Zoning Reg. art. II, § 23, tbl. 2b, item 28(a).

State v. Leary


No. 14051


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


217 Conn. 404; 587 A.2d 85; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 31


October 30, 1990, Argued  
February 12, 1991, Decided  
February 12, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from, inter alia, selling admission tickets to entertainment events in violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven at Meriden, where the court, Damiani, J., granted the plaintiff's action for summary judgment and denied the defendants' motion for summary judgment as to liability; after a hearing in damages, the court rendered judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant ticket sellers appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted summary judgment, injunctive relief, restitution, and a civil penalty to plaintiff State of Connecticut, ruling that the ticket sellers violated the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq. by selling tickets to entertainment events in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-289.


OVERVIEW: The State brought an action to enjoin the ticket sellers from charging more than three dollars over face value, for restitution, and for a civil penalty. The trial court granted summary judgment to the State. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-289, regulating ticket sales, did not violate equal protection or due process and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110b(a) was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The court ruled that allowing property owners holding events to sell tickets at higher prices did not violate equal protection because it was reasonably related to the statute's purpose to promote access, protect the public, and prevent economic loss. The court found that the ticket sellers' charges were not valid delivery charges, but were based on the quality of the ticket, the location and desirability of the seat, and the cost of procuring it. The court ruled that the action was properly filed, although no consumer complaints were received, because the consumer protection commission had a sufficient factual belief that the ticket sellers engaged in unfair methods of competition and unfair or deceptive practices under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110m.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment enjoining the ticket sellers from selling tickets for more that three dollars over their face value, ordering restitution, and imposing a civil penalty.

D & J Quarry Prods. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n

February 12, 1991, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in each case, from a decision by the defendant planning and zoning commission amending certain zoning regulations to provide restrictions and limitations on the excavation and processing of earth products, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the court, Fuller, J.; judgment sustaining, in part, the appeals, from which the defendants, on the granting of certification, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, defendant planning and zoning commission sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), which sustained, in part, the appeals of plaintiff sand and gravel companies from decisions by the commission amending certain zoning regulations.


OVERVIEW: The companies operated mining, excavation, and gravel processing facilities located in industrial and industrial park zones within the town. Both companies increasingly relied upon imported earth products from outside the town. The commission amended zoning regulations so as to prohibit the accessory processing of earth products excavated beyond town limits. Gen. Stat. § 8-2. The court held that by definition, accessory uses had to be located on the same lot, and had to be subordinate and customarily incidental to, the principal use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cases with direction to render judgment dismissing the companies' appeals.

SFA Folio Collections, Inc. v. Bannon


No. 14023

November 8, 1990, Argued  
January 22, 1991, Decided  
January 22, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the assessment of, inter alia, a sales and use tax liability against the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Satter, J.; judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant commissioner of revenue services appealed the decision entered in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which reversed the assessment of sales and use taxes imposed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-406 et seq. on plaintiff taxpayer's mail order business due to its finding that plaintiff's activities did not have a sufficient nexus to the state.


OVERVIEW: Defendant commissioner of revenue services informed plaintiff taxpayer that it was required to collect and remit sales and use taxes because it satisfied the definition of being engaged in business in the state pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-407(15). In determining whether any of the asserted contacts established some minimum connection between plaintiff and the state, the court found that defendant's claim ignored the fact that plaintiff's catalogs became the property of the residents, and that the use of a toll-free "800" number for Connecticut residents to place orders did not demonstrate a sufficient link to Connecticut. Defendant made no claim that plaintiff was incorporated or maintained for the purpose of evading sales and use taxes, and no such claim would be credible based upon the evidence presented at trial. Defendant's bald assertion that plaintiff purposely availed itself of the privilege of conducting activities in Connecticut, thus invoking the benefits and protection of its laws, fails to clarify how plaintiff was benefitted by local government when its contacts to Connecticut were solely through the United States mail and common carriers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with the crime of failing to assist a peace officer in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167b. The State appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which granted defendants' motions to dismiss.

Todd v. Glines


No. 14086


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


217 Conn. 1; 583 A.2d 1287; 1991 Conn. LEXIS 4


November 1, 1990, Argued  
January 1, 1991, Decided  
January 1, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in an automobile accident allegedly caused by the named defendant's negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the jury before Meadow, J.; verdict for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiff's motion to set aside the verdict and for a new trial and rendered judgment for the plaintiff; subsequently, the court granted the defendants' motion for remittitur and rendered a corrected judgment, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendants cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim appealed and defendant tortfeasor cross-appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), which entered judgment in favor of the victim in her action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in an automobile accident, but granted the tortfeasor's motion for remittitur and rendered a corrected judgment.


OVERVIEW: Two disputed issues in the case involved the liability for the accident and the causal relationship between the accident and the victim's claimed injuries. On review, the court affirmed. The court found that in formulating its verdict on liability and in determining damages, the jury was entitled to take into account the discrepancies in the testimony concerning the accident and the cause of the victim's hip injury. The court also found that merely because the victim asserted that she should have been awarded a larger sum for past and future noneconomic damages did not justify setting aside the verdict. The court determined that the legislature intended Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-225d(b)(3) to provide an award of fees even in the absence of a specific demand for them in the pleadings because the statute was mandatory and, therefore, no valid purpose was served by hinging its application to a pleading requirement. The court concluded that although the victim had not requested attorney's fees in her pleadings, she did make a general claim for "money damages" in her prayer for relief and that form of pleading was not fatal to such an award.


OUTCOME: The grant of the motion for remittitur and rendering of a corrected judgment in favor of the victim in an action to recover damages for injuries sustained in an accident was affirmed.

Wood v. Bridgeport


No. 14011


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


216 Conn. 604; 583 A.2d 124; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 420


October 5, 1990, Argued  
December 11, 1990, Decided  
December 11, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of the defendants' alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the action was withdrawn as against the named defendant, and tried to the jury before Jones, J.; verdict for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court denied the motions to set aside the verdict and for remittitur filed by the defendant Citytrust Company, and rendered judgment for the plaintiff in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant Citytrust Company appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowner appealed from the rulings of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which entered judgment on a jury verdict in favor of plaintiff pedestrian in an action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in a slip-and-fall on the landowner's sidewalk. The trial court allowed the pedestrian to reopen his evidence after the landowner made a motion for a directed verdict.


OVERVIEW: The trial court allowed the pedestrian to reopen the evidence to describe the location of the fall as within the landowner's property line. On appeal, the court held that the reopening of the evidence was within the sound discretion of the trial court and would not be disturbed unless there was an abuse of discretion or prejudice, such as when a party was allowed to prove on omitted but essential element of the case. The court examined the record and found that the pedestrian had actually proved the location of his fall in his original evidence although neither the trial court nor counsel had remembered it, so that the additional repetitive evidence was not essential for the pedestrian to establish a prima facie case. The court declined to review a claim that 1989 Conn. Acts 319, which permitted counsel to argue mathematical formulas for damages in closing arguments, was unconstitutional. The court held that the landowner had failed to present a record that preserved the issue for review. The court also declined to set aside a jury award as excessive because there was evidence of severe and permanent injuries that supported the award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the pedestrian against the landowner for damages in a slip-and-fall action.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, and substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree and attempted murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the informations were consolidated and tried to the jury before Purtill, J.; verdicts of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for acquittal of murder and granted the defendant's motion for acquittal of assault in the first degree; subsequently, the court rendered judgment of guilty of murder and judgment of guilty of attempted murder, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a), assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-59(a)(1), 53a-8, and attempted murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54a(a), 53a-49(a). The trial court later acquitted defendant of assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court should not have admitted into evidence police testimony describing an extrajudicial identification from a photographic array by the attempted murder victim, nor the transcript of the probable cause hearing at which the victim identified defendant in the courtroom. At trial, the State offered police testimony describing the victim's identification of defendant from a photographic array when it could not find the victim. The court held that the testimony should have been excluded as hearsay because it did not fall within any exception to the hearsay rule. As to the hearing transcript, the State contended that the victim's testimony was properly admitted under the former testimony exception to the hearsay rule, and was coupled with indicia of reliability adequate to satisfy the demands of the Confrontation Clause. The record indicated that the victim's testimony was given under oath, subject to criminal penalties for perjury before a tribunal that kept a judicial record. The trial court properly admitted the transcribed testimony of the victim's identification at the probable cause hearing at defendant's trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Lubus


No. 14013


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


216 Conn. 402; 581 A.2d 1045; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 383


September 25, 1990, Argued  
November 6, 1990, Decided  
November 6, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of escape in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Vertefeuille, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the case was presented to the court on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the trial court for escape under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-169(a)(2) (Rev. to 1989). The case was transferred from the Appellate Court of Connecticut to the court pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 4023.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was transferred to a community residence program after his felony conviction. The program permitted defendant to live in his own home. Relying on Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-100(d), the commissioner of correction promulgated a community residence agreement, which provided that defendant's failure to report to his supervising officer would constitute an escape under § 53a-169(a)(2). Defendant signed the agreement and was charged with escape for his single failure to report to his supervising officer. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss. On appeal from his conviction, the court reversed and remanded, holding that § 53a-169(a)(2) did not penalize as an "escape" a single failure to report to a supervisor and proof of such failure to report was insufficient to prove defendant guilty of an escape. The term "escape," under § 53a-169(a)(2), contemplated an unauthorized departure from, or failure to return to, a "community residence." Also, the commissioner's authority to promulgate rules of conduct for persons transferred to a "community residence" did not include the authority to define "escape" to include conduct that the legislature had not criminalized.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for escape. The case was remanded with direction to set aside defendant's conviction and for further proceedings.

Lizotte v. Conservation Com. of Somers


Nos. 13912, 13913


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT

June 1, 1990, Argued  
August 21, 1990, Decided  
August 21, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in the first case, from the named defendant's adoption of certain inland wetlands and watercourses regulations, and action, in the second case, for a declaratory judgment to determine the validity of a certain inland wetlands and watercourses regulation, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the defendant commissioner of environmental protection was defaulted for failure to appear in the first case; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, Jackaway, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal in the first case and judgment determining that the regulation was valid and denying other relief in the second case, from which the plaintiffs filed separate appeals.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed in the first case; affirmed in the second case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), that held in favor of defendant town commission that a regulation of the town that was challenged by the landowners did not go beyond the limits of the relevant enabling legislation, The Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-36 to 22a-45, and that it was a valid exercise of police power.


OVERVIEW: The regulation at issue established distances within which certain construction activities could not be conducted; the distances were from wetlands and watercourses. The landowners contended, inter alia, that the regulation imposed mandatory restrictions that were not necessary to preserve and protect inland wetlands and watercourses within the town. The Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Act (IWWA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-42(c), provided that a town could promulgate regulations necessary to protect the wetlands and watercourses within its territorial limits.Such regulation had to be in conformity with the regulations adopted pursuant to the IWWA, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-39. The court rejected the contention that the regulation was invalid because it was not in conformity with the statutory scheme set forth in the IWWA. The court thus rejected the assertion that the factors promulgated by the IWWA, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-41, had to be applied on a case-by-case basis and that the regulation, which made no provision for variations of its requirements through a permit process, was invalid because it conflicted with the procedures contemplated by the IWWA.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the town commission and against the landowners, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Lamme


No. 13792

216 Conn. 172; 579 A.2d 484; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 306


May 31, 1990, Argued  
August 7, 1990, Decided  
August 7, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and operating a motor vehicle with a suspended driver's license, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Geen, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., Stoughton and Norcott, Js., which affirmed the decision of the trial court, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed the trial court's judgments that convicted defendant of the operation of a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(a) and the operation of a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the operation of a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(a) and of the operation of a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215(a). Defendant sought review of the judgment, which the appellate court affirmed, and defendant sought further review. On appeal, defendant contended that Conn. Const. art. I, § 9 precluded the police from detaining him for limited investigative purposes without having probable cause to arrest. In affirming the convictions, the court held that the police made a valid Terry stop of defendant for driving without illuminated headlights in the dark of night and were justified in detaining him for sobriety tests when they smelled alcohol on his breath. The court ruled that the text, the history, and the policy embodied in Conn. Const. art. I, § 9 rebutted defendant's position that an investigatory detention without probable cause could not pass constitutional muster. The court held that defendant's brief detention did not violate his due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial and appellate courts convicting defendant of operation of a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and of the operation of a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension.
