Ford v. Blue Cross & Blue Shield, Inc.


No. 13667


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


216 Conn. 40; 578 A.2d 1054; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 269; 5 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 942; 117 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P56,473


April 5, 1990, Argued  
July 31, 1990, Decided  
July 31, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action by the plaintiff seeking reinstatement to her previous position with the defendant and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven at Meriden and tried to the jury before Clark, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed on appeal, new trial; cross appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a decision by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven at Meriden (Connecticut), which entered judgment following a jury verdict for appellee employer in an action by the employee seeking reinstatement to her previous position with the employer and for other relief.


OVERVIEW: The employee instituted this action pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-290a, claiming that the employer had terminated her employment because she had filed a claim for workers' compensation benefits. The case was tried before a jury that found in favor of the employee and awarded damages. The trial court rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict and additionally ordered that the employee be reinstated to her previous employment position. The dispositive issue in this appeal was whether the trial court properly instructed the jury concerning the allocation of burdens of proof in an action brought by an employee pursuant to § 31-290a, alleging wrongful termination of employment. On appeal the court concluded that the trial court improperly instructed the jury concerning the allocation of burdens of proof in an action brought pursuant to § 31-290a. The court held that the instructions were not presented to the jury in a way that clearly set forth the allocation of burdens of proof in the case. Accordingly, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which entered judgment following a jury verdict for the employer in an action by the employee seeking reinstatement to her previous position. The court held that that the jury instructions were not presented to the jury in a way that clearly set forth the allocation of burdens of proof.

 

278 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. State


No. 13744


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


216 Conn. 85; 579 A.2d 37; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 274


April 3, 1990, Argued  
July 31, 1990, Decided  
July 31, 1990, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to recover attorneys' fees and costs incurred by the plaintiffs in their successful action against the state to obtain authorization for Medicaid funding of certain abortion services, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Hodgson, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff class of indigent women (class) filed an action in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) against defendant state to recover attorneys' fees which they incurred in their successful suit to obtain authorization for Medicaid funding of abortion services. After a trial on the merits, the trial court awarded the class attorneys' fees in the amount of $ 134,505. The state appealed the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The state argued that the class was not entitled to attorneys' fees because the statute of limitations for the claim expired, and that Conn. Const. art. first, § 10 did not give the class a right to recover attorneys' fees. On appeal, the court held that the class timely filed its claim. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(a) required the class to file the claim within one year from the date its legal rights to the attorneys' fees accrued. The attorneys representing the class were obligated to carry out the trial court's order after the trial court entered the judgment, so the statute of limitations did not begin to run with the entry of the judgment. The court held that the state did not impede the class in their pursuit of constitutionally adequate "access" to the courts within the meaning of Conn. Const. art. first, § 10. The court also held that Conn. Const. art. first, § 10 did not give the class a right to attorneys' fees. Either the common law or a statute had to authorize their payment, and neither Congress nor the Connecticut legislature provided for the payment of the attorneys' fees to the class.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the class of indigent women and held that they were not entitled to recover the attorneys' fees. The court directed a judgment for the state.

 

279 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Payne v. Fairfield Hills Hosp.


No. 13875


Supreme Court of Connecticut


215 Conn. 675; 578 A.2d 1025; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 263


May 31, 1990, Argued  
July 24, 1990, Decided  
July 24, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant psychiatric security review board from exercising jurisdiction over the plaintiff, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the court, Curran, J.; judgment for the defendants denying the plaintiff injunctive relief, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate, who was acquitted of a charge of murder by reason of mental disease or defect, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), which denied the inmate's attempt to enjoin the psychiatric security review board (PSRB) from exercising jurisdiction over him. Defendants, a state hospital and other authorities, claimed the inmate failed to exhaust administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The court first addressed defendants' contention that the inmate was required to exhaust administrative remedies before instituting his action. The court agreed with the trial court that because an agency should not be called upon to determine whether the statute that created it was unconstitutional, there was no need for the inmate to have exhausted administrative remedies. The inmate contended that the statute creating the PSRB was a quasi-criminal statute that violated the ex post facto prohibition of U.S. Const., art. I, § 10. The court affirmed the trial court's holding that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-257b was not an ex post facto law. The court reasoned that the ex post facto prohibition applied to punishments and that the confinement of individuals with dangerous mental diseases or defects was not a punishment. Finally, the court rejected the inmate's claim that the act was improperly invoked to review the inmate's psychiatric status. The court pointed out that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-257f expressly authorized the PSRB to conduct periodic hearings to review acquittees' status at least every other year.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Cannata v. Department of Envtl. Protection


No. 13877


Supreme Court of Connecticut


215 Conn. 616; 577 A.2d 1017; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 260


May 10, 1990, Argued  
July 17, 1990, Decided  
July 17, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant enjoining the cutting of trees within the limits of a stream channel encroachment line on certain real property owned by the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the defendant Crele Construction Corporation et al. were defaulted for failure to appear, and tried to the court, Burns, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners brought an appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183 from a decision by defendant Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) requiring them to file an application for a permit to cut trees on their property within the stream channel encroachment lines. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut) dismissed for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners intended to cut trees within the stream channel encroachment lines in order to expand their agricultural crop land. The DEP issued a cease and desist order directing the property owners to stop cutting trees because they had failed to apply for a permit as provided in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-342. The property owners asserted that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-349 prohibited the DEP from applying Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-342 and subjecting them to the permit process. The court found that: 1) the DEP's jurisdictional authority to require the property owners to obtain permits was limited to the placement of obstructions or encroachments within the lines; 2) whether the property owners' proposed activity within the stream channel encroachment lines was an obstruction or encroachment and whether the proposed use of their land was an agricultural or farming use within Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-349 were factual determinations best left to the DEP; 3) by requiring the property owners to submit to the permit process under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-342, the DEP could make that decision; 4) the appeal to a superior court was not warranted until denial of the permit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal.

 

281 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Caldor, Inc. v. Heslin


No. 13754


Supreme Court of Connecticut


215 Conn. 590; 577 A.2d 1009; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 223


April 12, 1990, Argued  
July 10, 1990, Decided  
July 10, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the enforcement by the named defendant of a certain state regulation concerning the advertisement of prices of merchandise when manufacturers' rebates are involved, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and tried to the court, Fracasse, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant merchant sought review of the decision by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) rendering judgment for appellee Commissioner of Consumer Protection in action brought by appellant to stay enforcement of Conn. Agencies Reg. § 42-110b-19(e). Appellant argued that promulgation of Reg. § 42-110b-19(e), regulating rebate offers, exceeded appellee's authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110b(b, c).


OVERVIEW: Appellant merchant challenged the trial court's decision rendering judgment in favor of appellee Commissioner of Consumer Protection in appellant's action to enjoin enforcement of Conn. Agencies Reg. § 42-110b-19(e). The court held that appellee's promulgation of Reg. § 42-110b-19(e), preventing merchants offering a manufacturer's rebate from displaying the net price of an item unless the rebate was available to the customer at the time of purchase, did not exceed appellee's authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110b(b, c). Reg. § 42-110b-19(e) was not inconsistent with the rules of Federal Trade Commission--intended as guidance under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110b(b)--because the federal authorities had not adopted regulations inconsistent with the regulation. In addition, Reg. § 42-110b-19(e) had received approval from the legislative review committee as required under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-170. The court held that the regulation did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I or Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 4, 5. Appellee's investigation yielded a finding that net price advertising which included a manufacturer's rebate was inherently misleading. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the promulgation of the administrative regulation, governing the advertisement of a list prices associated with a manufacturers' rebate offer, did not exceed the appellee Commission of Consumer Protection's statutory authority. Because appellee determined the advertising was inherently misleading, the regulation did not violate federal or state constitutional protection of commercial speech.

Monroe v. Horwitch


No. 13831


Supreme Court of Connecticut


215 Conn. 469; 576 A.2d 1280; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 220


April 11, 1990, Argued  
June 26, 1990, Decided  
June 26, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Presentment by the plaintiff for alleged professional misconduct by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Vasington, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court for the judicial district of New London (Connecticut), which granted the motion to dismiss of defendant, the statewide bar counsel, in plaintiff's action alleging the defendant should be disciplined for professional misconduct.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that the statewide bar counsel had failed to enforce time limits for processing grievance complaints and had unconstitutionally acted as a judge. The statewide bar counsel argued that plaintiff lacked standing to bring the action. The superior court dismissed plaintiff's action. The court affirmed. Plaintiff could not directly request the court to discipline an attorney. She lacked standing because, as a member of the general public, she did not demonstrate how she was harmed in a unique fashion by the functioning of the statewide grievance process and did not establish a colorable claim of direct injury. Plaintiff was required to follow the grievance procedure set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-90e, which required complaints concerning the professional conduct of attorneys to be filed with the statewide bar counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the statewide bar counsel.

Concerned Citizens of Sterling, Inc. v. Connecticut Siting Council


No. 13920


Supreme Court of Connecticut


215 Conn. 474; 576 A.2d 510; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 218; 21 ELR 20039


May 4, 1990, Argued  
June 26, 1990, Decided  
June 26, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant granting a certificate of environmental compatibility and public need to the defendant Exeter Energy Limited Partnership for the construction of an electricity generating facility, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Mullarkey, J.; judgment for the defendants dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens group and individuals appealed a decision from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed its challenge to the procedures used by defendant Connecticut Siting Council to grant a certificate of environmental compatibility and public need to defendant energy company.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs maintained the proceedings before the council were fatally flawed in three respects: (1) noncompliance with the statutory notice of hearing requirements prescribed by Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 16-50l, 16-50m and 4-177; (2) violation of their constitutional rights to procedural due process; and (3) improper reliance by the council on expert findings not subjected to challenge by cross-examination. In affirming the decision, the court held that Rhode Island plaintiffs were not entitled to public notice under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-501(b). The court found no violation of the citizens due process rights. The notice they received enabled the citizens to participate in the hearings held by the council. The council did not abuse its discretion in denying a continuance. The citizens were not deprived of the opportunity to cross-examine the authors of the exhibit which was proffered and received as commentary on the citizens' own belated report. The citizens failed to prove that the council departed from its legal charge of treating the exhibit as mere argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision because it found no violation of the citizens' rights when the council made its decision.

Wheway v. Warden, State Prison


Nos. 13623, 13624


Supreme Court of Connecticut


215 Conn. 418; 576 A.2d 494; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 208


April 12, 1990, Argued  
June 19, 1990, Decided  
June 19, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition, in the first case, for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Axelrod, J.; judgment granting, in part, the petition, from which, on the granting of certification, the respondent appealed and the petitioner cross appealed.

Petition, in the second case, for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Santos, J.; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed.

The petitioners filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Reversed on the appeal, judgment directed; affirmed on the cross appeal. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners one and two, both out-of-state parolees, appealed the denial in part and in full respectively, by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), of their requests for writs of habeas corpus challenging pending parole violation detainers lodged against them by the states from which they were transferred. The State appealed the grant in part of petitioner one's request for habeas relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed the right to an immediate parole revocation hearing on the Mississippi parole violation detainer because his liberty interests in his confinement would otherwise be violated. The habeas court granted the petition in part. Petitioner two alleged that he had the right to an immediate parole revocation hearing either in Connecticut or Ohio. The habeas court denied his petition. The two appeals were consolidated. As to petitioner one, the court reversed as to the issues on the appeal, remanded to the trial court with direction to deny the petition and affirmed as to the issues on the cross appeal. As to petitioner two, the court affirmed. The court held that petitioners were neither entitled to an immediate parole revocation hearing while incarcerated for subsequent Connecticut convictions nor entitled to serve the balance of any out-of-state prison terms in Connecticut. Because prison authorities had full discretion as to early release programs, petitioners were not entitled to invoke due process considerations. The trial court was without authority to quash, dismiss, strike, or issue an order as to an out-of-state parole violation warrant lodged as a detainer.


OUTCOME: The court, in the first case, reversed as to the issues on the appeal and remanded to the trial court with direction to deny the petition. It also affirmed as to the issues on the cross appeal. In the second case, the court affirmed denial of the habeas petition.

Circuit-Wise, Inc. v. Commissioner of Revenue Services

Supreme Court of Connecticut


215 Conn. 292; 576 A.2d 1259; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 194

June 12, 1990, Decided  
June 12, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the assessment of taxes on certain hazardous waste generated by the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and referred to Hon. Philip R. Pastore, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a taxpayer, sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Conn.), which referred the case to a state trial referee, who dismissed the taxpayer's appeal regarding the assessment of taxes on certain hazardous waste made by defendant, the Commissioner of Revenue Services.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner assessed taxes against the taxpayer pursuant to the Hazardous Waste Assessment statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-132. The Commissioner rejected the taxpayer's protest and the taxpayer appealed to the trial court. At the trial court level, a state trial referee entered judgment for the Commissioner. In affirming the trial court's order on appeal, the court concluded that the assessment on the taxpayer's reclaimed wastes was reasonably related to the purpose of hazardous waste management in the state that there was no violation of the equal protection or due process clauses of either the federal or state constitutions. The court agreed with the trial court's finding that there was no difference between the hazardous waste that was dumped at a regulated landfill and the hazardous waste that was recycled or reclaimed. The court stated that the taxpayer failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that § 22a-132 violated the federal and state guarantees of equal protection. The court found that the application of § 22a-132 as applied to hazardous waste sent for recycling did not operate in an arbitrary or capricious manner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

State v. Jones


No. 13523


Supreme Court of Connecticut


215 Conn. 173; 575 A.2d 216; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 179


February 27, 1990, Argued  
May 29, 1990, Decided  
May 29, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before McKeever, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of kidnapping in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of kidnapping in the first degree, he appealed. On appeal the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that, while the State's use of defendant's post-Miranda refusal to sign his transcribed statement violated defendant's due process rights, the error was harmless in light of other evidence presented at trial. The State in its closing argument twice made reference to defendant's failure to sign his statement in an attempt to impeach that statement. The court found that defendant had clearly manifested his exercise of his right to remain silent. However, the court concluded that the record indicated that the State did not focus on or highlight defendant's invocation of his right to silence. The court noted that the State made only two references to defendant's failure to sign his statement and that those references were not the centerpiece of the State's case. Furthermore, because defendant failed to object to the State's references, the court determined that the failure to object or move for a mistrial indicated that defendant's counsel did not consider the State's comments to have substantially prejudiced defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Carothers v. Capozziello

John M. Alexander, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgments for the plaintiff in the first four cases, from which the named defendant et al. appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed, and judgment for the defendants in the fifth case, from which the plaintiff appealed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) entered judgment on behalf of plaintiff environmental protection commissioner (commissioner) in four cases against defendants, who were the principal owner and operator of a demolition businesses and the demolition businesses themselves (demolitionists), and in favor of the demolitionists in the fifth case. All parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner made findings that the demolitionists' activities gave rise to imminent and substantial damage to the environment or to the public health and issued two orders against the demolitionists to cease and desist from further disposal or transfer of solid waste to certain property and to correct established violations. OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments against the demolitionists in the first and third cases were affirmed. The trial court's judgments against the demolitionists in the second and fourth cases were reversed and remanded with direction to render judgments in favor of the demolitionists. The trial court's judgment against the commissioner in the fifth case was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney sought review of an order from the Superior Court for New Haven (Connecticut), which, upon allegations of professional misconduct brought by plaintiff grievance committee, determined that the attorney was guilty of the misconduct and suspended his license for one year.


OVERVIEW: The grievance committee alleged that the attorney had failed to account for and return funds to a client, had charged an unreasonable fee to a second client, had double charged and failed to make prompt payments to a third client, and had charged an excessive fee to a fourth client, all in violation of the state rules of professional conduct. The attorney denied the charges, but after a hearing, the trial court found the attorney guilty of misconduct and suspended his license for three months for each client, for a total of one year. The attorney sought review and argued that the grievance committee created an unconstitutionally court, that the attorney was denied due process, and that the trial court erred in applying a clear and convincing standard of proof. The court found that the grievance committee was authorized by the judiciary and properly acted as an arm of the court, that the attorney was entitled to and received notice of the charges against him, a fair hearing, a fair determination, and was afforded the right to appeal, and that the clear and convincing standard was the correct standard applicable to the attorney's case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's findings.

State v. Richardson


No. 13740


Supreme Court of Connecticut


214 Conn. 752; 574 A.2d 182; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 136

May 1, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of arson in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, and tried to the jury before Vasington, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) that, following the jury trial, convicted him of arson in the first degree. Defendant also challenged the denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of arson after his family's retail business was damaged by fire. On appeal, defendant asserted that some of the prosecutor's statements during closing argument had no foundation and deprived defendant of his right to a fair trial and an impartial jury. Specifically, defendant objected to the prosecutor's remark that the autodialer, when activated by a single breach of the security system's sensor beam in the retail business, repeatedly dialed defendant's contact number. Defendant contended, and the court agreed, that the prosecutor's conclusion was not established by the evidence. However, the court ruled that the comments were not so prejudicial as to deprive defendant of the opportunity for a fair trial and that the superior court did not abuse its discretion when it denied the request for a curative instruction. The court also held that the superior court did not abuse its discretion when it excluded a prior consistent statement, offered for impeachment purposes, made by a defense witness. The remark was not substantially inconsistent with testimony and did not sufficiently relate to a material matter. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Hamilton


No. 13696


Supreme Court of Connecticut


214 Conn. 692; 573 A.2d 1197; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 118


January 3, 1990, Argued  
April 24, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of possession of narcotics with intent to sell or dispense and with one count of the crime of possession of drug paraphernalia in a drug factory situation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Stodolink, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence and rendered judgment dismissing the charges, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to the Appellate Court, Spallone, Stoughton and Norcott, Js., which affirmed the trial court's decision, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Connecticut, sought review of the judgment of the appellate court (Connecticut), which upheld a grant of a motion to suppress certain keys used to unlock a van where drugs were stored filed by defendant in connection with two counts of unlawful possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell and one count of possession of drug paraphernalia in a drug factory situation.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court upheld a decision by a trial court to grant a motion to suppress certain keys used to unlock a van where drugs were stored filed by defendant in connection with three drug possession related charges. The appellate court's decision was based on its holding that, on the basis of the testimony given during the pretrial hearing on defendant's motion to suppress the van keys seized by the police in a search of defendant's apartment, the trial court could have reasonably concluded the a detective had reason to believe, prior to the procurement of the four search warrants involved, that the van was ordinarily locked, that the keys were kept in defendant's apartment, and that the detective entered defendant's apartment with the specific purpose of locating the keys and thus the discovery of such keys was not inadvertent to come within the plain view doctrine. On the basis of the same evidence, the court concluded that the appellate court did not err in concluding that the discovery of the van keys was not inadvertent within the meaning of the plain view exception. Accordingly, the appellate court's decision was affirmed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court that affirmed the decision of the trial court to suppress evidence.

 

292 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Somerville


Nos. 13536, 13550


Supreme Court of Connecticut


214 Conn. 378; 572 A.2d 944; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 97


February 7, 1990, Argued  
April 3, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and breach of the peace, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, from which the state, on the granting of permission, and the defendant filed separate appeals to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part on the state's appeal, further proceedings; no error on the defendant's appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of New London (Connecticut), which, following a jury trial, found defendant guilty of possession with intent to sell cocaine in a freebase form by a person who was not drug-dependent in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a).


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted by a jury of possession with intent to sell cocaine in a freebase form by a person who was not drug-dependent in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a), defendant appealed asserting that the superior court erred in denying his motion for judgment of acquittal. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but remanded the case for resentencing. The court noted that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35a instituted a definite sentencing scheme for any felony committed on or after July 1, 1981, and thereby implicitly repealed the indeterminate sentencing aspect of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a). The court agreed with defendant that in compliance with the definite sentencing requirement of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35a, the proper construction of the remaining penalty provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a) was a definite sentence anywhere within the statutory range of five years to life set forth in that statute. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of possession of narcotics with the intent to sell and found the rest of his appeal without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but remanded the case for the imposition of a definite sentence.

 

293 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Lehrer v. Davis


No. 13752


Supreme Court of Connecticut


214 Conn. 232; 571 A.2d 691; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 86


January 3, 1990, Argued  
March 20, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action seeking visitation rights with the defendants' minor children and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Coppeto, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved the question of the constitutionality of the statute governing visitation for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandparents filed an action against defendant parents, seeking visitation with their grandchildren. The parents filed a motion to strike. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) reserved the question concerning the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59 for the advice of an appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents sought visitation with their grandchildren. The parents contended that § 46b-59 was unconstitutional. The trial court granted a motion for reservation upon stipulated facts. The court declined to answer the reserved question because insufficient facts were presented. A party challenging the constitutionality of a statute was required to provide an adequate factual record in order to meet its burden of demonstrating the statute's adverse impacted on some protected interest of his own, in his own particular case. The court did not give advisory opinions, based on some set of hypothetical facts. Neither the parent's general right to raise their children without unwarranted state interference nor their stipulated status as an intact family provided the court with a basis to consider their constitutional claims on the incomplete record. The court determined that the custodial rights of an intact family did not automatically preclude the visitation rights of grandparents. Based on the record, the constitutionality of § 46b-59 was not ripe for adjudication.


OUTCOME: The court did not answer the reserved question. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

294 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Sanchez v. Warden, State Prison


No. 13820


Supreme Court of Connecticut


214 Conn. 23; 570 A.2d 673; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 55


December 12, 1989, Argued  
February 20, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petitions for writs of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the court, Axelrod, J.; judgment granting the petitions in part from which, on the granting of certification, the respondent appealed and the petitioner Joseph Wilson cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error on the appeal, judgment directed; no error on the cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In s habeas corpus proceeding, respondent prison warden appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut) that held that petitioners had a First Amendment right to regular radios that did not contain headphones. A petitioner appealed the reversal of a decision that he was entitled to his regular radio when it was discovered that the radio had a recording device.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners challenged the warden's policy that only headphone-equipped radios were allowed to be used in prison. The trial court found that the policy violated the First Amendment of the Constitution and ordered that petitioners be allowed to use non-headphone radios. However, the trial court held that the radio of one of the petitioners could not be returned to him because it contained a recording device. Both the warden and that petitioner appealed. The court reversed the decision that the warden's policy violated the Constitution while affirming the decision concerning that petitioner. The court held that petitioners did not show that the warden's radio policy violated the First Amendment. There was no First Amendment distinction between regular sound-emitting radios and headphone radios, and, therefore, no First Amendment issue was involved. There was no error when the trial court overturned the decision to return the one prisoner's radio to him when new information was discovered that the radio had a forbidden recording device.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the warden's appeal, set aside the judgment, and remanded the case with direction to render judgment for him. The court found no error in petitioner's cross appeal.

 

295 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Singh v. Singh


No. 13698


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 637; 569 A.2d 1112; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 38


November 2, 1989, Argued  
February 6, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the annulment of a marriage, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and referred to Hon. Simon Cohen, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment annulling the marriage; thereafter, the court, Kline, J., denied the parties' motion to open the judgment and the parties jointly appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband and defendant wife appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) that denied the parties' motion to open the judgment in which the parties sought a new ruling that their marriage, between an uncle and a niece of half-blood, did not violate Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46b-21, 53a-191 which declared their marriage incestuous and therefore invalid.


OVERVIEW: The court transferred the parties' appeal from the appellate court pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 4023. The parties argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-21 in providing those relationships which were prohibited from marrying did not specify that half blood relations could not marry and that that statute along with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-91 a penal statute criminalizing incest between the relationships specified in § 46b-21 should not be so construed. The court looked to the history of the incest law noting that since 1702 marriage between persons related by either consanguinity or affinity was prohibited. The court refused to narrowly construe the statutes so as to thwart the legislative intent. The court held that the degrees of relationship within which marriages were prohibited were not words of art. Rather, as fairly read, the prohibition against intermarriage of those related by consanguinity can be understood to extend to those of the half blood as well as of the whole blood.Therefore, a marriage between persons related to one another as half uncle and half niece was void under §§ 46b-21 and 53a-191 as incestuous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the parties' motion to open the judgment that annulled their marriage.

State v. Paradise


No. 13279


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 388; 567 A.2d 1221; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 3


November 8, 1989, Argued  
January 2, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of capital felony from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's arguments on appeal and found that: (1) the dismissal of the charges initially brought against defendant on the grounds that they were barred by the statute of limitations failed to render his subsequent prosecution on a more severe charge for the same conduct violative of due process; (2) a new trial was not required as a result of the state's misrepresentations concerning its sentencing recommendation for an accomplice witness; (3) the trial court did not commit error in prohibiting defendant from inquiring into charges of misconduct leveled against a physician who testified as to the cause of the victim's death because trial judges retain wide latitude to impose reasonable limits on such cross-examination based on concerns about, among other things, harassment, prejudice, confusion of the issues, the witness' safety, or interrogation that is repetitive or only marginally relevant; and (4) the trial court did not commit error in failing to ascertain on the record whether defendant had made a knowing, voluntary, and intelligent waiver of his right to testify.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

DiBerardino v. DiBerardino


No. 13717


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 373; 568 A.2d 431; 1990 Conn. LEXIS 6


November 7, 1989, Argued  
January 2, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and referred to Hon. Simon S. Cohen, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief; thereafter, the court, Freed, J., referred the motions to modify filed by the state, on the plaintiff's behalf, and by the defendant to Katherine Y. Hutchinson, family support magistrate, who recommended that the support award be increased; subsequently, the court, Kline, J., approved and adopted the findings and recommendations of the family support magistrate and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which adopted a family support magistrate's findings and recommendation that the father's support payments to plaintiff mother should be increased.


OVERVIEW: The superior court ordered an increase in the father's child support payments. On appeal, the court affirmed the superior court's order. The court held that: (1) the motion to increase support payments was heard and ruled upon under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-86(c); (2) the magistrate, who was charged with a duty of finding facts and rendering a report to a judge of the superior court, was not a judge of the supreme or superior court; therefore did not need to be appointed in accordance with the provisions of Conn. Const. art. fifth, § 2; (3) the state referee system did not encroach upon and did not unconstitutionally compete with other constitutional courts; (4) the trial court could reasonably have found that the changes in the circumstances of the parties were uncontemplated at the time of the dissolution order; and (5) the superior court did not err in ordering the father to contribute to the cost of a remedial reading program for the parties' son.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the superior court adopting the family support magistrate's findings and recommendation to increase the father's child support payments.

 

298 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Stein v. Katz


No. 13767


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 282; 567 A.2d 1183; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 353


November 9, 1989, Argued  
December 26, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for medical malpractice, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and referred to Hon. Douglass B. Wright, state trial referee, who, pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved the questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; thereafter, the reservation was transferred to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to the stipulations of the parties the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), reserved certain questions pertaining to the constitutionality of the prohibition contained in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584 against bringing an action for malpractice more than three years from the act or omission complained of.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient brought an action for medical malpractice against defendant dentist for conduct that occurred more than three years prior to the filing. The dentist, who died while the action was pending, asserted as a special defense the three-year bar to contained in § 52-584 that precluded such claims that occurred more than three years prior to any negligent act or omission. The parties stipulated the reservation of the questions concerning the constitutionality of § 52-584 and the court concluded that the statute was not unconstitutional. The patient contended that she could not have discovered the alleged negligence within that time period because she did not become aware of it until the dentist retired and another dentist advised her of the negligence. The court concluded that irrespective of her inability to reasonably discover the negligence, § 52-584 barred the claim. The statute did not violate the prohibition found in Conn. Const. art. first, § 10, that prevented the legislature from abolishing common law rights because the patient's action under common law would have abated with the death of the dentist and she would have no further right to pursue the claim.


OUTCOME: The court held that the prohibition contained in the statute against bringing an action for malpractice more than three years from the act or omission complained of as not unconstitutional.

 

299 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


McCarthy v. Warden


No. 13560


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 289; 567 A.2d 1187; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 354


November 8, 1989, Argued  
December 26, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Axelrod, J.; judgment granting the petition, in part, from which, on the granting of certification, the respondent appealed and the petitioner cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error on the appeal, judgment directed; no error on the cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate and respondent warden both challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Tolland (Connecticut), which granted judgment to the inmate relating to one disciplinary proceeding, reinstated good time credits for that incident, and granted the warden's motion to quash the claims relating to 20 other disciplinary actions. The inmate brought the habeas corpus action alleging constitutional errors in the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: A written report of an investigating correction officer was the sole basis for the disciplinary committee's finding that the inmate petitioner was guilty of misconduct for the assault in question. The inmate unsuccessfully attacked the constitutionality of the disciplinary hearing in federal court under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and then filed the instant action in state court. The trial court held that res judicata did not apply. On appeal, the court disagreed. In both actions, the inmate alleged that his inability to call the victim and the officer as witnesses deprived him of due process, so the federal court adjudicated the identical claim. Federal courts lacked the authority to restore good time credits, but the proposition that parallel proceedings in federal and state courts were allowed to expedite proceedings when administrative error was shown to exist did not justify relitigation of constitutional issues that had been found to be groundless. The warden's motion to quash was properly granted because a new rule imposing a substantive evidentiary standard to the revocation of good time credits added a new due process requirement that did not apply retrospectively.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the trial court that entered judgment for the inmate, directed judgment for the warden, and set aside the restoration of the inmate's good time credits. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted the warden's motion to quash.

Bolt Technology Corp. v. Dubno


Nos. 13648, 13652, 13653


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 220; 567 A.2d 371; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 346


October 11, 1989, Argued  
December 12, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal in each case from the assessment of additional corporate taxes and interest against the plaintiffs by the defendant commissioner, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Fracasse, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulations, reserved questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; thereafter, the reservations were transferred to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers, who appealed from a determination of defendant commissioner of revenue services that disallowed certain commission expenses that each taxpayer claimed on its state corporation business tax return, entered into stipulations for reservation, and the Superior Court (Connecticut) agreed to reserve the issue presented. The court transferred the reservations to itself.


OVERVIEW: The issue reserved for the court was one of statutory construction. The court was asked whether the sales commissions paid by taxpayer parent companies to their domestic international sales corporation (DISC) and deducted on their federal income tax returns were expenses related to the dividends received by the taxpayers from the DISC within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-217 (a) (D) (1) so that the commissions were not deductible to the extent of the dividends received in determining the taxpayers' tax liability. The taxpayers contended that the statute was intended to eliminate, in part, the corporation business tax on dividends, and not, as the commissioner concluded, to disallow the deduction of commission expenses to the extent of dividends that were paid to a parent company by its DISC. The court found the taxpayers' argument unpersuasive because it found the statute to be unambiguous. The court found that the sales commissions were expenses related to dividends because they were directly responsible for generating the dividends paid by the DISCs to their parent companies.


OUTCOME: The court answered in the affirmative to the question of law reserved. The question pertained to the disallowance of certain deductions of sales commission expenses by parent company taxpayers.

General Motors Corp. v. Martine


No. 13646


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 136; 567 A.2d 808; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 342


October 11, 1989, Argued  
December 5, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to vacate an arbitration award, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Lewis, J., granted the motion to intervene as party defendant filed by the department of consumer protection; thereafter, the court, Ryan, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved the questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; subsequently, the reservation was transferred to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant manufacturer sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Stamford-Norwalk District (Connecticut), which awarded plaintiff purchaser of a defective motor vehicle a refund of the purchase price without allowing defendant an offset to reflect damage that the vehicle had sustained in an accident caused by its defective condition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant manufacturer challenged the trial court's order, which, based on an arbitration decision, awarded plaintiff purchaser a refund of the purchase price of the defective motor vehicle without allowing defendant an offset to reflect damage that the vehicle had sustained in an accident caused by its defective condition. The court affirmed the order. The court found that claims brought to arbitration panels pursuant to Lemon Law II were essentially equitable, and thus did not warrant a jury trial. The court also found that the statute made no reference to any other deductions from refund orders, and since the arbitration panel carefully tracked each of the other provisions of the statutory formula, the court concluded that the arbitral decision did not exceed the scope of Lemon Law II.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which, based on an arbitration decision, awarded plaintiff purchaser a refund of the purchase price of the defective motor vehicle. The court concluded that the arbitral decision did not exceed the scope of Lemon Law II where it carefully tracked each of the other provisions of the statutory formula.

All Brand Importers, Inc. v. Department of Liquor Control


No. 13651


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 184; 567 A.2d 1156; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 343


October 3, 1989, Argued  
December 5, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff from a decision by the named defendant which determined that the defendant Star Distributors, Inc., had acquired distribution rights for the plaintiff's products as a result of its merger with the defendant A. Gallo Distributing Company, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Goldstein, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff importer challenged the order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed its appeal from a decision by defendant liquor department. Defendant new distributor acquired the importer's distribution rights by merger with defendant old distributor pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 33-369(c).


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose between a liquor importer and a new distributor regarding the acquisition of the importer's distribution rights. The liquor department determined that § 33-369(c) vested the new distributor with the importer's rights and that was compatible with the Liquor Control Act, particularly Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 30-17. The court affirmed the lower court's dismissal of the appeal of that decision. No reasonable statutory basis supported the assertion that § 30-17 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 33-369(c) could not coexist. The legislature presumably had knowledge of existing laws. Thus, § 33-369(c) applied to the importer's agreement with the old distributor. Pursuant to § 33-369(c), the merger vested in the new distributor the rights of the old distributor by operation of law. That automatic vesting did not deprive the importer of its Fourteenth Amendment or procedural due process rights. The liquor department had a legitimate interest in controlling the liquor industry. Also, the importer had no right to a hearing to contest automatic vesting. Finally, the court lacked jurisdiction over the importer's antitrust claims because such claims were exclusively federal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment dismissing the importer's appeal from a declaratory ruling by the liquor department.

Tower Business Park Associates Number One Ltd. Partnership v. Water Pollution Control Authority


No. 13762


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 112; 566 A.2d 696; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 331


October 12, 1989, Argued  
November 28, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a supplemental sewer assessment levied against certain real property of the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Fracasse, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Water Pollution Control Authority of the Town of Simsbury appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which was entered in favor of plaintiff limited partnership after the partnership appealed from a supplemental sewer assessment levied against certain of its real property.


OVERVIEW: The limited partnership converted a factory building on its property into a two story office building. The authority imposed a supplemental sewer assessment on the property. The partnership appealed the assessment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-250. The trial court rendered judgment for the partnership, thus invalidating the assessment on the ground that it was not determined on the basis of the actual benefit to the subject property adjusted to the time of the initial assessment. The authority appealed and claimed that the trial court erred in finding that the partnership's evidence was sufficient to overcome the presumption of the validity of the supplemental assessment. The court determined that because the partnership did not produce any evidence that the total assessment, both initial and supplemental, exceeded the difference in the market value of its property with and without sewers as of the time of the original assessment, the presumption of the validity of the assessment had not been overcome and the trial court's conclusion to the contrary was clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to render judgment for the authority.

Chotkowski v. State


No. 13683


Supreme Court of Connecticut


213 Conn. 13; 566 A.2d 419; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 326


October 4, 1989, Argued  
November 21, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for breach of an employment contract, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, O'Neill, J., granted the state's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in form of judgment; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employee appealed from the grant of summary judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), in favor of defendant State in his action to recover damages for breach of an employment contract.


OVERVIEW: The claimant contended that his suit could be maintained because the claims commissioner had authorized him to bring the action against the State pursuant to Conn. General Statutes § 4-160 (a), pursuant to which a special act had been enacted validating his claim against the State despite the fact that the limitation period for his claim had run. The trial court granted summary judgment to the State on the ground that as a state employee in the classified service, he had no contractual rights, express or implied, against the State as his employer but only those rights made available to state employees by statute. The court did not reach the substantive issues. The unconstitutionality of the special act defeated the trial court's jurisdiction to entertain the action. The special act allowing the state employee to sue the State despite failure to present his claim to the claims commissioner within the time allowed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148 (a) constituted the grant of "exclusive public emoluments or privileges" in violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 1. The court found that the special act could not withstand constitutional attack because it did not advance a public purpose.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was error in the form of the judgment. The court set aside the judgment and remanded the case with direction to the trial court to render a judgment of dismissal for lack of jurisdiction over the State.

Beacon Falls v. Posick


No. 13561


Supreme Court of Connecticut


212 Conn. 570; 563 A.2d 285; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 244


June 6, 1989, Argued  
August 8, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from operating a private landfill, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and referred to Hon. Joseph J. Chernauskas, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., Borden and Bieluch, Js., which set aside the trial court's judgment and directed judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a town, appealed a decision of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which reversed a trial court decision that invalidated certain ordinances and regulations of the town. The ordinances and regulations prohibited the operation of a dump in the town by defendant dump operator in the town's complaint for injunctive relief against the dump operator to enjoin his operation of the dump.


OVERVIEW: The dump operator obtained a permit from the Connecticut Department of Environmental Regulation to operate a solid waste disposal site. The town filed a complaint for injunctive relief against the dump operator, stating that Town of Beacon Falls, Connecticut, Zoning Regulations §§ 2.1, 6.4 prohibited its operation. The injunction, after referral to a referee, was granted, but reversed on appeal. On further appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the statement in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-208(c) that a department permit did not override local zoning regulations was not affected by 1984 Conn. Pub. Acts. 84-331. The court held that the restriction in 1984 Conn. Pub. Acts. 84-331 was to limit the application of local zoning regulations to land owned by the Connecticut Resources Recovery Authority, but not to private land, such as that owned by the dump operator. The court concluded that trial referee's decision regarding the constitutionality of the regulation was not clearly erroneous because the zoning regulation enjoyed a presumption of constitutionality and there was no evidence to establish its unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision declaring that the local zoning regulation was preempted by state law.

Sgueglia v. Milne Constr. Co.


No. 13686


Supreme Court of Connecticut


212 Conn. 427; 562 A.2d 505; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 245


June 15, 1989, Argued  
August 8, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of the defendant's alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and referred to Hon. Lester H. Aaronson, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, granted the motion of D&M Masonry Company, Inc., to intervene as a party plaintiff and to file a complaint against the defendant; thereafter, the court, Mulcahy, J., granted the defendant's motion to implead D&M Masonry Company, Inc., as a third party defendant; subsequently, the court, Purtill, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment against the plaintiff and the intervening plaintiff D&M Masonry Company, Inc., and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee of a subcontractor appealed an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted summary judgment to defendant general contractor in the employee's action to recover for injuries he sustained as the result of the contractor's negligence, contending that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-291 created an impermissible emolument for the contractor in violation of Conn. Const. art. First, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for a subcontractor that was hired by the contractor to participate in a construction project. The employee was injured as the result of the contractor's negligence and brought an action to recover for those injuries. The contractor asserted that it was the principal employer of the employee and was immune from liability pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-291. The contractor filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted by the superior court. The employee appealed, contending that § 31-291 created an impermissible emolument for the contractor in violation of Conn. Const. art. First, § 1. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that the contractor was a principal employer under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-291 and, as such, was responsible for payment of workers' compensation benefits for injuries sustained by the employee and that the employee was therefore barred from any common law action against it. There was no violation of Conn. Const. art. First, § 1 because the contractor not only failed to receive any emolument or privilege but paid its own workers' compensation coverage and that of the subcontractor indirectly through the contract price.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment awarded to the contractor.

 

307 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Spicer v. Noank Fire Dist. Zoning Com.


No. 13678


Supreme Court of Connecticut


212 Conn. 375; 562 A.2d 21; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 232


June 7, 1989, Argued  
August 1, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal in two counts from a decision of the defendant zoning commission which approved an application for site plan review of certain real property owned by the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Purtill, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss count one of the plaintiffs' complaint and rendered judgment thereon, and the plaintiffs filed a motion to set aside the judgment, which was denied, from which the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which granted defendant zoning commission's motion to dismiss on the ground the landowners failed to serve or cite the clerk of the municipality of the landowners' appeal from a zoning decision as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(b). The Supreme Court transferred the action to itself pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book. § 4023.


OVERVIEW: The landowners challenged a decision of the zoning commission, and filed an appeal of the decision to the trial court. The zoning commission was the sole defendant. The zoning commission filed a motion to dismiss the landowners' appeal for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because the clerk of the municipality was not served pursuant to the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(b). The landowners claimed that 1988 Conn. Acts 88-79, § 3 saved their appeal. The trial court granted the zoning commission's motion and denied the landowners' motion to set aside the dismissal, and the landowners appealed. The Supreme Court took the appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 4023. The court held that although 1988 Conn. Acts 88-79, § 3 saved appeals with merely technical defects, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(b) required that the clerk of the municipality at least be given copies of the pleadings. In dismissing the appeal, the court held that failure to name the clerk and to provide copies of the pleadings were more than mere technical defects and warranted dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

308 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Krozser v. New Haven


No. 13589


Supreme Court of Connecticut


212 Conn. 415; 562 A.2d 1080; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 237


May 11, 1989, Argued  
August 1, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the wrongful death of the plaintiff's decedent, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Flanagan, J., granted the motion to dismiss filed by the defendant state of Connecticut et al. and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the action was withdrawn against the named defendant, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted the motion of defendants, the State of Connecticut and its commissioner of correction, to dismiss an action to recover damages for the wrongful death of decedent.


OVERVIEW: The administrator alleged that the deliberate indifference to the decedent's serious medical needs while he was incarcerated directly resulted in his death. The trial court dismissed defendants from the action, holding that it was barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The court affirmed the order and held that the State could not be sued without its consent. The administrator was unable to point to any statute that waived the State's sovereign immunity and did not receive permission from the claims commissioner to bring an action against the State. The court concluded that 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was not intended to override sovereign immunity of the State. Although immunity could be waived by the claims commissioner under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160, that did not happen in this case and, thus, the lower court had no jurisdiction to hear a claim for monetary damages. The court stated that 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 did not give the lower court authorization to borrow the language in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160 to determine if the State could be liable. The court concluded that § 1988 was only applicable when federal law was inapplicable or in some way deficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, which granted the motion to dismiss filed by defendants, state and commissioner of correction. The court held that the lower court did not have jurisdiction to hear plaintiff administrator's action for monetary damages resulting from a wrongful death unless the state gave its permission to be sued or the claims commissioner waived the state's right to sovereign immunity.

State v. Ruscoe


No. 13447


Supreme Court of Connecticut


212 Conn. 223; 563 A.2d 267; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 226


March 30, 1989, Argued  
July 25, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of selling equipment with defective identification marks and one count each of the crimes of larceny in the second degree and use of drug paraphernalia, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the jury before Maiocco, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of larceny in the second degree, use of drug paraphernalia, and three counts of selling equipment with defective identification marks.


OVERVIEW: The police had a warrant to search defendant's house for silver candleholders, napkin rings, and a mug, which had been stolen during a recent burglary. During the search, the police seized drug paraphernalia, electronic equipment, and major appliances. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment in part. The court held: (1) there was sufficient probable cause for the search warrant based on information provided by a confidential informer; (2) defendant was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing to challenge the search warrant; (3) the search warrant was sufficiently particular; (4) the police sufficiently complied with the knock and announce rule when executing the search warrant; (5) the plain view doctrine allowed the seizure of the objects not described in the search warrant; and (6) defendant could not be punished for multiple violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-132 based on the simultaneous possession of more than one piece of electronic equipment with defective identification marks.


OUTCOME: The court vacated two of defendant's convictions for selling equipment with defective identification marks. The court affirmed the remainder of the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Breton


No. 13677


Supreme Court of Connecticut


212 Conn. 258; 562 A.2d 1060; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 225


June 6, 1989, Argued  
July 25, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Breton, 235 Conn. 206, 663 A.2d 1026, 1995 Conn. LEXIS 319 (1995)
Reaffirmed State v. Breton, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 244 (Conn., June 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of murder and one count of the crime of capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the state filed a notice of aggravating factor; thereafter, the court, Heiman, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss the notice of aggravating factor, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; remanded for sentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Waterbury (Connecticut), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the notice of aggravating factor in connection with a count of capital felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the term "especially cruel" in the aggravating factor violated the federal and state constitutions. Defendant was later found guilty on two counts of the crime of murder and one count of the crime of capital felony. On appeal, the court held that the term "especially cruel," while unconstitutionally vague standing alone, could be limited and construed so as to pass constitutional muster. Defendant argued that neither the court nor the trial court should engage in any further definition of the term because that task fell within the legislature's domain. The State maintained that the court had an independent responsibility for statutory construction. The court agreed with the State. The court ruled that within a capital felony context, the term "especially cruel" had to include the intentional infliction of extreme pain or torture above and beyond that necessarily accompanying the underlying killing. The court adopted that definition of "especially cruel" as an acceptable core construction of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(h)(4).


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court to proceed with the sentencing hearing in a manner consistent with the court's opinion.

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which imposed fines and granted injunctive relief in an action by plaintiff Commissioner of Transportation seeking removal of outdoor advertising sign structures erected by defendant upon private property bordering the interstate.
