State v. Anderson


No. 13302


Supreme Court of Connecticut


212 Conn. 31; 561 A.2d 897; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 195


March 29, 1989, Argued  
July 4, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Anderson v. Warden, State Prison, 1990 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1777 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 20, 1990)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Anderson v. Mangano, 1995 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3267 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 16, 1995)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Request granted Anderson v. Warden, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 317 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 17, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Anderson v. Warden, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 76 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 2, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Anderson v. Warden, State Prison, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3056 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, and one count each of the crimes of attempted robbery in the first degree, and attempted sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Kline, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count each of kidnapping in the first degree, attempted robbery in the first degree and attempted sexual assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Anderson, 211 Conn. 18, 557 A.2d 917, 1989 Conn. LEXIS 101 (1989)



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him upon a jury verdict for first degree kidnapping pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(B), first degree attempted robbery pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-49(a)(2), -134(a)(3), and first degree attempted sexual assault pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-49(a)(2), -70(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of various crimes for, according to his victim, taking her to a school yard, attempting to engage in sexual intercourse, taking her to his apartment, and engaging in sexual intercourse, all at knife point. On appeal, defendant argued double jeopardy, improper instructions, insufficient evidence, and other grounds. The court affirmed. Trying defendant for two counts of kidnapping and for both attempted sexual assault and sexual assault did not violate double jeopardy, because defendant was only sentenced for one count of kidnapping and for attempted sexual assault. The trial court's instructions as a whole properly explained that defendant could only be guilty of first degree kidnapping if he were also guilty of the underlying felony. It was not reversible error to give the jury a missing witness instruction, because defendant did not timely object and because the evidence indicated that defendant failed to produce two witnesses who were able to testify, were within his power to produce, and would support his claim that he knew the victim socially. Despite making inappropriate comments, the trial court did not rely on improper evidence in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant for kidnapping, attempted robbery, and attempted sexual assault.

Motor Vehicle Mfrs. Asso. v. O'Neill


No. 13555


Supreme Court of Connecticut


212 Conn. 83; 561 A.2d 917; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 200


May 2, 1989, Argued  
July 4, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the constitutional validity of a public act concerning, inter alia, dispute resolution procedures for defective new motor vehicles, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, M. Hennessey, J., granted the motion of John J. Woodcock III to intervene as a party defendant; thereafter, the case was tried to the court; the court, having declared the act to be constitutional, rendered judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, motor vehicle manufacturer associations (associations), brought an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendant state challenging the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 42-181 to -185 (Lemon Law II). The Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) declared Lemon Law II to be constitutional and rendered judgment for the state. The associations appealed.


OVERVIEW: The associations sought review of the statutory procedures under Lemon Law II, specifically the arbitration of motor vehicle disputes that, for manufacturers but not for consumers, severely limited the scope of judicial review for challenges to adverse arbitration determinations. The trial court concluded that the associations had failed to establish any violation of their state or federal constitutional rights. On appeal, the court held that the associations were not deprived of their right to a trial by jury because the record demonstrated the essentially equitable nature of the Lemon Law II claims. The associations were not entitled to relief from filing fees because there was a rational nexus between the legislature's goal of creating a fiscally independent arbitration mechanism for automobile consumers and the requirement that manufacturers pay the fee. The court held, however, that the judicial review provisions did not satisfy constitutional due process requirements. The arbitration procedures were compulsory and, thus, the limited review provided was constitutionally insufficient and constituted disparate treatment.


OUTCOME: The court found error and set aside the trial court's judgment. The case was remanded to the trial court with direction to render judgment for the associations.

Enthone, Inc. v. Bannon

Supreme Court of Connecticut


211 Conn. 655; 560 A.2d 971; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 183


May 9, 1989, Argued  
June 27, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff from the assessment of a hazardous waste tax, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and referred to Hon. Harold M. Mulvey, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which rendered judgment in favor of defendant Commissioner of Revenue Services who assessed the taxpayer a hazardous waste tax pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-132.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner assessed the taxpayer a tax on hazardous waste that was shipped from one of the taxpayer's plants. The taxpayer alleged that because it did not generate the hazardous waste, it was not subject to a hazardous waste assessment. The Commissioner argued that the taxpayer was liable for the assessment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-132(a)(1) because it had to file the uniform hazardous waste manifest required by the Resource Conservation and Recovery Act of 1976. The court agreed with the taxpayer and held that neither the statutes nor the regulations authorized the imposition of an assessment on hazardous waste that was not generated by the shipper. The court stated that the material was not produced by the taxpayer but only shipped to the taxpayer for treatment. The court determined that the taxpayer had to identify itself on the federal form as the generator of the hazardous waste because the federal law prohibited any modification of the form. The taxpayer did explain in the space provided that the material had been shipped to its location by another company.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the lower court's judgment and remanded the case back for judgment to be rendered in the taxpayer's favor.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempted sexual assault in the second degree, sexual assault in the fourth degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area six, and tried to the jury before Gray, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant appealed his conviction for attempted sexual assault in the second degree, sexual assault in the fourth degree, and risk of injury to a child under the age of 16 years, entered in the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: The defendant's primary challenge to his convictions was based on whether the provision of Conn. Gen. Additionally, the trial judge did not abuse his discretion when he refused the defendant's request to charge the jury on the credibility of a child witness. The defendant's claims that his rights of confrontation and to impeach witnesses were violated were examined by the court and any errors found were deemed harmless. The court found no errors in the trial court's jury instructions.

Franklin v. Berger


No. 13450


Supreme Court of Connecticut


211 Conn. 591; 560 A.2d 444; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 176


January 12, 1989, Argued  
June 20, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the court, Koletsky, J.; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner appealed to the Appellate Court, Daly, Norcott and Foti, Js., which set aside the trial court's decision and remanded the case with direction to credit the petitioner with time spent in confinement prior to trial, and the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state official appealed a judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which set aside a judgment of a habeas court that denied petitioner insanity acquitee's request for habeas corpus relief. The appellate court further remanded the case with direction to credit petitioner with time spent in confinement prior to trial.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was arrested and charged with manslaughter in the first degree. He was confined in jail for 293 days prior to trial and spent 378 days in a mental hospital while his competency to stand trial was determined. He was found not guilty by reason of insanity and committed to a mental institution for 10 years. The State declined to credit petitioner's pretrial jail time against the maximum term of his commitment and the trial court upheld the denial in petitioner's habeas corpus action in which he alleged an equal protection violation. On petitioner's appeal, the appellate court set aside the trial court's decision. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the appellate court, holding that the State did not violate the guarantees of equal protection contained in the Connecticut and United States Constitutions by declining to credit the pretrial jail time. The State was not treating wealthy and poor insanity acquittees differently because, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-257a et seq., jail time credit was irrelevant in calculating the release of an insanity acquittee because he was confined or released based on his dangerousness.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, which in turn had set aside the trial court's denial of petitioner's habeas corpus action.

State v. Delossantos


No. 13230


Supreme Court of Connecticut


211 Conn. 258; 559 A.2d 164; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 139


March 9, 1989, Argued  
May 23, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before Fuller, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court; thereafter, the trial court denied the defendant's motion for a new trial and the defendant filed an amended appeal to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of unlawful possession and transportation of cocaine with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a) (1987) and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession and transportation of cocaine with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a) (1987) and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38 (1987). On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that a warrantless search of the hatchback area of an automobile driven by defendant was valid as a search incident to a lawful arrest because the hatchback was an extension of the passenger compartment. It was not error to bar a defense witness's testimony that the owner of the automobile was a cocaine dealer where there was no direct evidence of the owner's involvement in the crime and defendant's possession of the automobile for two days immediately preceding his arrest attenuated the owner's connection to the automobile. "Operability" of the "weapon" was not an essential element of a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38 (1987). A jury instruction correctly permitted the jury to infer defendant's possession of cocaine from his exclusive possession of the automobile. Also, the trial court complied with the definite sentencing requirement of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35a.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful possession and transportation of cocaine with intent to sell and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle without a permit. The court held that an automobile hatchback was part of the passenger compartment and, therefore, it was within the scope of a search incident to defendant's lawful arrest, and that "operability" of a revolver was not an essential element of the weapons charge.

Merly v. State


No. 13527


Supreme Court of Connecticut


211 Conn. 199; 558 A.2d 977; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 130


March 9, 1989, Argued  
May 16, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the wrongful death of the plaintiff's decedent while a patient in a state medical facility, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, McGrath, J., granted the state's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff decedent's estate challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) that granted defendant State's motion for summary judgment and entered judgment thereon in the estate's action for the wrongful death of the decedent.


OVERVIEW: The estate filed an action to recover damages for the wrongful death of the decedent while a patient in a state medical facility. The trial court granted the state's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon. The court affirmed finding that 1984 Conn. Spec. Acts 21 § 1, which excused the failure of the estate to present its claim to the claims commissioner within one year after it accrued, was unconstitutional special legislation. Although the estate's claim was not necessarily barred by the delay from the decedent's death, that the family did not investigate the circumstances surrounding the decedent's suicide until one and one-half years after the death constituted as a matter of law a failure to exercise reasonable care to discover the accrual of the claim. The special legislation was essential because the legislature's rejection of the commissioner's recommendation that no award be granted to the estate did not authorize further consideration by the commissioner of the request for permission to sue. There was no public purpose sufficient to sustain the special enactment because state officials were not responsible for the delay in presenting the claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment and the judgment rendered thereon for the State in the estate's action for wrongful death.

 

320 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Faraci v. Connecticut Light & Power Co.


No. 13539


Supreme Court of Connecticut


211 Conn. 166; 558 A.2d 234; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 119


February 8, 1989, Argued  
May 9, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the second district dismissing the plaintiff's claim for disfigurement compensation benefits, brought to the compensation review division, which affirmed the commissioner's decision and dismissed the appeal, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee challenged an order of the compensation review division (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal of the denial of his claim against defendant employer for disfigurement workers' compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: Reasoning that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-308(d) excluded awarding workers' compensation benefits for any scar that resulted from spinal surgery, the review division dismissed the employee's appeal of his claim's denial. The court affirmed that dismissal, rejecting the employee's claims that § 31-308(d) violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20's Equal Protection Clauses. The court reasoned that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-308's disfigurement coverage for scars had evolved from a system of enumerated inclusions to one of enumerated exclusions and that the hernia operation exclusion changed to an inguinal hernia operation exclusion to make the disfigurement provision consistent with the prior practice of allowing compensation for "visible scars and to promote the state interest in compensating workers for those scars. The court also held that the exclusion rationally related to that interest by denying benefits for a disfigurement that was unlikely to be exposed to view. The court also held that precedent showed that § 31-308 passed the rational relationship test even if it was not made with mathematical nicety or it resulted in some inequality in practice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the employee's claim for disfigurement workers' compensation benefits for his scar from his spinal surgery.

State v. Hull


No. 13189


Supreme Court of Connecticut


210 Conn. 481; 556 A.2d 154; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 76


January 4, 1989, Argued  
March 21, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the jury before Arena, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a), in connection with the stabbing death of his wife, appealed the denial of his motion for acquittal from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: The principal issue was whether defendant's constitutional rights were violated by the admission of testimony informing the jury that defendant, after having been advised of his Miranda rights, invoked his right to silence by requesting an attorney. The court considered whether the trial court erred in permitting three state's witnesses to testify and the prosecutor to comment that defendant, after his arrest and after he had been advised of his Miranda rights, requested the assistance of his attorney. Defendant contended that admission of this evidence violated his due process rights as guaranteed by the Fourteenth Amendment. The court found that especially since defendant took the stand to testify in his own behalf, it was fundamentally unfair and a deprivation of due process to allow his silence to be admitted as evidence against him at trial. But an examination of the record showed that neither the prosecutor nor the state's witnesses focused upon or highlighted defendant's invocation of his right to counsel. Furthermore, the evidence of defendant's guilt was overwhelming. Thus the constitutional error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

Connecticut Light & Power Co. v. Department of Public Utility Control


No. 13480


Supreme Court of Connecticut


210 Conn. 349; 554 A.2d 1089; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 54


December 7, 1988, Argued  
March 14, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant determining that the plaintiff was obligated to purchase, at the municipal rate, the entire electricity output of a proposed solid waste disposal plant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the town of East Lyme et al. intervened as party defendants; thereafter, the court, Allen, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved certain questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; subsequently, the reservation was transferred to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff power company sought review of a decision of defendant department of public utility control, which determined that the company was obligated to purchase, at the municipal rate, the entire electricity output of a proposed solid waste disposal plant.


OVERVIEW: The regional resources recovery authority filed a petition with the department seeking a declaratory ruling determining the amounts and the prices that the company would be required to pay for the electrical output generated by the authority's municipal solid waste disposal facility. The department determined that the company was obligated to purchase, at the municipal rate, the entire electricity output of the solid waste disposal plant. The trial court reserved the matter for the consideration and advice of the appellate court, which transferred the case to the court for its consideration. The court reversed and remanded the department's decision holding that it had misconstrued Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-243e. The court further held that because only 70 percent of the municipal solid waste that would fuel the resources recovery facility came from municipalities served by the company, it was only required to pay the municipal rate on 70 percent of the purchased electricity. The court further held that the company, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-243a(b), was only required to purchase the remaining 30 percent of the output at the avoided cost rate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the department's decision, which determined that the company was obligated to purchase, at the municipal rate, the entire electricity output of a proposed solid waste disposal plant.

State v. Spigarolo


No. 13220


Supreme Court of Connecticut


210 Conn. 359; 556 A.2d 112; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 66


Argued December 13, 1988  
March 14, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the second degree and four counts of the crime of risk of injury to a minor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed; thereafter, this court, sua sponte, remanded the case to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing to address the admissibility of videotaped testimony of the minor victims; on remand, the court, Hadden, J., determined that the state had shown a compelling need for the videotaped testimony, and the parties filed supplemental briefs to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of sexual assault and risk of injury to a minor, and decided, on remand, that the use of videotape testimony of both minor victims comported with case law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-86g, which permitted a minor who was a victim of sexual assault to give testimony out of the courtroom, unconstitutionally deprived him of his right to face-to-face confrontation with his accusers. The court disagreed with the defendant's characterization that § 54-86g did "not permit" the trial court to conduct an evidentiary hearing to evaluate the state's need to exclude the defendant from the physical presence of the complainants, a procedure constitutionally required under case law. The court additionally found that the trial court did not err in permitting non-expert opinion evidence at the evidentiary hearing on remand on the issue of whether the defendant's physical presence would seriously have called into question the reliability and trustworthiness of the complaining minor witnesses' testimony. The court found that the trial court was not clearly erroneous in ruling that there was clear and convincing evidence that defendant's physical presence would have adversely affected the minors' testimony.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that there was no error.

American Totalisator Co. v. Dubno


Nos. 13408, 13410, 13411, 13412


Supreme Court of Connecticut


210 Conn. 401; 555 A.2d 414; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 63


December 16, 1988, Argued  
March 14, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Three appeals from the assessments of sales and use tax deficiencies, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the court, O'Neill, J.; judgment for the defendant in the first case, from which the plaintiff and the defendant filed separate appeals; judgment for the defendant in the second case, from which the plaintiff DTP Royalty, Inc., appealed and the defendant cross appealed; and judgment for the defendant in the third case, from which the plaintiff GTECH Corporation appealed and the defendant cross appealed.

The defendant filed motions for reargument which were denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-422, appealed, and defendant Commissioner of Revenue Services appealed in one case and cross appealed in another, from judgments rendered in the Superior Court (Connecticut) on the taxpayers' appeals from deficiency assessments of use taxes, penalties, and interest. The trial court had upheld the assessment of taxes but determined that they were not liable for penalties and interest.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers contracted with the state of Connecticut to provide personal property, training, personnel, and services to establish systems to enable the state to conduct its various wagering enterprises. They purchased or leased computers and related personal property on which they paid no sales tax. The taxpayers contended that that their purchases were not retail sales as defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-407(3) because the items had been purchased for resale and were not subject to the use tax under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-411. The court held that that the trial court committed no error. First, the language of the taxpayer's contracts with the state indicated that the property was incidental to the primary purpose of the contracts, which was to provide wagering systems, so it was not purchased or leased for resale and the assessment of the use tax was proper. Second, the abatement of penalties and interest was proper because the taxpayers had a firm and reasonably held belief in the correctness of their legal position, none of them brought suit for delay, and the relief was within the trial court's equitable powers pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-1.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court in all three consolidated cases were affirmed.

State v. Snook

210 Conn. 244; 555 A.2d 390; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 36


December 13, 1988, Argued  
March 7, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of sexual assault in the second degree, one count of the crime of sexual assault in the third degree and two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a minor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Gray, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed; thereafter, this court, sua sponte, remanded the case to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing to address the issue of the admissibility of videotaped testimony of the minor victim; on remand, the court, Gray, J., determined that the state had shown a compelling need for the videotaped testimony, and the parties filed supplemental briefs to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions by a jury in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for sexual assault in the second degree, sexual assault in the third degree, and risk of injury to a minor. Following a remand by this court to the superior court for an evidentiary hearing, defendant's appeal was heard.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of inappropriate sexual behavior with his six-year-old daughter. Over defendant's objection, the trial court granted the State's motion to have the daughter's testimony taken on videotape outside the defendant's physical presence, as provided in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-86g. Defendant appealed his conviction, but the case was remanded so the trial court could supplement the record in support of its decision regarding the videotaped testimony. This appeal then continued. Defendant argued § 54-86g violated his right to confrontation. He also argued the remand order violated due process by allowing the State to create a record after the fact. The court found defendant did not show how the statute violated his right to confrontation and the burden was on him to do so. Moreover, the court followed the language of the statute in demonstrating by clear and convincing evidence, on the record, that defendant's presence would call into question the daughter's reliability as a witness.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Connecticut Education Asso. v. Tirozzi


No. 13380


Supreme Court of Connecticut


210 Conn. 286; 554 A.2d 1065; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 38


January 3, 1989, Argued  
March 7, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutional validity of the state Education Enhancement Act, which invalidated all permanent and standard teaching certificates, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Vasington, J., granted the motion of the Connecticut State Federation of Teachers to be made a party plaintiff; thereafter, the court, R. O'Connell, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved certain questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; the reservation was then transferred to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, unions and teachers, filed an action against defendants, Commissioner of Education and the state board of education, and they sought a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the Education Enhancement Act, which invalidated all permanent and standard teaching certificates. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut) reserved the constitutionality issue for the instant court.


OVERVIEW: The Education Enhancement Act required teachers to exchange their standard or permanent teaching certificates for professional educator certificates and it also conditioned the renewal of the professional educator certificates upon the teachers' completion of continuing education classes. Plaintiffs contended that the Act deprived them of their substantive and procedural due process rights. The court held that (1) while the teachers had a constitutionally protected property interest in their certificates, the issuance of the new certificates did not violate their procedural due process rights because they were afforded the same rights under the new certification system as they were afforded under the old system and thus, the Act did not constitute a significant present impairment or deprivation of their property interests in their teaching certificates and (2) the Act did not violate the teachers' substantive due process rights because it was not irrational or arbitrary for the legislature to decide that its goal of enhancing the quality of the state's educational system required permanent teachers to continue to sharpen their educational skills.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the Education Enhancement Act did not violate the teachers' procedural and substantive due process rights.

State v. Smith


No. 13446


Supreme Court of Connecticut


210 Conn. 132; 554 A.2d 713; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 26


November 4, 1988, Argued  
February 21, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty from which the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant invited a woman back to his apartment and made advances on her. Though the woman repeatedly rejected his advances, defendant persisted. The woman testified that she believed defendant was determined to have sex with her and that he would hurt her if she did not go along with it. She reported the assault immediately. Defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-70. On review, defendant claimed several errors including that the trial court should have granted his motion for acquittal due to insufficiency of the evidence on the element of lack of consent. Defendant argued that he did not realize that the woman was not consenting, and that such subjective intent on his part was an element of the crime. The court disagreed. According to the court, the jury could properly have found beyond a reasonable doubt that the woman's words and actions could not reasonably be viewed to indicate her consent to intercourse. The court held that the inquiry on the issue of consent was not the subjective state of mind of defendant or the victim, but rather the victim's manifestations of lack of consent by words or conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual assault in the first degree.

In re Luis C.

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted a petition by the commissioner of children and youth services to terminate the parental rights of respondent and the father in their minor child.


OVERVIEW: This was an appeal by a mother whose parental rights to her young son were terminated pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 17-43a(b)(2) and (4). On appeal, the mother claimed that the trial court erred in concluding that she had failed to achieve a degree of personal rehabilitation that would allow her to assume a responsible position in the child's life. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 17-43a(d), the trial court made specific findings regarding the statutory factors necessary for consideration in a proceeding to terminate parental rights. For example, the court found that the counseling services provided to the mother had little effect in improving her parenting skills. It also found that the mother had displayed little dedication to meeting obligations that she had agreed to, such as attending parenting skills programs. It further found that the young boy had bonded with his foster parents, and that the mother had made only limited efforts to adjust her conduct and circumstances so that her son's return to live with her would be in his best interests. In light of these findings, the court found that the trial court's determination was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment that terminated the mother's parental rights to her young son.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, after a jury trial, from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), for sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the second degree, and risk of injury to a minor.


OVERVIEW: The victim was a five year old child who gave videotaped testimony outside defendant's physical presence. After defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the second degree, and risk of injury to a minor, he appealed. The court found no error. The trial court was not clearly erroneous in concluding that there was clear and convincing evidence that defendant's physical presence would seriously have called into question the victim's reliability and trustworthiness as a witness. The State's expert witnesses testified that the victim would have experienced anxiety and trauma if required to testify before defendant, rendering the testimony less reliable. The trial court's conclusion on remand that the evidence was clear and convincing that defendant's physical presence would seriously have called into question the minor victim's reliability during the videotaping procedure was legally and logically correct, and was supported by the facts. Defendant gave no evidence to contradict their testimony that the victim would have been intimidated by his presence, and that such intimidation would have undermined the reliability of the victim's testimony.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's conviction for sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the second degree, and risk of injury to a minor.

Lampasona v. Jacobs


No. 13281


Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 724; 553 A.2d 175; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 13


November 4, 1988, Argued  
January 31, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Summary process action, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Walsh, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, Hull and Daly, Js., which set aside the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings; on remand, the court, O'Connell, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mobile home park owner sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which upon remand from an appellate court, granted defendant mobile home owner's motion to dismiss. The owner sought to gain possession of a lot in his mobile home park and alleged that the mobile home owner occupied the lot without right or privilege and served a notice to quit upon the mobile home owner.


OVERVIEW: The owner claimed that the trial court erred in dismissing the case because it looked beyond the question of subject matter jurisdiction and decided the motion to dismiss on the merits of the case. The owner claimed that the trial court's interpretation of the term "resident," as used in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21-64, violated her constitutional rights. On review, the court found no error in the trial court's decision. The court held that the trial court was authorized to hear the action. The court found that the trial court had properly construed Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21-64(5) and its finding that the mobile home owner was a resident was correct. The court held that the trial court's determination that the owner had an affirmative duty under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21-79 to give the mobile home owner an application to purchase the home in the owner's park and, in acting on the application, the owner had a duty to state her reasons for granting or denying it. The court found that the owner did not do this and, therefore, acquiesced to the mobile home owner's residency in the park. The court concluded that the owner did not have her property unconstitutionally taken.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's dismissal of the mobile home park owner's complaint.

Supreme Court of Connecticut

January 31, 1989, Decided

DISPOSITION: No error.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of kidnapping in the first degree, sexual assault in a cohabiting relationship, and attempted assault in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his due process rights were violated when the state tried him for the crimes of sexual assault in a cohabiting relationship and sexual assault in a non-cohabiting relationship at the same time. The court found the joinder of the two counts was permissible. Defendant's voluntary decision to maintain mutually inconsistent defenses did not result in a due process violation that would require the state to make an election between the counts to which those defenses applied. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the defendant's motion for election. Although the trial court committed error in failing to instruct the jury on the burden of proof relative to the affirmative defense of cohabitation, the court found that it was harmless error. The court concluded that the trial court's instructions did not mislead the jury to believe that it must convict defendant of either Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70b or § 53a-70 if it found that the state had established the alleged sexual assault common to both offenses. The court also held that the trial court did not err in charging the jury on both statutory definitions of abduct.


OUTCOME: The court found no reversible error.

OVERVIEW: The truckers were an association made up of members who owned and operated trucks in interstate commerce, at times in and through Connecticut. The truckers argued the tax was illegal. Defendants, the State of Connecticut, the commissioner of revenue services and the state treasurer, moved to dismiss the action. Bottone v. Westport


No. 13370


Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 652; 553 A.2d 576; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 6


October 13, 1988, Argued  
January 24, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of a certain Westport town ordinance and its enabling statute, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Fuller, J.; judgment declaring the enabling statute unconstitutional, from which the named defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee landowner filed a declaratory judgment action to determine the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-147, which permitted municipalities to enact waterway protection ordinances. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) found that the statute was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority. Appellant town sought review.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned two building lots that a stream passed through or near. The town claimed that the lots were subject to Westport's Waterway Protection Lines Ordinance (WPLO), Westport Conn., Code §§ 148-1 through 148-17. The landowner requested permission to construct a single-family residence on each of his two lots, which was denied because the proposed construction was held to be inconsistent with the WPLO. The trial court did not consider the legality of the ordinance because it found that § 7-147, the enabling statute for the ordinance, lacked sufficient standards to guide municipalities in enacting waterway protection ordinances under it. On appeal, the court held that the state legislature's delegation of power to the town could be challenged on the ground that the statute was unconstitutionally vague under traditional due process analysis, but that § 7-147 protected against arbitrary and capricious action by local officials and that its language was sufficient to put an ordinary person on notice of what conduct could and could not have been engaged in under the law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 636; 553 A.2d 166; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 8

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Maiocco, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An information charging defendant with the crime of felony murder was brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) and tried to the jury. Defendant was found guilty and he appealed. The principal issue was whether defendant had established that the state discriminatorily employed a peremptory challenge to exclude a black venireman from the jury that convicted him.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court concluded that, on the record before it, defendant did not establish by a preponderance of the evidence that the state's use of a peremptory challenge to remove an individual from the venire was racially motivated. Defendant also claimed that the trial court erred in its charge to the jury as to the limited purpose of the oral prior inconsistent statements. Because defendant had failed to comply with the procedures established for preserving review of his claim regarding the jury instruction, the court declined to review it. Lastly, the court concluded that the flight instructions of the trial court did not violate any constitutional or statutory right of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error.

Cioffoletti v. Planning & Zoning Com.


No. 13403


Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 544; 552 A.2d 796; 1989 Conn. LEXIS 5


October 13, 1988, Argued  
January 10, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant commission granting with modification the plaintiffs' application for permission to expand a mining and excavation operation on certain of their property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the court, Moraghan, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed and the defendant cross appealed.

The appellants-appellees filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners sought review after the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) dismissed their appeal. Defendant zoning commission, acting as the town's inland wetlands board, had granted with modification the owners' application for permission to expand a mining and excavation operation under the Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-36 through 22a-45. The commission filed a cross appeal.


OVERVIEW: The owners applied to the commission for permission to expand their mining operation within and adjacent to existing wetlands. The commission voted to reduce substantially the area upon which they sought to excavate. The commission issued a special permit with several conditions, including a performance bond. On appeal, the owners attempted to introduce evidence as to the economic effect on their property of the commission's failure to grant their excavation permit in accordance with their application, arguing that the commission's action constituted a taking without just compensation, § 22a-43a(a). The trial court excluded the evidence and dismissed the appeal. The court dismissed the cross appeal because the commission was not aggrieved. The court found error in part as the trial court should have admitted the contested evidence. It would have been futile for the trial court to remand the case to an inland wetlands commission for the purpose of hearing evidence relevant only to the issue of an unconstitutional taking, which that agency might not have been empowered to resolve. Agencies were incompetent to decide certain constitutional issues.


OUTCOME: The court found error in part, set aside the judgment, and remanded for further proceedings. The court dismissed the cross appeal.

 

337 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Virgo v. Lyons


No. 13430


Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 497; 551 A.2d 1243; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 370


October 11, 1988, Argued  
December 27, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of, inter alia, an alleged assault and battery on the plaintiff, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Noren, J., granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff alleged victim filed suit against defendants, city and its police chief and officers, in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) for injuries sustained as a result of an alleged assault and battery. The victim claimed he was subject to a false arrest and the unjust use of force by the officers. The victim appealed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to defendants.


OVERVIEW: Defendants alleged that the doctrine of collateral estoppel prevented the victim from relitigating his claims because a prior federal court case had already adjudicated the claims. The victim argued that the compensatory and punitive damages he received in the previous federal suit were compensation only for a violation of his civil rights, and that he was entitled to litigate his tort claims in a state court action. The court held that the elements of collateral estoppel were satisfied. Both causes of action arose out of the same alleged wrongs, allegedly committed by the same defendants, and involved the same injuries. 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 provided a remedy in the form of damages for actual injuries suffered by reason of a violation of the accused's civil rights. The issue of damages for those same injuries could not be relitigated in a state tort action when they had already been decided in the § 1983 action. The jury in the federal court action was instructed in accordance with the common law rules of damages, the accused's damages were calculated in accordance with those rules, and he was compensated for the actual injuries he proved.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of defendants was affirmed.

Fazio v. Brown


No. 13434


Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 450; 551 A.2d 1227; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 372; 5 A.L.R.5th 1176


November 2, 1988, Argued  
December 27, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the named plaintiff as a result of the defendants' alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Melville, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiffs; thereafter, the named plaintiff rejected the court's additur and the court granted the named plaintiff's motion to set aside the verdict and for a new trial on damages, and the defendants appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, Borden and O'Connell, Js.; judgment affirming the trial court's decision, from which the defendants, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action, defendants, an automobile driver and the owner of the vehicle, appealed by writ of certiorari a judgment of an appellate court (Connecticut), which affirmed a trial court's order that granted a motion to set aside the jury verdict filed by plaintiffs, a motorcycle operator and his father, and ordered a new trial limited solely to the issue of damages.


OVERVIEW: The motorcycle operator was severely injured after colliding with the automobile. In a personal injury action against the automobile driver and owner, the jury returned a verdict in favor of the motorcycle operator, who filed a motion to set aside the verdict on the grounds that the amount of damages awarded by the jury was inadequate. The trial court granted the motion and ordered a new trial on the issue of damages. On appeal of the trial court's order, the appellate court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in setting aside the verdict and limiting the new trial to the issue of damages. The court agreed with the appellate court with respect to setting aside the verdict because the trial court properly found that the verdict shocked any sense of justice and was entirely disproportionate to the motorcycle operator's injury. However, the court remanded to the trial court for a trial on all issues because the issue of damages was so interwoven with the issue of liability that, in the interest of fairness, a new trial was mandated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and remanded the action to the trial court for a new trial on all the issues.

Bartlett v. Krause


No. 13358


Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 352; 551 A.2d 710; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 348


October 7, 1988, Aruged  
December 13, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant fire commissioners terminating the plaintiff from her position as fire marshal for the first fire district of the town of Redding, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the court, Ballen, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant fire commissioners appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) in favor of plaintiff fire marshal on her action alleging she was improperly discharged from her position as fire marshal without due process.


OVERVIEW: The fire marshal was terminated by the commissioners and she challenged her discharge in the superior court. That court concluded that the commissioners acted illegally, arbitrarily, and in abuse of their discretion y terminating her without written notice of the specific grounds for the dismissal and an opportunity to be heard in her defense.. This appeal followed. The commissioners argued they did not violate the fire marshal's due process rights because she had no property right to her job and, even if that right existed, they gave the fire marshal sufficient process. The court found both parties knew and expected that the fire marshal would continue her employment until she were "removed for cause" as provided by the terms of the fire marshal's appointment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-297. This created a property interest in the job for which the fire marshal was entitled to due process. Because the fire marshal was not afforded a meaningful opportunity to confront the accusations against her, and she was not given sufficient notice to challenge the findings against her, she was not given a sufficient pretermination hearing. She was thereby denied due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the fire marshal.

Daddona v. Liberty Mobile Home Sales, Inc.


No. 13467


Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 243; 550 A.2d 1061; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 333


October 6, 1988, Argued  
November 29, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the defendant's alleged violation of the state unfair trade practices act, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the defendant filed a counterclaim, and tried to the court, Meadow, J.; judgment for the plaintiff on the complaint and on the counterclaim, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant park owner appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court (Connecticut) that found in favor of plaintiff administratrix in an action alleging violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21-79 and the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq. The park owner also appealed from the denial of its counterclaim for unpaid rent.


OVERVIEW: The administratrix's decedent owned a mobile home on a lot in the park owner's park. The administratrix desired to sell the home on-site, but the park owner refused to allow such sale and offered to buy the home for a fraction of its on-site fair market value. The administratrix alleged that the park owner's refusal to permit an on-site sale violated Conn. Gen. OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the judgment in favor of the administratrix, and it vacated and remanded that portion of the judgment that had awarded punitive damages and attorney's fees to the administratrix. It also vacated and remanded the denial of the park owner's counterclaim for unpaid rent.

State v. Daniels

Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 225; 550 A.2d 885; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 331


October 4, 1988, Argued  
November 22, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder, capital felony and sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to a three judge court, Edelberg, Foti and Conway, Js.; judgment of guilty of murder, capital felony and sexual assault in the second degree, after which, pursuant to a capital sentencing hearing after a jury had failed to return a verdict in respect to the imposition of the death penalty, the trial court imposed sentence, from which the state, on the granting of permission, and the defendant appealed to this court, which remanded the matter to the trial court for further articulation on the state's appeal; on remand, the court, Edelberg, J., articulated its reasons for imposing a life sentence on the capital felony count, after which this court granted the state's motion to file supplemental briefs on its appeal and ordered further argument on both appeals.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of murder, capital felony, and sexual assault in the second degree. The court had previously remanded defendant's appeal to the trial court for a further articulation of its reasons for dismissing the death penalty phase of the proceeding and imposing the life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Two issues were before the court: First, on the state's appeal, the question was whether a death penalty proceeding must be reinstated because the trial court either lacked the discretion to impose a life sentence or abused its discretion in its exercise. Second, with regard to defendant's appeal, the question was whether the trial court violated the principles of double jeopardy in imposing two life sentences upon defendant, one for the murder of a victim and the other for the capital felony of killing of the same victim and another. The court found no error an affirmed defendant's conviction holding that the trial court did not err in imposing a life sentence, because the trial court articulated that it emphasized its exercise of discretion and its concern for the futility and expense of another trial and its adverse impact upon defendant, the victims' family, and society. The court further found that no error occurred in imposing two life sentences upon defendant, because double jeopardy did not preclude the imposition of one life sentence for each victim because the state has joined a separate count of murder to a count of capital felony.


OUTCOME: The court found no error and affirmed defendant's conviction of murder, capital felony, and sexual assault in the second degree and the imposition of a life sentence.

 

343 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Talton


No. 13367


Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 133; 547 A.2d 543; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 270


June 8, 1988, Argued  
September 13, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of manslaughter in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the state attempted to nolle the information; thereafter, the court, Ronan, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment dismissing the case without prejudice, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was changed by substitute information with the crime of manslaughter in the first degree. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), in which the state attempted to nolle the information, thereafter granted defendant's motion to dismiss. The superior court rendered judgment dismissing the case without prejudice, from which defendant appealed. At issue was whether dismissal without prejudice was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: A decision was required as to whether Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 819, which supposedly granted the option of dismissing the information either with or without prejudice, applied to defendant's demand to dismiss pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56b. Section 819 appeared under the same heading as § 815 and, as there was no other framework within which to construe § 819, it must have been construed as complementary to § 815. Section 815 contained no provision for a motion to dismiss as the proper vehicle for defendant to address the state's attempt to enter a nolle. The court concluded, therefore, that § 819, which authorized entry of a dismissal with or without prejudice in response to defendant's § 815 motion, had not applied to a § 54-56b demand for dismissal. The dismissal of a criminal prosecution in response to a § 54-56b demand was per se a dismissal with prejudice. Section 54-56b gave defendant the right to have charges disposed of with finality, which was only achieved by a dismissal with prejudice. It was the extrication of defendant from the judicial limbo to which he was exiled by the entry of a nolle prosequi or a dismissal without prejudice that was the aim of § 54-56b.


OUTCOME: As there was error, the judgment of dismissal without prejudice was set aside. The case was remanded to the superior court with direction to render a judgment of dismissal with prejudice.

State v. Dukes


No. 13246


Supreme Court of Connecticut


209 Conn. 98; 547 A.2d 10; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 267


February 10, 1988, Argued  
September 6, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the jury before Hauser, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted him of possessing narcotics with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a) and of possessing a weapon in a motor vehicle in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court violated Conn. Const. art. I, § 7 in denying his motion to suppress certain evidence taken from his person and the motor vehicle that he was operating at the time of his arrest. The court disagreed. Conn. Const. art. I, § 7 proscribed unreasonable searches and seizures; however, there was no ready test for determining reasonableness other than by balancing the need to search or seize against the invasion that the search or seizure entailed. The actions observed by the arresting officer might have had more significance to him in determining whether the law was being violated at the given place and time than they would have to a layman. The officer's experience was entitled to some weight on the ultimate question of probable cause. Here, the officer, alone at 6:30 a.m. on the interstate with defendant and his passenger, legally conducted a search of defendant's person. The search of defendant's vehicle was also proper. The discovery of contraband in defendant's pockets, coupled with all the officer knew, including the fact that he was presented with a misdemeanant, gave him probable cause to search the vehicle for contraband.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession of narcotics with intent to sell and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle.

208 Conn. 620; 546 A.2d 805; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 231

August 16, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the defendant's alleged interference with the plaintiffs' right to sell their mobile home, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, Housing Session at Waterbury, where the defendant filed a counterclaim, and tried to the court, Barnett, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs on the complaint and on the counterclaim, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners of a mobile home (owners), filed an action for injunctive relief and damages against defendant corporation, which owned the lot where the owners' mobile home was located. The owners alleged that the parties' rental agreement illegally prevented the owners from selling the mobile home while it remained on the corporation's lot. The Superior Court (Connecticut) rendered judgment for the owners and the corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court rendered judgment for the owners on the count of the complaint alleging a violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq. It also issued a permanent injunction prohibiting the corporation from interfering with the on-site sale of the owners' mobile home and ordering the corporation to restore running water to the home. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding in favor of the owners, except as to the awards for compensatory damages, punitive damages, disbursed costs, and attorney's fees, which were set aside. The case was remanded for further proceedings to determine the amount of compensatory damages to be awarded to the owners.

Norwich v. Norwalk Wilbert Vault Co.


No. 13200


Supreme Court of Connecticut


208 Conn. 1; 544 A.2d 152; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 160


March 3, 1988, Argued  
June 21, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from operating a trucking terminal on certain of its premises, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the court, Edelberg, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, Borden and Daly, Js., which affirmed the trial court's decision, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner challenged the judgment of the Connecticut Appellate Court, which upheld a decision in favor of plaintiff city and enjoined the owner from operating a trucking terminal on certain of its premises without prior site plan approval pursuant to Norwich, Conn., Zoning Ordinances § 10.2.2.


OVERVIEW: The owner increased the use of its property without prior site plan approval by the zoning commission. The trial court enjoined the increased use of the premises as a trucking terminal. The appellate court found that the owner had not been aggrieved by Norwich, Conn., Ordinances § 10.2.2 and agreed with the trial court that the owner did not exhaust available administrative remedies. The court however applied an exception to the exhaustion of remedies principle and held that the owner could defend on the ground of the general invalidity of the ordinance, without exhausting all available administrative remedies. Where the owner contested the very validity of § 10.2.2 , relief under § 10.2.2 was inadequate or futile. The owner's situation was distinguishable from a case where a landowner challenged the validity of an ordinance as applied. The court rejected the owner's argument that § 10.2.2 was unconstitutional because the city charter did not specifically confer authority to approve site plans on the commission. The court affirmed the judgment on the ground that city council's delegation of authority to the commission was proper and did not deprive the owner of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city that enjoined the owner from operating a trucking terminal on its premises without prior site plan approval.

 

350 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schriver


No. 13245


Supreme Court of Connecticut


207 Conn. 456; 542 A.2d 686; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 121


April 7, 1988, Argued  
May 17, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of risk of injury to a minor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, and tried to the jury before Dranginis, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court found the defendant in contempt and rendered judgment of guilty of risk of injury to a minor and of contempt, and the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) which convicted him of risking injury to a minor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. Defendant contended that his conviction violated his right to due process because § 53-21 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant grabbed a 13-year old girl by the waist and said, "I just want to feel you." He was convicted for risking the health of a minor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. He contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court set aside the judgment of guilty and remanded with directions to vacate the conviction. The court held that § 53-21 was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to manifest minimal guidelines by which innocent acts could be objectively and foreseeably distinguished from conduct that violated the statute. The court further held that judicial decisions did not make grabbing the waist of a fully clothed minor while uttering a sexually suggestive remark was not the type of lewd conduct prohibited by the morals clause of the statute. The court further held that case law required deliberate, blatant physical abuse to violate the health clause. Finally, the court declined to extrapolate guidelines for prosecution for impairing mental health of minors because § 53-21 provided no tangible criteria, prior cases did not add definitive gloss, and the state offered no workable standards.


OUTCOME: The remanded with direction to vacate defendant's conviction. The court held that the controlling statute was unconstitutionally vague because defendant had no reasonable opportunity to know that his conduct was prohibited by the impairment of morals clause of the statute. The court further held that defendant's conduct did not come within the physical health clause because judicial gloss limited it to instances of deliberate, blatant abuse.

 

351 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Zapata v. Burns


Nos. 13014, 13025, 13027, 13029, 13031, 13040, 13042


Supreme Court of Connecticut


207 Conn. 496; 542 A.2d 700; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 124


February 4, 1988, Argued  
May 17, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in each case, to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of a bridge collapse, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the defendant impleaded Tippetts-Abbett-McCarthy-Stratton seeking indemnification and the plaintiffs filed complaints in the alternative against the third party defendant; thereafter, the court, Cioffi, J., granted the third party defendant's motion for summary judgment on the plaintiffs' alternative complaints and rendered judgment thereon for the third party defendant, from which the plaintiffs filed separate appeals.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrators challenged a decision of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which granted defendant architectural firm summary judgment in the administrators' action for damages in connection with a bridge collapse that killed their loved ones. The trial court found that the action was barred by the statute of limitations, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584a.


OVERVIEW: The administrators argued that § 52-584a, which applied to architects and engineers, was unconstitutional. They claimed that the statute impinged on their fundamental right of access to the courts. The court noted that a constitutional right to court access did not automatically translate every claim into one invoking fundamental rights. The court employed the rational basis test, and concluded that the classification of architects and engineers in a manner different from other groups involved in the construction process had a rational relationship to a legitimate state end. With the passage of time, it was more likely that any defect was caused by improper maintenance rather than defects in design. The court found that § 52-584a did not violate Conn. Const. art. I, § 10 because at the time of the constitution's adoption, the administrators would not have been able to pursue the claims that they now maintained that the legislature unconstitutionally abrogated by enacting the statute. Thus, the administrators' causes of action for wrongful death furnished no basis for a claim of the statute's unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the architectural firm because the action was barred by the statute of limitations.

 

352 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Pet v. Department of Health Servs.


No. 13163


Supreme Court of Connecticut


207 Conn. 346; 542 A.2d 672; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 115


February 4, 1988, Argued  
May 10, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from proceeding with certain disciplinary action against the plaintiff physician, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Spada, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Health Services appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff physician's request for interlocutory injunctive relief in an administrative action brought by the department before defendant medical examining board, on the department's charges that the physician had violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-13c.


OVERVIEW: The physician was charged by the department with not providing proper psychiatric care and treatment to certain patients. A hearing was begun and then continued. During the continuance, the physician brought suit seeking a temporary injunction and broader discovery from the department. The trial court granted the request and, on appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the physician had failed to exhaust his administrative remedies and deliberately bypassed a direct appeal. Absent a showing of immediate and irreparable harm, the physician could not institute an independent action. The board's suggested schedule to hear the department's case was a reasonable one that presented no constitutional infirmity. The physician was not entitled to a right, constitutional or otherwise, to general pretrial discovery that was concomitant to that required in civil cases.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting interlocutory injunctive relief to the physician was set aside and remanded with instructions to dismiss the case for lack of jurisdiction on the grounds that the physician had failed to exhaust administrative remedies.
