State v. Taylor


No. 13211


Supreme Court of Connecticut


207 Conn. 109; 540 A.2d 64; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 92


December 10, 1987, Argued  
April 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of larceny in the third degree, twenty counts of the crime of forgery in the third degree, and eight counts of the crime of criminal impersonation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven where, after the remaining charges were nolled, the case was presented to the court, Foti, J., on pleas of guilty to one count each of larceny in the third degree, forgery in the third degree, and criminal impersonation; judgment of guilty in accordance with the pleas; thereafter, the court, Fracasse, J., granted the defendant's amended petition for habeas corpus and remanded the case for resentencing or to allow the defendant to withdraw his pleas; on remand, the court, Foti, J., imposed a new sentence from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of sentence imposed by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), on remand from a habeas court's decision granting defendant's amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus and thereby ordering the trial court to vacate the original sentence and to resentence defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to larceny in the third degree, forgery in the third degree, and criminal impersonation. The agreed upon recommendation was a sentence of no more than three years. The trial court imposed a total effective sentence of five years, suspended after two and one-half years, with probation for three years. Defendant's amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus was granted. The trial court was ordered to vacate the sentences and either to impose an effective sentence of not more than three years or to allow defendant to withdraw his pleas. The trial court, upon resentencing, vacated the sentences and imposed a total effective sentence of three years. On appeal, defendant claimed that the increase in the term of incarceration, without an articulation of the reasons for that increase, violated his due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8. The court affirmed, noting that the sentence was in accord with the remand order and holding that no realistic motive for vindictive sentencing existed. The court held that the Pearce presumption of vindictiveness did not apply and that defendant failed to prove any actual vindictiveness.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the sentence imposed by the trial court.

Nardini v. Manson


No. 13167


Supreme Court of Connecticut


207 Conn. 118; 540 A.2d 69; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 93


January 7, 1988, Argued  
April 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Satter, J.; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner appealed to the Appellate Court, Borden, Daly and Bieluch, Js., which remanded the matter to the trial court with direction to grant the petition, and the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state, sought review of the judgment of an appellate court (Connecticut), which reversed a trial court decision denying petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus and remanded the matter to the trial court with direction to grant the petition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that he had been denied effective assistance of counsel when his attorney failed to raise constitutional due process objections to the use, for impeachment purposes, of two prior felony convictions obtained when petitioner was unrepresented by counsel. The habeas court denied the petition. The appellate court reversed, having found a violation of due process, and remanded with instructions to grant the petition. Upon the court's grant of certification, the state appealed, claiming that the appellate Court should have addressed the further issue of whether the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court agreed that the dispositive issue was whether the ineffective assistance of petitioner's trial counsel affected the outcome of his case. The court held that the evidence in support of a finding that petitioner was guilty of the crimes charged was so extensive that no such effect could be shown. Therefore, the court reversed the appellate court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court. The case was remanded to that court with direction to remand the matter to the trial court to reinstate the judgment denying the petition.

Barde v. Board of Trustees


No. 13180


Supreme Court of Connecticut


207 Conn. 59; 539 A.2d 1000; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 58


January 12, 1988, Argued  
April 12, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine whether the plaintiff was entitled to the status of a tenured full professor at Manchester Community College, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Noren, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff professor sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted defendant Board of Trustee's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon in an action for declaratory judgment.


OVERVIEW: The professor filed an action for declaratory judgment against the board to determine whether he was entitled the status of tenured full professor at the community college and an increase of pay. The board moved to dismiss the action claiming that the doctrine of sovereign immunity deprived the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction. The trial court granted the motion. The trial court held that the allegations of constitutional violations were insufficient, and the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction by reason of the doctrine of sovereign immunity. On appeal, the court found no error and that the trial court correctly held that there was no subject matter jurisdiction. The court found that the unilateral expectation of benefits was not enough to create a constitutionally protected property interest within the meaning of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court held that the constitutional claims had not been established and thus the doctrine of sovereign immunity operated as a bar to subject matter jurisdiction. With respect to the monetary claim for a salary increase, the professor admittedly failed to present his claim to the commissioner of claims.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment that granted the board's motion to dismiss the declaratory action filed by the professor.

 

356 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williamson


Nos. 13248, 13249


Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 685; 539 A.2d 561; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 48


December 9, 1987, Argued  
March 29, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crime of rape, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of rape in the first degree and kidnapping in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Barber, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty in both cases, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) for rape, rape in the first degree, and kidnapping in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape based on a June incident and of rape in the first degree and kidnapping in the second degree based on an October incident. The court affirmed. Although the procedures used for the June victim's photo identification of defendant were impermissibly suggestive, the identification was reliable under the "totality of the circumstances." She had time to observe defendant during the daytime attack, she was able to describe his physical characteristics, the identification was made the morning after the attack, she identified defendant and his brother as resembling her attacker, and she identified defendant's more recent picture with absolute certainty. The October victim's testimony at the June rape trial, limited to her identification of defendant, was admissible to rebut defendant's alibi testimony that he was away from the area from May to November. The trial court was authorized to impose a sentence consecutive to that imposed by another jurisdiction. The court refused to entertain defendant's ineffective assistance claim on direct appeal. The trial court properly charged the jury on every element of the offenses, including definitions of key terms.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's convictions for rape, rape in the first degree, and kidnapping in the second degree.

Bishop v. Kelly


No. 13051


Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 608; 539 A.2d 108; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 29

March 22, 1988, Decided

Dalton; verdict for the plaintiff Elyse L. Dalton; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiff Elyse L. Dalton's motion for double or treble damages and rendered judgment for the plaintiff Elyse L. Dalton doubling the jury's award of damages, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff's motion and awarded her double damages pursuant to Conn. OVERVIEW: Defendant sought relief from the trial court's award of double damages to plaintiff, who was injured in a motor vehicle accident. The court held that Conn. Gen. The court held that § 14-295 violated the right of trial by jury afforded to defendant by Conn. Const. art. I, § 19. The court set aside the trial court's damage award.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the double damages award in favor of plaintiff and remanded the case with instructions to render a judgment against defendant in the amount of damages determined by the jury.

 

358 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Bowen v. Heintz


No. 13172


Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 636; 539 A.2d 122; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 32


January 14, 1988, Argued  
March 22, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant commissioner terminating the plaintiff's eligibility for AFDC benefits, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, M. Hennessey, J.; judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal and remanding the matter to the department of income maintenance for further proceedings, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant commissioner of income maintenance sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which reversed a decision of a hearing officer that upheld action taken by the department of income maintenance terminating plaintiff mother's eligibility for Aid to Families with Dependent Children (AFDC) benefits. The trial court remanded the matter to the department.


OVERVIEW: The mother claimed at oral argument that the case was moot because she had not been receiving AFDC benefits. The commissioner did not contest the mother's factual claim. The mother further noted her continuing obligation as the parent of an AFDC beneficiary to repay to the State the full amount of any such aid paid to or on behalf of her children under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-83e. The commissioner did not claim in opposition to the mother's claim of mootness that the case was not moot because it presented a situation that was capable of repetition, yet evaded review. Therefore, the court dismissed the appeal for mootness. The court found that the existence of an actual controversy was an essential requisite to appellate jurisdiction and that it was not the province of appellate courts to decide moot questions disconnected from the granting of actual relief or from the determination of which no practical relief could follow.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the commissioner's appeal for mootness.

 

359 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Milner


No. 12980


Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 512; 539 A.2d 80; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 41


November 3, 1987, Argued  
March 15, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before L. Dorsey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) of murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen earlier on the day of a stabbing murder with a knife, and then was seen fleeing from the scene of the murder. The court held that the trial court's refusal to allow the impeachment of a witness with charges against him for making a false statement was not error because there was no evidence that the witness was responsible for the crime and defendant was permitted to cross-examine as to the inconstancies. The court held that it was error to have admitted a police report containing an anonymous phone call as a business record; however, the error was harmless. The court held that the trial court unreasonably restricted defendant's cross-examination of a witness who identified defendant from his picture; however, the error was harmless because the identification was related to another incident and there was a great deal of evidence against defendant. The court held that defendant failed to demonstrate that another photographic identification was unduly suggestive. The court held that the prosecution's open file policy did not deprive defendant of his right to a fair trial because defendant could show no exculpatory evidence which was withheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

State v. Champagne


No. 13192


Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 421; 538 A.2d 193; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 53


January 6, 1988, Argued  
March 1, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for a restraining order prohibiting the defendant from transferring certain of his property that the state had probable cause to believe was subject to forfeiture pursuant to the state Corrupt Organizations and Racketeering Activity Act, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Jacobson, J., rendered judgment denying the defendant's motion to discharge the CORA lien filed by the state against the defendant's property, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal of an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) that prohibited him from transferring, depleting or otherwise alienating or diminishing any property subject to forfeiture to the State upon conviction of charges of knowingly engaging in a "pattern of racketeering activity" in violation of the Corrupt Organizations and Racketeering Activity Act (CORA).


OVERVIEW: The appeal called for a determination of the extent to which the State had the authority, in pretrial proceedings, to garnish mortgage payments that are the cash proceeds of alleged illegal racketeering activity. Defendant claimed principally that the trial court erred in not allowing him to use a portion of the forfeitable property to pay for attorney's fees he would incur defending the CORA prosecution. The State asserted that, as "proceeds," the mortgage payments were forfeitable under § 53-397(a) in their entirety. On appeal, the court agreed with defendant's claim for modification of the CORA lien based on the statutory exemption contained in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-398(b). The court concluded, as defendant argued, that defendant was entitled to retain a portion of the mortgage payments under § 53-398(b) because, until a final judgment of forfeiture was rendered, the interest component of each mortgage payment qualified as "net income or profits" within the exemption.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order. On remand, the trial court was directed to determine what portion of defendant's mortgage payments constituted interest and, thus, qualified for the exemption and whether the income made available to the defendant by the statute would suffice to afford him reasonable access to counsel. The court also stated that defendant had a renewed right to further interlocutory review if dissatisfied.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for an adjudication of the defendant minor as a delinquent child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Hartford, where the court, Goldstein, J., granted the state's motion to transfer the matter to the criminal docket of the Superior Court; thereafter, the state filed an information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, which was brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and presented to the court, Purtill, J., on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff state's motion to transfer the matter to the criminal docket of the superior court. The state had brought a petition for an adjudication of defendant as a delinquent child. The defendant was a minor, age 14, and charged with murder.

State v. Torres

Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 346; 538 A.2d 185; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 106

O'Connell, J., denied the defendant's motion to transfer the matter to the juvenile docket of the Superior Court; thereafter, the case was presented to the court, Purtill, J., on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which refused to transfer defendant back to the juvenile docket after the state failed to show probable cause to sustain a charge of murder, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, for which defendant had been transferred to the adult docket under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-427 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Following a hearing on probable cause, as mandated by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-127, the juvenile division of the trial court transferred defendant's case to the adult docket. The court found that there was no need to consider defendant's other claims of error.

State v. Walker


No. 13034


Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 300; 537 A.2d 1021; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 38


December 1, 1987, Argued  
February 16, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before S. Freedman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a). On appeal, defendant challenged: (1) the prosecutor's comment on his post-arrest silence; (2) the prosecutor's comments on his failure to testify; (3) the admission into evidence of photographs of the victim's body; and (4) the sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant voluntarily went to a detective bureau after the victim's body was found. Defendant received no Miranda warnings and was not under arrest. Defendant was arrested a month later. The prosecutor commented on defendant's silence at the bureau. The main prosecution witness was defendant's brother-in-law, who was in a car with defendant and the victim on the day of the murder. The court found no error with the trial court's judgment of conviction. The court determined that the prosecutor's comment violated neither state nor federal due process rights of defendant because impeachment in closing arguments by use of prearrest silence did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment. The court decided that the trial court's charge to the jury regarding the right of defendant to refrain from testifying supported a conclusion beyond a reasonable doubt that any improper prosecution comments did not contribute to the verdict. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting photographs of the victim's body. The court concluded that there was more than sufficient evidence for the jury to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of murder.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was no error with the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Schroff


No. 13081


Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 182; 536 A.2d 952; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 23


November 4, 1987, Argued  
February 2, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the jury before Corradino, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which, after a jury trial, convicted defendant of murder of a missing woman whose body was found due to information given by defendant while incarcerated on an unrelated charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was incarcerated on an unrelated charge. While in prison, defendant approached police with information pertaining to the disappearance of a woman. Prior to defendant's arrest for murder of the woman, defendant gave nine statements to police concerning the location of the body. After the discovery of the body, defendant was arrested. Defendant's motion to suppress the statements was denied as to some of the statement and granted as to others. After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of murder. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the suppression of some of the statements was proper as the interrogations contained inducements and promises from police. The court held, however, that the discovery of the body was an intervening event, which changed the character of the interaction between police and defendant such that defendant was no longer being induced to make statements in order to reveal the location of the body. The court concluded that the statements given in response to being shown photographs of the grave site was proper admissible because it was not tainted by any of the prior, induced statements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress as to certain statements.

 

365 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Ames v. Sears, Roebuck & Co.


No. 13208


Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 16; 536 A.2d 563; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 9


December 1, 1987, Argued  
January 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of the defendant's alleged negligence, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Vasington, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, Daly and Bieluch, Js., which affirmed the trial court's decision; thereafter, the trial court, Hurley, J., denied the defendant's postjudgment application for a writ of audita querela, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant judgment debtor appealed a decision in favor of plaintiff judgment creditor by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which denied the debtor's petition for a writ of audita querela in a products liability action.


OVERVIEW: The creditor was injured when he borrowed a riding lawnmower from the mower's owner. The owner and the creditor executed a release in which the creditor released the owner from any claims for $ 25,000. The creditor then obtained a judgment against the debtor for $ 175,000. The creditor lost the appeal. The debtor then claimed through the post-trial remedy of audita querela that the judgment should have been reduced by $ 25,000 to be paid by the owner, which had yet to be paid. The trial court ruled against the debtor and the appellate court refused to hear the claim because it was not raised at the first appeal. The court held that the debtor was not entitled to the offset. The court reasoned that once the trial and appeal were concluded, any other claims regarding what the debtor owed were barred. The post-trial relief of audita querela was only available for new defenses and the pre-trial settlement was not a new claim and it was raised at trial. Even where there was a change of interpretation regarding the application of pre-trial settlements to a judgment, the creditor was still not entitled to the writ of audita querela.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision against the debtor.

 

366 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Palmer


Nos. 12785, 12786, 12787


Supreme Court of Connecticut


206 Conn. 40; 536 A.2d 936; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 12


October 9, 1987, Argued  
January 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment and amended information in the first two cases, charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree with a firearm, and robbery in the first degree, and indictment and amended information in the third case charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree with a firearm, and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Nigro, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty of three counts of kidnapping in the first degree, three counts of unlawful restraint in the first degree, one count of sexual assault in the first degree, two counts of sexual assault in the first degree with a firearm, two counts of robbery in the first degree and one count of assault in the third degree, from which the defendant filed three separate appeals to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of three counts of kidnapping in the first degree, three counts of unlawful restraint in the first degree, one count of sexual assault in the first degree, two counts of sexual assault in the first degree with a firearm, two counts of robbery in the first degree, and one count of assault in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: The court found no merit to defendant's contention that the trial court erred in instructing the jury regarding intent in connection with the crime of kidnapping in the first degree. The trial court's charge to the jury clearly delineated the state's burden of proof regarding each and every element of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, including intent, and any possible confusion engendered by the challenged portion was overcome by other instructions. The court further found that defendant could have committed the crime of kidnapping in the first degree in each case without having first committed the lesser-included offense of unlawful restraint in the first degree. Thus, there was no violation of the double jeopardy clause and no error in the trial court's imposition of consecutive sentences for each of the distinct offenses. Finally, the court found that pre-arrest, pre-arraignment, general conversations engaged in by the police and defendant in connection with voice identifications by the victims did not implicate defendant's right to counsel under the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Kevin Roche-John Dinkeloo & Associates v. New Haven


No. 12816


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 741; 535 A.2d 1287; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 1


November 12, 1987, Argued  
January 12, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for breach of contract, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Mancini, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to cite in the New Haven Coliseum Authority as a party defendant; thereafter, the court, Zoarski, J., granted the named defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered a partial judgment thereon; the case was tried to the jury before Zoarski, J., as against the defendant New Haven Coliseum Authority, which had filed a counterclaim; directed verdict and judgment for the defendant on the complaint, directed verdict and judgment for the plaintiff on the first count of the counterclaim and verdict and judgment for the plaintiff on the second count of the counterclaim, from which the defendant New Haven Coliseum Authority appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant coliseum authority sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which directed verdict and judgment for plaintiff architectural firm for counts one and two on a counterclaim alleging breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in its instruction to the jury with respect to plaintiff's expert witness in that the trial court purported to summarize the evidence presented by the expert witness, thereby unfairly emphasizing the testimony of the witness. Although the court agreed that the trial court's commentary focused in greater detail on the testimony of plaintiff's expert witness, the court held that the comments were not unfair. The trial court first summarized the testimony of one of defendant's experts before summarizing six of plaintiff's experts. The court held that although a more balanced presentation of the evidence might have resulted had the trial court summarized the testimony of defendant's two other witnesses, the charge was not invalidated. The trial judge also gave numerous cautionary instructions to the jury to consider all of the evidence, not just that which had been summarized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Adolphson v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


No. 13131


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 703; 535 A.2d 799; 1988 Conn. LEXIS 7


October 6, 1987, Argued  
January 5, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant board which granted an application for variances and a special permit filed by the defendants Michael A. Brunetto et al., brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and referred to Hon. Milton J. Herman, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal from a decision by defendant town zoning board that granted an application for variances and a special permit filed by defendant property owners.


OVERVIEW: Both plaintiff's and defendants' properties were located in an industrial district 1 zone. The prior owners of defendants' property used it for the operation of an aluminum casting foundry, a nonconforming use. Defendants intended using it as an automobile repair shop. Defendants filed an application with the board for three variances and a special exception. The board granted the application, and the trial court affirmed. Plaintiff argued that the trial court erred in upholding the board's grant of defendants' application for a variance to Town of Fairfield, Conn., Zoning Regulations § 19.4.6. He asserted that variances should not have been used to accomplish what was, in effect, a substantial change in the uses permitted in the specified zone. The court held that the board's action in granting defendants permission to operate an automobile repair shop, a prohibited activity in an industrial district 1 zone, was consistent with the board's variance power under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6(3) and did not constitute a usurpation of the function of the planning and zoning commission.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the dismissal of plaintiff's appeal.

State v. Price


No. 13054


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 616; 534 A.2d 1196; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 1076


November 3, 1987, Argued  
December 29, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder and murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Kline, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which entered a conviction against him for felony murder, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-54c. Defendant argued that the district court made numerous errors in its jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after borrowing a gun from a friend, defendant approached the victim and shot him in the left temple. After the victim fell to the ground, defendant searched the victim's pockets. As a result, defendant was convicted of felony murder. On appeal, defendant argued that the district court erred in its jury instructions concerning the strong corroboration element of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-49(b), an essential element of the attempted robbery theory of felony murder, and the intent element of felony murder. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. Specifically, the court held that the district court's instruction regarding examples of conduct that were strongly corroborative of the actor's criminal purpose in a substantial step was technically inaccurate, however, the error was harmless where the district court clearly explained the corroboration principle of attempted robbery before and after the misstatement. Finally, the court found that it was not error for the district court to instruct the jury that it had the prerogative to draw inferences that were "reasonable and logical" where it was made clear that the jury was not required to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Gonzalez


No. 12884


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 673; 535 A.2d 345; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 1079


November 3, 1987, Argued  
December 29, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of attempted robbery in the first degree, three counts of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree with a firearm, and three counts of the crime of attempted assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Purtill, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him of one count of attempted robbery in the first degree, three counts of kidnapping in the first degree with a firearm, and three counts of attempted assault in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly entered a store brandishing a gun, ordered the employees to open a safe while threatening them with his gun, and fought with them when they attacked. Defendant was determined incompetent to stand trial, but that determination was reversed at a second hearing. Defendant was excluded from the courtroom after numerous disruptive outbursts, but he was found still competent at a third competency hearing held after he attempted suicide and was prescribed an antipsychotic drug. The court held that the trial court properly refused to permit defendant to discharge his attorney because he did not make a sustained effort to discharge and did not offer a substantial reason for the appointment of new counsel. The trial court undertook a proper independent judicial inquiry when it ordered the third competency examination and did not err in excluding defendant from the courtroom because of his disruptive behavior. Although the trial court erred in using "more probable than not" language in its instruction regarding the inferences the jury could draw from circumstantial evidence, the error was harmless and not misleading as to the State's burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's judgment of conviction and the sentence imposed thereon.

 

371 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Scheyd v. Bezrucik


No. 13299


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 495; 535 A.2d 793; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 1064


November 24, 1987, Argued  
December 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action pursuant to statute to direct the respondent town clerk to declare the petitioners to have been elected to the office of alderman at large for the city of New Britain, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, where the court, Spada, J., pursuant to a stipulation of facts by the parties, certified for the expedited review of this court its decision on a number of questions of law including, inter alia, the constitutionality of the state statute requiring minority representation on local legislative bodies.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to direct the respondent town clerk to declare petitioners to have been elected to the office of alderman for the City of New Britain, the Superior Court of the Hartford-New Britain Judicial District (Connecticut) certified, for expedited review, its decision on certain questions of law, including the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-167a, the state statute requiring minority representation on local legislative bodies.


OVERVIEW: The dispositive issue in this case is whether a challenge to the constitutionality of the state's minority representation statute, came within the jurisdictional confines of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-328 which, under narrowly defined circumstances, provided expedited judicial procedures for the resolution of election disputes. The case arose out of a municipal election for aldermen at large. The trial court concluded that it had jurisdiction to proceed § 9-328, but determined that, on the merits, the petitioners could not prevail. The court remanded the case for dismissal without reaching the merits. Absent an allegation of a violation of a specific election statute, § 9-328 only applied when an elector or a candidate claimed to have been aggrieved by any ruling of any election official in connection with an election for any municipal office or that there was a mistake in the count of votes. The outcome of the election was governed by the minority representation statute and for purposes of § 9-328 it didn't matter how the municipality decided to allocate the permissible number of alderman to any one political party. The town clerk, in this case, did not make a § 9-328 "ruling."


OUTCOME: There was error in the trial court's decision to entertain this action and the case was remanded with direction to dismiss the complaint.

State v. Laracuente


No. 13165


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 515; 534 A.2d 882; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 1066


October 9, 1987, Argued  
December 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of impairing the morals of a child and sexual assault in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Ronan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument en banc which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of risk of injury to a child by doing an act likely to impair her morals under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 and of sexual assault in the fourth degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-73a(a)(1)(A).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of fondling the genitals of a six-year-old girl, who was his girlfriend's daughter, while she slept. Defendant was convicted violating Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-21, 53a-73a(a)(1)(A). The court found no error in the convictions. The court held that defendant's potential alibi defense did not create a per se requirement that the State limit the times in the information more narrowly than the available evidence warranted. The court found that the fact that defendant might have offered an alibi defense was a factor to be considered by the trial court in deciding whether to grant his motion for a bill of particulars setting forth a specific date or dates of the occurrence. The court held that it was not necessary for a conviction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 for the State to prove the child's awareness of the act. The court concluded that it was within the jury's province to draw reasonable inferences from proven facts that it was likely that the child would waken fully or partially during the act with resultant impairment of her morals. The court found that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of risk of injury to a child by doing an act likely to impair her morals and of sexual assault in the fourth degree.

State v. Williams


No. 13063


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 456; 534 A.2d 230; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 1061


September 30, 1987, Argued  
December 8, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the second degree and interfering with an officer by resistance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the court, Falsey, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which found him guilty of burglary in the second degree, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-102, and interfering with an officer by resisting arrest, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a.


OVERVIEW: The victim agreed to buy a tape player from defendant. Defendant accompanied the victim to her home where she retrieved money to pay him. Later that night the victim awoke and found an intruder in her home. Two officers stopped defendant on the street because he matched the description of the intruder. Defendant began to loudly object to an officer's order not to leave the immediate area. Defendant was arrested for breach of peace. The victim went to the police station and identified defendant as the intruder, and the following day, the victim realized that defendant had also sold her the tape player. On appeal, defendant's convictions were upheld. The evidence amply supported the conclusion that defendant knowingly and intelligently waived his right to trial by jury. Defendant physically resisted arrest. Section 53a-167a was not unconstitutionally vague, and it limited the criminal conduct to conduct that amounted to meddling in or hampering with the activities of the police in the performance of their duties. Although defendant received his presentence investigation report late, there was no actual prejudice to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the third degree, sexual assault in the third degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, and tried to the jury before Licari, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, Spallone and Bieluch, Js., which set aside the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision from the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which set aside a judgment from the trial court that convicted defendant of assault in the third degree, sexual assault in the third degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of assault in the third degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-61, sexual assault in the third degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-72a, and unlawful restraint in the first degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-95. Defendant asserted that the jury instruction on circumstantial evidence misled the jury in its application of the evidence. The court reversed the decision that set aside the conviction and remanded with directions to reinstate the judgment because it determined that while the jury instruction was erroneous; the error was harmless because of the substantial direct evidence that supported every element necessary to prove the crimes.

Stroiney v. Crescent Lake Tax Dist.


No. 13141


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 290; 533 A.2d 208; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 1048


October 6, 1987, Argued  
November 17, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the validity of the creation of the defendant tax district within the town of Enfield, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Quinn, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the defendants appealed to this court, which dismissed the appeal; the Superior Court, Aronson, J., thereafter granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which awarded summary judgment in favor of appellee tax district in the taxpayers' action for declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the validity of the creation of the tax district within their town.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that the tax district was a de facto municipal corporation and thus, its validity could be challenged only by the state in a quo warranto proceeding and not by private parties. Thus, the trial court held that the taxpayers had no standing to bring their action. On appeal, the court found that the requirements to establish a de facto municipal corporation were: (1) a charter or general law under which such a corporation as it purports to be might lawfully be organized; (2) an attempt in good faith to organize thereunder; and (3) an actual user of the corporate franchise. The taxpayers contended that no de facto municipal corporation existed because the tax district failed to circulate organizing petitions that complied with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-9. In upholding the trial court's decision, the court found that the taxpayers failed to claim in their complaint that, for the first eight months of its existence, the tax district acted in anything other than good faith.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court which granted the tax district's motion for summary judgment.

Ecker v. West Hartford


No. 12971


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 219; 530 A.2d 1056; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 1001


May 6, 1987, Argued  
September 8, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the plaintiff's decedent as a result of the defendants' alleged negligence, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before Geen, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff against the named defendant et al., from which the named defendant et al. appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and city building inspector, sought review of a judgment entered in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), which awarded damages under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555 to plaintiff estate administratrix for fatal injuries sustained by decedent when he was struck by a wooden canopy that fell from a building.


OVERVIEW: The decedent of plaintiff estate administratrix was killed when he was struck by a wooden canopy that fell from a building. Plaintiff brought a wrongful death action under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555 against defendants, city and city building inspector, and other parties. During the first day of trial, defendants for the first time requested the trial court to dismiss the action on grounds that it was barred by the three-year time limitation in § 52-555. After the trial court denied defendants' request, the jury rendered a verdict in favor of plaintiff, and the court entered judgment. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court held that plaintiff failed to satisfy the limitations period in § 52-555, which was a jurisdictional prerequisite that could not be waived. The court further held that § 52-555 did not violate Conn. Const. art. I, § 10 because the statute's repose period did not abrogate rights that existed when that provision of the Connecticut constitution was adopted and because the limitations period was rationally related to the state's interest in promoting the prompt settlement of the economic and legal affairs of deceased individuals.


OUTCOME: The court set the judgment aside and the case was remanded to the trial court with direction to render judgment dismissing the action.

State v. Pollitt


No. 12431


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 132; 531 A.2d 125; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 997


June 10, 1987, Argued  
September 1, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Mulvey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings to determine whether the state had suppressed certain evidence favorable and material to the defendant; on remand, the court, Hadden, J., resolved the issue in favor of the state.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court, New Haven (Connecticut), which, based on a jury verdict, convicted him of kidnapping in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree. On remand, the superior court was instructed to determine whether the State had suppressed certain evidence favorable and material to defendant. The superior court resolved the issue in favor of the State.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction of kidnapping in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree. The court held that there was no prejudicial error which required the reversal of the conviction. The court concluded: (1) that the trial court did not err in finding and concluding that the State had not suppressed Brady material that was favorable and material to defendant because, in light of the totality of the evidence presented at trial, there was no reasonable probability that had the statement of the unavailable witness been disclosed, the outcome of the trial would have been different; (2) that there was no error in the charge on the elements of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and there was no reasonable probability that the jury was misled; (3) that the trial court did not err in failing to adequately instruct the jury on the dangers of eyewitness identification; (4) that the trial court's comment on the evidence did not amount to reversible error because the comments neither advised or directed the jury how to decide the case; and (5) that, based on the totality of the circumstances the victim's identifications were reliable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of kidnapping in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree.

American Universal Ins. Co. v. DelGreco


No. 13067


Supreme Court of Connecticut


205 Conn. 178; 530 A.2d 171; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 999


June 11, 1987, Argued  
September 1, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to vacate an arbitration award, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the defendant filed an application to confirm the award, and tried to the court, D. Dorsey, J.; judgment confirming the award, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurance company filed an application with the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) to vacate an arbitration award granted in favor of defendant, the administrator of decedent's estate. The trial court upheld the arbitration award, ruling that the insurance company could not setoff the award under Conn. Agencies Regs. § 38-175a-6(d). The insurance company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The administrator of decedent's estate pursued a claim under the Dram Shop Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-102, against a restaurant that served liquor to an individual who was involved in an automobile accident that resulted in the decedent's death. The administrator filed a claim for the underinsured motorist benefits under the decedent's policy. The setoff provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38-175c (b)(1) did not apply to a dram shop policy because it was not classified as automobile coverage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court upholding the arbitrators' award in favor of the administrator of decedent's estate.

Stat. § 53a-111, after a trial to the court, and sentence of 10 years imprisonment. He claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress a statement he made while in custody and in denying his motion to suppress clothing seized from him while in custody.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for breach of the peace and released on a written promise to appear. 380 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State Management Asso. v. O'Neill


No. 12978


Supreme Court of Connecticut


204 Conn. 746; 529 A.2d 1276; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 972


May 14, 1987, Argued  
August 11, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of a certain statute which allegedly deprives the plaintiff state managerial employees of, inter alia, the right to bargain collectively with the state, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Satter, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, state managerial employees, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which entered judgment in favor of defendant, State and others, in the employees' action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the State Employees' Relations Act (SERA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-270(b), (g).


OVERVIEW: The employees sought to determine whether § 5-270(b), (g) were unconstitutional because they denied to those state employees who were designated as "managerial employees" or "managers" the right to union representation and the right to bargain collectively with the State concerning the terms and conditions of their employment. The trial court entered judgment for the State. On appeal, the court found no error. Since the legislation involved did not create a suspect classification, the employees had to establish that the statutory classification was without a rational basis in order to successfully challenge it on equal protection grounds. The trial court properly found that the classification of managerial employees under § 5-270 and the denial to them of collective bargaining rights under the SERA bore a rational relationship to the legitimate state end of ensuring that the State had the undivided loyalty of its top level personnel acting on its behalf. Further, the statute was not void for vagueness because the classification system, which was based upon characterizing the principal functions of employees, was sufficiently clear and explicit.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the decision of the trial court, which entered judgment in favor of the State in the employees' action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of SERA, which allegedly deprived the employees of the right to bargain collectively with the State.

State v. Boscarino


Nos. 12667, 12684


Supreme Court of Connecticut


204 Conn. 714; 529 A.2d 1260; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 971


June 9, 1987, Argued  
August 11, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with one count of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, one count of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree and three counts of the crime of assault in the second degree, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with one count of the crime of burglary in the first degree and three counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Wagner, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty in each case, from which the defendant filed separate appeals to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trials.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision in the Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree and three counts of the crime of assault in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by information that arose from four factually similar, but legally unrelated cases. Defendant was tried jointly on two indictments, and was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree, assault in the second degree, burglary in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree. Defendant appealed his conviction on grounds that the court abused its discretion in permitting defendant to be tried jointly on the charges that arose from the unrelated cases. On appeal, the court reversed because the denial of severance of trials resulted in substantial injustice to defendant, and the resulting prejudice was beyond the curative power of the court's instruction. In addition, the court held that a curative instruction was not inevitably sufficient to overcome the prejudicial impact of inadmissible "other crimes" evidence. Finally, the court held that if the procedures used to identify a defendant were not unnecessarily suggestive, a court needed not independently analyze whether the identification was reliable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and ordered a new trial.

State v. Mayette


No. 12930


Supreme Court of Connecticut


204 Conn. 571; 529 A.2d 673; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 942


June 9, 1987, Argued  
August 4, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number thirteen, and tried to the jury before Wagner, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70. He was sentenced to a term of imprisonment of eleven years, execution of which was suspended after five years, and placed on probation for four years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in granting the State's motion in limine, which precluded him from calling witnesses to testify as to a third party's declarations against penal interest, which were exculpatory to defendant. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that the declarant's statements were not trustworthy. The statements were made approximately three weeks after the crime and were not made to confidants in whom he would be expected to repose trust. There was also insufficient corroborating evidence as to the statements' truthfulness. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the out-of-court photo identifications by the victim and by a witness. The court held that the identification procedure was not unnecessarily suggestive, under the totality of the circumstances. Finally, defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion for judgment of acquittal. Reviewing the evidence as set forth above in the light most favorable to sustaining the jury's verdict, the verdict was one that jurors could reasonably have reached.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual assault in the first degree, finding no errors.

Liscio v. Liscio


No. 13135


Supreme Court of Connecticut


204 Conn. 502; 528 A.2d 1143; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 936

July 28, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to set aside a conveyance of real property as having been procured by undue influence and for the impression of a resulting and constructive trust on the defendant's interest in certain real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Hon. Michael J. Sicilian, state trial referee; verdict and judgment for the defendant from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; new trial as to the first count.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an administratrix, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court (Connecticut), which rendered a verdict and judgment in favor of defendant, a beneficiary, in an action to set aside a conveyance of real property as having been procured by undue influence and for the impression of a resulting and constructive trust on the beneficiary's interest in certain real property.


OVERVIEW: The administratrix of a decedent's estate alleged that the beneficiary obtained a quitclaim deed of certain real property from the decedent through undue influence. The administratrix also claimed that the deceased had paid the purchase price for the property and claimed the impression of a resulting and constructive trust. In a charge to the jury, the superior court directed a verdict in favor of the beneficiary on the count of undue influence. On the second count, the superior court returned a verdict for the beneficiary and found that an earlier quitclaim deed in the decedent's chain of title executed by only one of two joint tenants was a nullity, and could not act to sever a joint tenancy. The administratrix appealed. On review, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court reversed the directed verdict in favor of the beneficiary on the count of undue influence because the superior court's erroneous instruction concerning effect of the quitclaim deed foreclosed jury from considering the issue of undue influence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part the verdict in favor of the beneficiary on the count of undue influence and ordered a new trial. The court affirmed in part the judgment in favor of the beneficiary on the second count pertaining to the impression of a resulting and constructive trust.

 

384 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hernandez


No. 12526


Supreme Court of Connecticut


204 Conn. 377; 528 A.2d 794; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 925


April 1, 1987, Argued  
July 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of felony murder, and amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of arson in the first degree and burglary in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Higgins, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of arson in the first degree and burglary in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Although the trial court erred when it refused allow inquiries on voir dire as to the credibility of fire officials police officers, such error was harmless because the credibility of such persons was never called into question during trial. Although their testimony was important with respect to the circumstances surrounding the incident and to the results of their respective investigations, defendant was linked to the crime by his own detailed, written confession, and by the testimony of a third party lay witness. The voluntariness of the confession was a question of law that the trial court decided prior to trial. The trial court did not err in excluding the hearsay confession of a third party, which statement was sought to be introduced through an in-court witness. Although the trial court improperly determined that the credibility of the in-court witness was questionable, such was harmless because the trial court also determined that the hearsay statement was untrustworthy. Specifically, the statement was not corroborated by other evidence and there was no close, confidential relationship between the declarant and the witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. White


No. 12749


Supreme Court of Connecticut


204 Conn. 410; 528 A.2d 811; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 927


February 3, 1987, Argued  
July 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with three counts of criminally negligent homicide and three counts of violation of the state fire code, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, and tried to the jury before McDonald, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a jury verdict of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him of three counts of criminally negligent homicide in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-58, 53a-3(14), and with three counts of failing to provide a smoke detector in violation of Connecticut State Fire Safety Code §§ 11-1.8.1, 11-3.3.3.1 and Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 29-292, 29-295.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminally negligent homicide and failing to provide a smoke detector after occupants of a residential building he owned died in a fire in the building. Defendant appealed his convictions on several grounds. The appellate court held (1) the state fire safety code provisions and applicable statutes were not unconstitutionally vague because they enabled a person of ordinary intelligence to know what was permitted and what was prohibited, (2) the fire safety code regulations exceeded the scope of authority conferred on them by § 29-292 because the purpose of the statute was to give the fire marshal the ability to enact reasonable minimum requirements for safety in new and existing buildings, and (3) liability based on criminal negligence presupposed a duty to act or refrain from acting and defendant had no duty to install smoke detectors in his building because no building permit was issued for the building on or after the effective date of § 29-292.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was set aside, and the case was remanded to the trial court with an order to grant the defendant's motion for acquittal on all counts.

State v. Andrews


No. 13069


Supreme Court of Connecticut


204 Conn. 429; 528 A.2d 361; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 928


February 3, 1987, Argued  
July 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with eight counts of criminally negligent homicide and three counts of violation of the state fire code, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, and tried to the court, Licari, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of criminally negligent homicide, failing to install smoke detectors, and violation of the state fire code. Defendant claimed that the state fire safety code's enabling act was unconstitutionally vague and that the State could not prove that he was guilty of criminally negligent homicide as a matter of law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned a three story apartment building that caught fire when discarded smoking materials smoldered and then ignited. Eight occupants of the apartment building perished in the fire. The apartment building was not equipped with smoke detectors. Occupants who survived the fire stated that had they been alerted to the fire earlier, they would have been able to lead other occupants to safety. There was no evidence introduced at trial that a building permit was issued for defendant's building on or after October 1, 1976. Defendant was convicted of criminally negligent homicide in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-58, failing to install smoke detectors in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-292 (1985) and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-295, and violation of the state fire code. In reversing on appeal, the court held that it found error based upon a decision decided on the same date as the instant case, which held that fire safety code regulations exceeded the authority of their enabling statute where the enabling statute required that smoke detectors be installed only in those buildings for which a building permit was issued on or after October 1, 1976.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision from the trial court, which convicted defendant of criminally negligent homicide, failing to install smoke detectors, and violation of the state fire code. The court remanded the case, directing the trial court to render a judgment of not guilty.

Phelps Dodge Copper Prods. Co. v. Groppo


No. 13007


Supreme Court of Connecticut


204 Conn. 122; 527 A.2d 672; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 906


March 3, 1987, Argued  
June 16, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the defendant commissioner's assessment of a sales and use tax deficiency against the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, A. Aronson, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved the question of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; thereafter, the reservation was transferred to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the assessment by defendant Commissioner of Revenue Service of a sale and use tax deficiency against the taxpayer. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) reserved a question of law that was transferred to the court. The question focused on the validity of a regulation that interpreted Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-412(34).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer installed a new production line at its copper plant. It purchased the components for the new line from various sources, although all the components were purchased at the same time, and they were all required to complete the new line. The Commissioner, applying Conn. Agencies Regs. § 12-426-11b(c)(1), assessed tax on all components that were not purchased from the same vendor as the basic machinery. The question posed by the lower court was whether a component part of a machine would have to constitute a machine in and of itself or be purchased in conjunction with a machine in order to be exempt from the Connecticut sales and use tax pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-412(34). The taxpayer argued that such an interpretation of the statute frustrated the legislative purpose behind the statute. The court disagreed, holding that the regulation validly limited the exemption to components purchased at the same time and from the same vendor as the basic machinery. The court reasoned that the regulation had been approved by a committee of Connecticut's legislature, was consistent with the language of the statute, and did not contravene the legislative intent behind the statute.


OUTCOME: The court answered the question by finding that the regulation was valid.

 

388 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Heintz


No. 13012


Supreme Court of Connecticut


204 Conn. 17; 526 A.2d 1318; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 892


March 5, 1987, Argued  
June 9, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from enforcing or executing restrictions on payment for abortions for patients eligible for state medical assistance, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Berdon, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs; thereafter, the court granted in part the plaintiffs' motion for costs and attorneys' fees and rendered a supplemental judgment awarding the named plaintiff et al. costs and attorneys' fees, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patients filed a declaratory judgment action to invalidate a regulation issue by defendant commissioner which conditioned funding for abortions on a determination by a physician that the abortion was necessary to save the patient's life. After invalidating the regulation, the Superior Court (Connecticut) entered a supplemental judgment awarding the patients attorney fees and costs. The commissioner appealed the supplemental judgment.


OVERVIEW: The state claimed that the award violated the sovereign immunity of the state, was not authorized by any statute, and was contrary to the established precedent that, in the absence of a special agreement or an applicable statute, each litigant had to bear his own legal expenses. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court found that there was no statutory nor court-authored basis for awarding attorney fees to the patients. Neither the private attorney general nor the substantial benefit rule applied because the determination of whether a public policy was vindicated was better left to the legislature, and the award against the state would result in all taxpayers, not just those benefitting from the judgment, paying for the costs. The court held that the patients' claims for attorneys' fees incurred in obtaining necessary health related benefits erroneously denied to them by state officials fell within the jurisdiction of the claims commissioner, as set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-142, to hear and determine all claims against the state. The patients' failure to pursue this administrative remedy precluded an adjudication of the constitutional claim they raised.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the supplemental judgment and remanded to the trial court with direction to render judgment dismissing the claim for attorney fees and costs.
