State v. Rollinson


No. 12814


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 641; 526 A.2d 1283; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 862


April 8, 1987, Argued  
June 2, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before J. Healey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by jury in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut) of having committed the crime of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a. Defendant sought appellate review of his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. On appeal, he challenged the validity of the information charging him, and the admissibility at his trial of inculpatory statements made while he was a patient in a hospital alcohol detoxification unit. Defendant also alleged that the trial court improperly instructed the jury, and that it erred in denying his motion for acquittal. Although defendant was charged by information rather than indicted by a grand jury, the court found that the crime itself predated the effective date of the information charging statute, and that his prosecution was governed retrospectively by the new statutory procedures. The court held that defendant's challenge to the statute as an ex post facto law was without merit. The court found that the change from indictment to information did not so disadvantage defendant as to require the dismissal of the charges against him. The court also held that defendant's inculpatory statements made in a noncustodial setting were not privileged under federal or state law and were therefore admissible. The court held that the jury instructions were adequate and accurate. The court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and held that the trial court did not err in its rulings or instructions.

State v. Proto


Nos. 12740, 12842


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 682; 526 A.2d 1297; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 865


April 1, 1987, Argued  
June 2, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information, in the first case, charging the defendant with nine counts of election law crimes and three counts of the crime of larceny in the sixth degree, and information, in the second case, charging the defendant with four counts of election law crimes, three counts of the crime of larceny in the sixth degree and one count of the crime of larceny in the fifth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Norcott, J., granted, in each case, the defendant's motion to dismiss with prejudice the election law violation charges, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed and the defendant in the first case cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of judgments of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted defendants' motions to dismiss charges of election law crimes on the grounds that the provisions of the Campaign Financing Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 9-333-9-348dd, were unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with election law crimes in violation of the Campaign Financing Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 9-333-9-348dd. The trial court granted defendants' motions to dismiss on the grounds that the provisions of the Act were unconstitutionally vague. U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV protect the rights of political expression and association. The court held that legislative restriction on such rights, like those imposed by the Act, were permissible only if the state demonstrated a sufficiently important interest and employed means closely drawn to avoid unnecessary abridgement of associational freedoms. The court held that there was a distinction made by the U.S. Supreme Court between the regulation of contributions, which was permissible, and the regulation of expenditures, which was not permissible. The court held that the Act was not unconstitutionally vague because it was sufficiently definite to enable a person to know what conduct he had to avoid. The court held that the trial court erred in determining that the Act was vague. The court reversed and remanded judgments of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a judgment of the trial court, which granted defendants' motions to dismiss election law charges on the grounds that the Campaign Financing Act (Act) was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the Act differentiated between the regulation of contributions and expenditures and that it was sufficiently definite to enable defendants to know what conduct to avoid.

French v. Amalgamated Local Union 376, UAW


No. 13059


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 624; 526 A.2d 861; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 861; 125 L.R.R.M. 2709


March 11, 1987, Argued  
June 2, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from picketing outside the residence of the plaintiff, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Kelly, J.; order for temporary injunction for violation of General Statutes § 31-120, from which the defendants appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; temporary injunction dissolved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a president of a company, brought an action in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut) to enjoin defendants, a union and other affiliated labor organizations, from continuing to picket on a street in front of the president's residence. A temporary injunction for violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-120 was granted. Defendants appealed, the president cross-appealed, and the case was transferred.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that § 31-120, which banned all residential picketing except labor picketing conducted at a residence located at the situs of a labor dispute, was unconstitutional because it violated the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution. The court agreed and held that § 31-120, on its face, was unconstitutional. The court found that § 31-120 was virtually identical to an Illinois statute declared unconstitutional by the United States Supreme Court. By banning all residential picketing that did not relate to an ongoing labor dispute, the court found that § 31-120, like the Illinois statute, stifled the very debate on issues of public concern that the First Amendment was intended to promote. The court found that § 31-120 discriminated among speech-related activities in a public forum and that the residential privacy rationale was an insufficient justification for the content-based distinction between labor and nonlabor picketing. The court considered whether an alternate construction of § 31-120 would save it from constitutional demise, but found none.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the order of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to dissolve the temporary injunction.

Huck v. Inland Wetlands & Watercourses Agency


No. 12876


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 525; 525 A.2d 940; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 859


January 15, 1987, Argued  
May 19, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant agency which denied the plaintiff's application to construct a house and septic system on her property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Bingham, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wetland agency appealed from a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff property owner's appeal of defendant's denial of plaintiff's application to construct a house and septic system on her property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owner appealed defendant wetland agency's decision, which denied her application to residentially construct upon her wetland property. The trial court reversed and found that plaintiff had been deprived by defendant of the reasonable and proper use of her property and that there had been an unconstitutional taking without just compensation. Defendant appealed, and the court reversed, holding the failure of plaintiff's application to garner enough votes for its approval amounted to a rejection of the application and constituted "action" by defendant within the 65 day period required. Therefore, defendant did not fail to take "action" within 65 days of the public hearing. The court concluded that the record contained substantial evidence to support defendant's reason for denying the application, and there was substantial evidence to support the denial. Defendant did not "whimsically ignore substantial expert testimony," nor was its action the result of the prejudicial desire of defendant to have plaintiff's land remain in a natural state. Defendant did not act arbitrarily on its own experience nor in disregard of contrary expert evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court decision, which had reversed defendant agency's decision denying plaintiff property owner's application to residentially construct upon her property. The court found error in the trial court's conclusion that defendant did not give "reasons" for its decision, and it concluded that there was substantial evidence to support defendant's denial.

Smith v. Planning & Zoning Bd.


Nos. 12768, 12872


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 317; 524 A.2d 1128; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 837


December 5, 1986, Argued  
April 28, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision of the named defendant changing the name of a Milford street, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the court, Kulawiz, J., rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, Hull and Spallone, Js.; judgment setting aside the trial court's decision and remanding the case for further proceedings, from which the defendants, on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city planning and zoning board and a corporate remainderman, sought review of a judgment from the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which held that plaintiff life tenant was a "person owning land" for purposes of Conn. OVERVIEW: The zoning board granted an application of the corporate remainderman to change the name of a street abutting its property. The life tenant, claiming to be aggrieved, appealed the zoning board's decision to the trial court. The appellate court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The zoning board and the remainderman were granted permission to appeal by certification. On appeal, the court held, in affirming the appellate court's judgment, that the life tenant had an interest in the land sufficient to entitle her to the benefit of the automatic appeal for landowners set forth in § 8-8. Therefore, the life tenant was not required to prove aggrievement.

Manchester Sand & Gravel Co. v. South Windsor


No. 12811


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 267; 524 A.2d 621; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 833


December 9, 1986, Argued  
April 21, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from enforcing its ordinance which prohibited truck traffic on certain roads in the town of South Windsor, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Bieluch, J., granted the motion to intervene as party plaintiff filed by the city of New Britain; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, which rendered judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town appealed a permanent injunction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) barring it from enforcing a town ordinance that prohibited trucks with a gross vehicle weight (gvw) in excess of 15,000 pounds from traveling over certain roads. Plaintiff gravel company was joined by two intervening neighboring towns.


OVERVIEW: The gravel company and the refuse carrier for one of the intervening towns complained that any alternate routes they were forced to travel, if their trucks were prohibited from using their normal routes through the town, were circuitous and would cost them time and money. The town contended that its ordinance was not an attempt to regulate through trucks because it applied to all trucks in excess of 15,000 pounds, whether through or intratown, and that the ordinance was a reasonable regulation to promote safety and to prevent deterioration of town streets. A review of the transcript of the hearing, however, made it clear that the principal target of the ordinance was gravel and refuse truck traffic. The court held that the ordinance was invalid because it constituted a regulation of through truck traffic, a function reserved to the state traffic commission by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-298. The ordinance, which had the effect of regulating through truck traffic by imposing a locally determined weight limit, was invalid.


OUTCOME: The injunction granted to the gravel company and intervening towns was affirmed.

State v. Williams


No. 13023


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 159; 523 A.2d 1284; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 827


February 10, 1987, Argued  
April 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the New Haven District Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53(a)-134(a)(3) and burglary in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53(a)-101(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: The victim was entering an apartment when defendant followed her inside, brandished a knife, and stole the victim's pocketbook. The victim identified defendant from an array of photos and in court. At trial, there was an issue over whether defense counsel should have proceeded after it was discovered that a "lookalike" suspect was also a client of the public defender's office. Defendant asserted that the trial court committed numerous errors. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court stated that a pre-trial photographic array was not unduly suggestive because the victim observed hundreds of photos before identifying defendant and defendant failed to show that the identification procedure violated his constitutional rights. The court concluded that the trial court did not err in allowing certain officer testimony over objection because the testimony was limited for a specific purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Cubano


No. 12889


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 81; 523 A.2d 495; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 820


January 13, 1987, Argued  
April 7, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and of being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Vasington, J.; verdicts and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) which convicted defendant after a jury trial of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4), and of being a persistent dangerous felony offender in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the robbery of a convenience store. The clerk told police that a man with a stocking on his face had pointed a "bluish" revolver at him. Defendant was stopped three days later with a blue revolver on the floor of his car, and a witness had seen him earlier with a brown nylon stocking mask. The clerk later identified defendant from a photo array. The photos had arrest dates that indicated that only two of the individuals had been arrested within the time frame indicated by the officer, and only one of those two fit the description the clerk provided. After summations at trial, the trial judge denied a mistrial when a juror reported that she had seen a friend of hers in the courtroom and was "shocked" that the friend was a friend of defendant, but that she could decide the case fairly. On appeal, the court found no error. The court held that the photo array was impermissibly suggestive, but the identification was properly admitted as reliable under the totality of the circumstances. The court found that defendant failed to show bias sufficient to disqualify the juror or that he was deprived of his right to an impartial jury.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the superior court judgment.

Butzgy v. Glastonbury


No. 12821


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 109; 523 A.2d 1258; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 823


December 11, 1986, Argued  
April 7, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from extending a certain town road, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, M. Hennessey, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which held that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the property owners' complaint in nuisance against defendant town and which granted the town's motion to dismiss. The property owners' action sought injunctive relief against an extension of a road.


OVERVIEW: The property owners owned land on a road. The town's plan and zoning commission approved a corporation's application to subdivide land adjacent to the road. The approval was conditioned upon the construction of an extension to the road. Some of the property owners in the instant action filed an administrative appeal from the commission's decision that contested the extension. The administrative appeal was withdrawn. Some months after the withdrawal of the administrative appeal, the instant action was brought. The property owners' complaint alleged that the extension violated town ordinances; would have an adverse effect on traffic, noise, and the safety of the road; and created a dangerous nuisance. The trial court ruled that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The property owners appealed. The court held that the action was properly dismissed under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-28 because the claims should have been brought by way of an administrative appeal. The court held that the action was properly dismissed under Conn. Const. art. 1, § 10 where the property owners possessed a reasonable alternative to litigating their claims in an independent action in nuisance but chose not to.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

398 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Blue Sky Bar, Inc. v. Stratford


No. 12837


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 14; 523 A.2d 467; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 804


December 9, 1986, Argued  
March 31, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from enforcing a certain town ordinance prohibiting vending on public or town property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Jacobson, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to the Appellate Court, Borden, Spallone and Daly, Js., which affirmed the trial court's decision, and the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ice cream truck drivers appealed from the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which upheld the trial court's refusal to declare invalid and enjoin the enforcement of an ordinance enacted by defendant town purportedly under the authority of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148(c)(7)(H)(iv). The ordinance prohibited vending from any type of motor vehicle upon the streets or public property within town limits.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that § 7-148(c)(7)(H)(iv), which provided for municipal regulation of peddlers, gave the town the authority to enact the ordinance. The drivers contended that, construed with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21-37, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148(c)(7)(H)(iv) permitted municipalities only to regulate street vending, not to prohibit it altogether. However, the court held that the ordinance was regulatory in nature because it did not forbid the drivers from vending their products from non-motorized vehicles. The ordinance was a reasonable exercise of police power, because it was rationally related to the town's concern for public safety. The ordinance did not violate due process or equal protection because it bore a reasonable relationship to a proper legislative purpose in a manner that was neither arbitrary nor discriminatory. The ordinance did not require compelling governmental interest because the privilege of engaging in business was not a fundamental right. Finally, the ordinance did not interfere with interstate commerce because it treated out-of-state sellers on the same basis as local sellers and any minimal interference was outweighed by public interest in safety.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which upheld the ordinance at issue.

 

399 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Motor Vehicle Mfrs. Asso. v. O'Neill


No. 12985


Supreme Court of Connecticut


203 Conn. 63; 523 A.2d 486; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 808


February 10, 1987, Argued  
March 31, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the constitutional validity of a public act concerning, inter alia, dispute resolution procedures for defective new motor vehicles, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, M. Hennessey, J., granted the motion of John J. Woodcock III to intervene as a party defendant; thereafter, the court, Satter, J., pursuant to the stipulation of the parties, reserved nine questions of law for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After plaintiffs, a motor vehicle manufacturers association and others, filed suit against defendants, a governor, governmental officials, and a legislator, challenging the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 42-181 - 42-184, regarding dispute resolution for claims of defective new motor vehicles, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) reserved questions of law for the court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action against defendants for declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the constitutionality of a law concerning dispute resolution for defective new motor vehicles. The law in question was Lemon Law II, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 42-181 - 42-184. The trial court, pursuant to the stipulation of the parties, reserved nine questions of law for the court. Plaintiffs contended that the law deprived them of the right to a jury trial. The court held that: (1) review of such a serious challenge to the validity of Lemon Law II required an adequate factual record; (2) the court lacked a basis for determining the extent to which the proceedings authorized by Lemon Law II were essentially legal or equitable; and (3) because it would be improvident to resolve such a crucial issue on the current record and because disposition of the issue could obviate the need to address the other questions that had been reserved to the court, it was inappropriate for the court to respond to any part of the reservation.


OUTCOME: The court did not answer the reserved questions and remanded the case to the trial court.

 

400 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cates


No. 12879


Supreme Court of Connecticut


202 Conn. 615; 522 A.2d 788; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 796


November 4, 1986, Argued  
March 24, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of aiding and abetting a burglary in the third degree and of larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Jackaway, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aiding and abetting a burglary in the third degree and of larceny in the second degree in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, Geographical Area Number Six (Connecticut). He appealed and contended (1) that it was error to deny a motion to suppress evidence, (2) that the information lacked specificity and had not given him adequate notice of the charge, and (3) that the evidence was insufficient.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged the erroneous denial of his motion to suppress a mink cape obtained at his apartment, because the warrant allegedly lacked probable cause. However, when the court considered the case in light of all factors, it was evident that any minimal taint stemming from the allegedly illegal search was sufficiently purged. He also claimed that the count of the information charging him with larceny was constitutionally infirm because it failed to specify the date on which he supposedly committed the offense. The language "on or after" was a technical error, but it was never seriously challenged. Moreover, the language had not prejudiced defendant in the preparation of his defense, as he chose not to testify or to present any evidence. He was sufficiently informed of the nature of the crime with which he was charged. Defendant also contended that the evidence introduced at trial was insufficient to establish his guilt on both counts beyond a reasonable doubt. However, the court held that the evidence implicating defendant, while certainly not overwhelming, when considered in the light most favorable to the state was in fact sufficient to support the jury's verdict of guilty.


OUTCOME: There was no error.
